===== PAGE 50 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
50 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
3.10.1.1.2 Advantages 
• Versatility: The block system allows users to create almost any type of layout, from 
simple text documents to complex project management dashboards. 
• Relational Databases: It offers a powerful way to organize data with custom properties 
(tags, dates, formulas) and different views (Gallery, Kanban, List) that are very intuitive 
for non-technical users. 
• Seamless Collaboration: As a cloud-native tool, it excels at real-time multi-user editing, 
making it an ideal choice for teams that need to share information instantly. 
• Aesthetics and Ecosystem: It features a minimal visual design and a vast marketplace of 
templates that lower the barrier to entry for new users. 
3.10.1.1.3 Disadvantages 
• Performance and Latency: Because Notion relies on a constant connection to remote 
servers, users often experience significant delays (latency) when opening pages or 
searching for content. This "input lag" can be frustrating during deep-focus work. 
• Lack of Data Sovereignty: Since data is stored on proprietary servers, the user does not 
have true ownership of their information. If the service is down or the company changes 
its terms, the user's "Second Brain" could become inaccessible. 
• Limited Offline Mode: While it has a basic cache, Notion is fundamentally not designed 
to work offline. For a user who needs to work in isolated environments or values 
permanent access, this is a significant limitation. 
• Generalist Bloat: Notion tries to be everything for everyone. For a technical user, this 
results in a cluttered interface with many features (like team calendars or payroll 
templates) that are irrelevant for personal knowledge synthesis and documentation. 
• No Technical Specialization: It lacks native support for the "power-user" features found 
in Tessellum, such as advanced terminal -style code rendering or a high -performance 
local Knowledge Graph. 
 
3.10.1.2 Obsidian 
3.10.1.2.1 Description 
Manufacturer: Dynalist Inc. (Created by Erica Xu and Shida Li). 
Obsidian is a powerful, local -first knowledge base that operates on a folder of plain -text 
Markdown files. Unlike Notion, it does not rely on a proprietary database; instead, it acts as a 
"window" into the user's filesystem. It is designed around the concept of "networked thought," 
allowing users to create bi -directional links between notes to build a personal "Vault" of 
information. While the core application is free for personal use, it is a closed -source product 
with a vast open-source plugin ecosystem. 
===== PAGE 51 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 51 
 
3.10.1.2.2 Advantages 
• Data Sovereignty: Since all files are stored locally in Markdown format, the user has full 
ownership. There is no "vendor lock-in," as the notes can be opened by any text editor 
at any time. 
• Extensibility: It has one of the largest communities in the PKM space, offering over a 
thousand community -developed plugins that allow users to customize almost every 
aspect of the app. 
• Graph Visualization: It features a native "Graph View" that helps users visualize the 
relationships and clusters within their knowledge base. 
• Offline Performance: Being local-first, it does not suffer from the network latency issues 
typical of cloud-based tools like Notion. 
3.10.1.2.3 Disadvantages 
• "Plugin Bloat" and Fragmentation:  To achieve a "Technical User" workflow (such as 
slash commands, terminal callouts, or advanced code rendering), the user must find, 
install, and maintain multiple third-party plugins. This often leads to stability issues and 
a fragmented user experience where different parts of the UI don't feel cohesive. 
• Resource Consumption (Electron): Built on the Electron framework, Obsidian bundles a 
full Chromium browser. Even for simple text editing, it can be heavy on system memory 
(RAM), which contradicts the "lightweight" requirement of the Tessellum project. 
• Manual Setup Complexity: The "blank slate" philosophy means that a user must spend 
hours configuring the environment before it becomes productive. It lacks the 
specialized, "out-of-the-box" technical features that Tessellum provides by default. 
• Mobile-First Compromises:  Because Obsidian tries to maintain parity between its 
desktop and mobile versions, some of its desktop features feel constrained by mobile 
UI paradigms. 
 
3.10.1.3 Logseq 
3.10.1.3.1 Description 
Manufacturer: The Logseq Open Source Community (Led by Tiensen Qin). 
Logseq is an open-source, privacy-first knowledge management platform that focuses on a "non-
linear" outliner approach. Like Obsidian, it is local -first, storing data in plain-text Markdown or 
Org-mode files. However, its core philosophy is fundamentally d ifferent: it is built around a 
"Daily Journal" and an atomic data structure where every line is a "block." This allows for 
granular data manipulation and cross-referencing at the bullet-point level. 
===== PAGE 52 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
52 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
3.10.1.3.2 Advantages 
• Privacy and Transparency: Being fully open-source and local-only, it offers the highest 
level of transparency regarding data handling and security. 
• Structured Outlining: Its block-based architecture makes it exceptionally powerful for 
structured brainstorming and managing complex, nested hierarchies of information. 
• Built-in Academic Tools: It includes native support for PDF annotation and a Flashcard 
system (Spaced Repetition), making it popular in academic and research circles. 
• Granular Linking: Users can link to specific blocks (bullet points) rather than just whole 
pages, allowing for a very high level of precision in networked thought. 
3.10.1.3.3 Disadvantages 
• Significant Performance Bottlenecks:  Logseq is built using ClojureScript and runs 
primarily in a browser environment (even the desktop app is a wrapper). When a user's 
knowledge base grows beyond a few thousand blocks, the application often suffers from 
severe lag during indexing and graph rendering. 
• Outliner Rigidity: The "everything is a bullet point" format is polarizing. It is excellent 
for notes but becomes a hindrance for long -form technical writing, essays, or creating 
standard documentation—tasks that a document -based editor like Tessellum handles 
more naturally. 
• Steep Learning Curve:  The journal-based workflow and the logic of block -refs can be 
unintuitive for users accustomed to traditional file-and-folder systems. 
• Ecosystem Stability: Because it is community-driven and currently in "Beta," the API and 
core features undergo frequent changes, which can lead to broken workflows or data -
syncing glitches. 
 
3.10.1.4 VS Code 
3.10.1.4.1 Description 
Manufacturer: Microsoft Corporation. 
Visual Studio Code (VS Code) is a highly extensible source-code editor. While its primary purpose 
is software development, its robust extension marketplace allows it to be transformed into a 
Markdown-based note -taking environment through tools like "Markdo wn All in One," 
"Dendron," or "Foam." 
3.10.1.4.2 Advantages 
• Technical Power:  It offers advanced text -editing features available, including multi -
cursor editing, regex search, and deep Git integration. 
===== PAGE 53 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 53 
 
• Zero New Footprint: For developers, using VS Code for notes means one less application 
to keep open, saving system resources. 
• Total Customization:  Through its settings.json and thousands of extensions, the 
environment can be tailored to an extremely specific technical workflow. 
3.10.1.4.3 Disadvantages 
• Lack of Cohesion:  VS Code is an IDE, not a "Second Brain." Even with extensions, the 
experience of a Knowledge Graph or bi -directional linking feels like an "afterthought" 
rather than a core feature. 
• High Distraction Factor: The interface is cluttered with debugging tools, terminal panels, 
and coding extensions that can distract from the creative process of knowledge 
synthesis. 
• Fragile Workflow: A PKM setup in VS Code usually relies on 5 –10 different extensions 
from different authors. If one extension stops being updated, the entire "Second Brain" 
workflow can break. 
• No Specialized QoL: It lacks the unified, seamless integration of features like Tessellum's 
slash commands  and terminal callouts , requiring the user to manually configure 
complex snippets or keyboard shortcuts for every formatting task. 
 
3.10.2 Technical Shell 
The choice of a desktop shell dictates the application’s memory footprint, cross -platform 
stability, and access to system -level APIs. While modern web technologies offer rapid 
development cycles, they often come at the cost of high resource consumption. Th is analysis 
compares industry -standard frameworks to determine which environment provides a good 
balance between a rich, interactive UI and a "lightweight" system presence. 
3.10.2.1 Electron 
3.10.2.1.1 Description 
Electron is the most widely used framework for building cross -platform desktop applications 
using web technologies (HTML, CSS, and JavaScript). Developed and maintained by GitHub, it 
combines the Chromium rendering engine with the Node.js runtime. This all ows developers to 
build desktop apps that feel like websites but have access to the underlying operating system. 
It is the engine behind industry giants such as Visual Studio Code, Discord, and Obsidian. 
3.10.2.1.2 Advantages 
• Massive Ecosystem : It has the most extensive collection of libraries, tutorials, and 
community support in the desktop development world.

===== PAGE 54 =====

• Development Speed : Since it uses standard web technologies, web developers can 
transition to desktop development almost instantly. 
• Unified Environment: The developer uses the same language (JavaScript/TypeScript) for 
both the user interface and the backend logic. 
  
3.10.2.1.3 Disadvantages 
• High Resource Consumption : Electron is known for its high RAM usage. Because it 
bundles a full Chromium browser for every application instance, even a simple text 
editor can consume high amounts of memory. 
• Large Binary Sizes: The minimum size for an empty Electron app is typically over 100MB, 
which contradicts the "lightweight" philosophy of a tool meant to be kept open all day. 
• Security Surface: Including a full Node.js runtime alongside a web browser provides a 
large attack surface if not configured with extreme care. 
 
3.10.2.2 Flutter 
3.10.2.2.1 Description 
Flutter is an open -source UI software development kit created by Google. While originally 
designed for mobile, it has expanded to support desktop environments. Unlike Electron, Flutter 
does not use a web browser to render the UI; instead, it uses its own r endering engine (Skia or 
Impeller) and compiles the application code (written in the Dart language) into native machine 
code. 
3.10.2.2.2 Advantages 
• High Performance: Because it compiles to native code and avoids the overhead of a web 
browser, it offers smoother animations and more consistent frame rates than browser-
based alternatives. 
• Consistent U I: Flutter draws every pixel on the screen itself, ensuring that the 
application looks exactly the same on Windows, macOS, and Linux. 
• Strong Developer Tooling : It includes features like "Hot Reload," which significantly 
speeds up the design and layout process. 
3.10.2.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Ecosystem Limitations: While growing, the Dart ecosystem is significantly smaller than 
the JavaScript or Rust ecosystems, especially for specialized libraries like graph 
visualization or Markdown parsing. 
• Integration Challenges : Integrating complex web -based components —such as the 
CodeMirror 6 editor engine required for Tessellum —into Flutter is difficult and often 
results in performance degradation. 
===== PAGE 55 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 55 
 
• Non-Native Feel: Because Flutter renders its own components rather than using the 
operating system's native ones, the UI can sometimes feel slightly "off" or inconsistent 
with the host OS's design language. 
 
3.10.2.3 Qt 
3.10.2.3.1 Description 
Qt is a long -standing, industrial -grade framework for developing cross -platform applications 
using C++. It is the traditional choice for high -performance software, used by applications like 
Adobe Photoshop, VLC Media Player, and Maya . It provides a comprehensive set of libraries 
for everything from UI design to networking and database management. 
3.10.2.3.2 Advantages 
• Peak Performance: As a C++ framework, it offers the highest possible performance and 
the most efficient use of system resources (CPU and RAM). 
• True Native Capabilities : It allows for deep integration with the operating system, 
providing a user experience that is indistinguishable from a native application. 
• Maturity: It is a battle -tested framework with decades of history in critical and high -
performance environments. 
3.10.2.3.3 Disadvantages 
• Complexity and Safety: Developing in C++ is significantly slower and more error -prone 
than using modern languages like Rust or TypeScript. It lacks the built-in memory safety 
guarantees that protect against common bugs and security vulnerabilities. 
• Licensing Costs: While there is an open-source version, many of its professional features 
require expensive commercial licenses, which can be a barrier for independent or 
academic projects. 
• Modern Web Integration : Modern technical users expect highly interactive, web -like 
interfaces. Building these in Qt’s UI systems (Widgets or QML) is often more 
cumbersome than using modern web frameworks like React. 
 
3.10.2.4 NW.js 
3.10.2.4.1 Description 
NW.js (formerly Node-webkit) is an older contemporary of Electron. It also allows developers to 
build desktop apps with HTML and CSS and enables calling Node.js modules directly from the 
DOM. It was one of the first frameworks to successfully bridge the ga p between the web and 
the desktop. 
===== PAGE 56 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
56 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
3.10.2.4.2 Advantages 
• Direct DOM Access : Unlike Electron, which separates the rendering process from the 
main process, NW.js allows Node.js and the browser context to share the same script 
environment. 
• Legacy Support: It often supports older versions of operating systems better than more 
modern frameworks. 
3.10.2.4.3 Disadvantages 
• Resource Overhead : Similar to Electron, it suffers from significant memory and disk 
space overhead due to the bundled Chromium instance. 
• Declining Popularity: The community and development momentum have largely shifted 
toward Electron and more modern alternatives, making it harder to find updated plugins 
and security patches. 
 
3.10.3 Backend Logic 
The backend serves as the orchestration layer for file indexing, graph calculations, and system 
communication. For a tool intended to handle thousands of technical notes without stuttering, 
the choice of language is critical. We evaluate candidates based on three non-negotiable criteria: 
memory safety, concurrency handling, and compilation speed. 
3.10.3.1 Go (Golang) 
3.10.3.1.1 Description 
Go is an open -source, compiled, and statically typed programming language developed by 
Google. It was designed to bridge the gap between high -level ease of use and low -level 
performance. Go is particularly well-known for its "Goroutines," which provide a highly efficient 
way to handle thousands of concurrent tasks with minimal overhead. It is widely used for 
building cloud infrastructure, CLI tools, and microservices. 
3.10.3.1.2 Advantages 
• Concurrency by Default: Its native support for concurrency makes it an excellent choice 
for tasks like watching thousands of files for changes. 
• Development Speed: Go has a very simple syntax with few keywords, making it much 
faster to write and maintain than more complex languages. 
• Fast Compilation: It offers extremely fast build times, which significantly speeds up the 
development and testing cycle. 
===== PAGE 57 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 57 
 
3.10.3.1.3 Disadvantages 
• Garbage Collection (GC) : Go uses a garbage collector to manage memory. While 
efficient, the GC can introduce small "stop-the-world" pauses that may impact the low-
latency performance. 
• Safety vs. Control : While it is safer than C++, it does not provide the same level of 
"compile-time" memory safety guarantees that prevent data races as rigorously as other 
modern systems languages. 
• Binary Size: Go binaries are statically linked and include the runtime, which results in 
larger file sizes compared to languages that don't require a runtime. 
 
3.10.3.2 C++ 
3.10.3.2.1 Description 
C++ is a general-purpose programming language that has been the industry standard for systems 
programming and high -performance applications for decades. It provides low -level memory 
manipulation and high -level abstractions. It is the language of choice for  performance-critical 
software such as game engines, operating systems, and heavy -duty database management 
systems. 
3.10.3.2.2 Advantages 
• Unmatched Performance : It offers high execution speed and  granular control over 
hardware resources and memory allocation. 
• Immense Library Support: Having been around for decades, C++ has a library for almost 
every conceivable technical requirement, including highly optimized graph and search 
algorithms. 
• Zero-Cost Abstractions: Developers can use high-level features without a performance 
penalty, which is ideal for complex logic like the Grafeo engine. 
3.10.3.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Memory Safety Risks : C++ requires manual memory management. This makes the 
application highly susceptible to memory leaks, buffer overflows, and segmentation 
faults, which can lead to crashes and security vulnerabilities. 
• Technical Debt and Complexity: The language is notoriously difficult to master. Writing 
safe, modern C++ requires a high level of expertise and significantly more development 
time. 
• Slower Build Times : Compiling large C++ projects can be extremely time -consuming, 
slowing down the iteration process during the development of user stories. 
 
===== PAGE 58 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
58 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
3.10.3.3 Node.js 
3.10.3.3.1 Description 
Node.js is an open -source, cross -platform JavaScript runtime environment that executes 
JavaScript code outside a web browser. In the context of a desktop application, using Node.js 
for the backend allows the developer to use a single language (TypeScript) for the entire stack. 
It is built on the Chrome V8 engine and uses an event-driven, non-blocking I/O model. 
3.10.3.3.2 Advantages 
• Unified Stack : Using TypeScript for both the frontend and backend simplifies data 
sharing and reduces the "context switching" required by the developer. 
• NPM Ecosystem: It provides access to one of the largest ecosystems of open-source 
libraries, making it easy to integrate Markdown parsers and search utilities. 
• Fast Prototyping: It is exceptionally fast to get a working backend prototype up and 
running due to the flexibility of the language. 
3.10.3.3.3 Disadvantages 
• Single-Threaded Nature: Node.js runs on a single-threaded event loop. While great for 
I/O, it struggles with CPU-bound tasks like heavy file-content indexing or complex graph 
calculations, which can block the entire backend. 
• Resource Overhead: Running the V8 engine on the backend adds significant memory 
overhead, which conflicts with the project's goal of being a lightweight tool. 
• Runtime Safety: Unlike compiled systems languages, many errors in JavaScript/Node.js 
are only caught at runtime, which can lead to a less stable experience for the end user. 
 
3.10.3.4 Java 
3.10.3.4.1 Description 
Java is a high-level, class-based, object-oriented programming language designed to have as few 
implementation dependencies as possible. Developed by Sun Microsystems (now Oracle), its 
core philosophy is "Write Once, Run Anywhere" (WORA), achieved by execu ting code on the 
Java Virtual Machine (JVM) . It has been a cornerstone of enterprise software, Android 
development, and large-scale data processing for decades. 
3.10.3.4.2 Advantages 
• Industrial Maturity: Java offers one of the most stable and battle-tested environments 
in software engineering, with exhaustive documentation and community support. 
• Standardized Library Support: It possesses world-class libraries for search and indexing, 
most notably Apache Lucene (the industry -standard library that inspired the Tantivy 
engine used in this project). 
===== PAGE 59 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 59 
 
• Robust Multithreading: Java’s concurrency models are highly sophisticated, allowing it 
to manage complex background tasks —such as file indexing and graph calculations —
efficiently across multiple CPU cores. 
3.10.3.4.3 Disadvantages 
• High Memory Overhead : The JVM requires a significant amount of system memory 
(RAM) just to initialize. For a "lightweight" tool like Tessellum, which is intended to run 
in the background without affecting system performance, this overhead is a major 
disadvantage. 
• Startup Latency : Java applications often suffer from "cold starts," where the initial 
launch is noticeably slower than natively compiled languages like C++ or Rust. 
• Distribution Complexity: Packaging a Java backend within a desktop shell (like Tauri) 
requires bundling a Java Runtime Environment (JRE). This would drastically increase the 
installation size and complicate the deployment process compared to a single -binary 
approach. 
 
3.10.4 Graph Engine 
The core value of a "Second Brain" lies in its ability to map relationships between disparate ideas. 
The graph engine must handle complex relational queries with sub -millisecond latency. This 
section explores different paradigms for managing these connecti ons, from pure in -memory 
data structures to embedded graph databases that support standardized query languages. 
3.10.4.1 Petgraph 
3.10.4.1.1 Description 
Petgraph is the most popular and mature general-purpose graph library in the Rust ecosystem. 
It provides a wide array of graph data structures (such as Graph, StableGraph, and GraphMap) 
and implements standard graph algorithms like Breadth -First Search (BF S), Dijkstra’s shortest 
path, and cycle detection. It is designed to be highly flexible and performant for in -memory 
graph manipulation. 
3.10.4.1.2 Advantages 
• Feature Richness: It includes out -of-the-box support for almost every standard graph 
algorithm required for network analysis. 
• Performance: Being a native Rust library, it offers excellent execution speed and type 
safety, preventing common memory errors. 
• Maturity: It is battle-tested and widely used across the Rust community, ensuring high 
reliability and extensive documentation.  
===== PAGE 60 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
60 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
3.10.4.1.3 Disadvantages 
• Persistence Challenges : Petgraph is primarily an in -memory structure. It does not 
natively handle synchronization with a database (like SQLite), requiring significant 
custom code to map graph changes to disk. 
• Complexity: Its API is highly generic and can be overwhelming for projects that only 
need a subset of graph functionalities, leading to more "boilerplate" code. 
 
3.10.4.2 Neo4j 
3.10.4.2.1 Description 
Neo4j is the industry -standard graph database management system. It uses the Cypher query 
language, which is specifically designed for traversing complex relationships. While it is usually 
used as a standalone server, it can be interfaced via drivers or us ed in embedded modes in 
certain environments. 
3.10.4.2.2 Advantages 
• Advanced Querying : Cypher makes it incredibly easy to perform complex pattern 
matching and relationship analysis that would be difficult in SQL or standard libraries. 
• Visual Tooling: It comes with powerful administrative tools for visualizing and managing 
data during development. 
• Industrial Power : It can handle millions of nodes and edges with ease, providing 
features like ACID transactions and high availability. 
3.10.4.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Extreme Overkill: For a local -first desktop app, Neo4j is excessively heavy. It typically 
requires a Java environment or an external server, which violates the "lightweight" and 
"zero-configuration" requirements of Tessellum. 
• Resource Heavy : The memory and CPU overhead of running a full graph database 
engine would significantly slow down the user's machine. 
 
3.10.4.3 Kuzu 
3.10.4.3.1 Description 
Kuzu is an open -source, in-process graph database management system  (GDBMS) built for 
query speed and scalability. It is often described as the "DuckDB of graphs" because it is designed 
to be embedded directly into the application rather than running as a separate server. It utilizes 
the Cypher query language—the industry standard for graphs —and is optimized for modern 
hardware, employing columnar storage and vectorized execution to handle complex analytical 
queries. 
===== PAGE 61 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 61 
 
3.10.4.3.2 Advantages 
• Embedded Architecture: Since it is an in -process database, it requires zero setup or 
external maintenance. This aligns perfectly with the "local -first" and "zero -
configuration" goals of Tessellum. 
• High Performance : It is specifically engineered for analytical workloads, making it 
capable of handling large-scale knowledge bases with millions of links without sacrificing 
speed. 
• Structured Querying: The support for the Cypher language allows for the execution of 
sophisticated relationship queries (like "find all notes linked by my most -used tags") in 
a very readable and standardized way. 
3.10.4.3.3 Disadvantages 
• External Dependency Complexity: Although it has a Rust API, the core engine is written 
in C++. Integrating it requires a C++ compiler toolchain, which increases the complexity 
of the build process and the final binary size compared to a pure Rust crate like Grafeo. 
• Overhead for Smaller Vaults: For a personal knowledge management tool where users 
might only have a few hundred or thousand notes, the power of a full GDBMS like Kuzu 
might be excessive compared to the lightweight footprint of simpler graph libraries. 
• Project Maturity : While extremely promising, Kuzu is a newer project compared to 
established alternatives like Petgraph, meaning it has a smaller ecosystem of auxiliary 
tools and community-vetted patterns. 
 
3.10.5 Visualization 
For a knowledge graph to be actionable, the visualization layer must handle hundreds of 
interactive nodes without taxing the CPU. Here, we weigh the benefits of low -level, GPU -
accelerated rendering against higher-level, DOM-based libraries that offer easier customization 
but potential performance bottlenecks. 
3.10.5.1 D3.js 
3.10.5.1.1 Description 
D3.js is a low -level JavaScript library for producing dynamic, interactive data visualizations in 
web browsers. It utilizes SVG, HTML5, and CSS standards. Unlike specialized graph libraries, D3 
is a general-purpose tool that gives the developer total control over the visual representation of 
data through a powerful functional programming interface. 
3.10.5.1.2 Advantages 
• Total Flexibility: It allows for the creation of a wide range of visualization types , from 
simple bar charts to complex, physics-based custom network layouts. 
• Vast Community : As the industry standard for web visualization, it has a massive 
community and thousands of open-source examples to learn from. 
===== PAGE 62 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
62 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Standard-Based: It works directly with the DOM and web standards, ensuring long-term 
compatibility without relying on a proprietary rendering engine. 
3.10.5.1.3 Disadvantages 
• Steep Learning Curve : Being a low -level library, the developer must manually handle 
everything from the math of the layout to the event listeners for zooming and dragging. 
• Performance with Large Graphs: Since it primarily uses SVG (Scalable Vector Graphics), 
rendering thousands of nodes can become slow, as every node is an individual element 
in the browser's DOM. 
• Development Time: Building a fully functional "Knowledge Graph" with node dragging 
and automatic layouts requires significantly more development time than using a 
specialized library. 
 
3.10.5.2 Sigma.js 
3.10.5.2.1 Description 
Sigma.js is a JavaScript library dedicated specifically to graph drawing. It is designed to handle 
large-scale networks by utilizing WebGL for rendering. This offloads the graphical processing to 
the GPU, making it capable of displaying and animating tens of thousands of nodes and edges 
with high frame rates. 
3.10.5.2.2 Advantages 
• High Performance: It is well suited for graphs with tens of thousands of nodes, where 
SVG-based rendering becomes a bottleneck. 
• Specialized API : Its functions are tailored specifically for graph structures, making it 
easier to load and manipulate network data than general-purpose tools. 
• Customizability: It allows for deep customization of how nodes and edges are rendered 
through specialized WebGL shaders. 
3.10.5.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Styling Constraints: Because it renders to a Canvas/WebGL context, it is much harder to 
use standard CSS for styling individual nodes compared to SVG-based alternatives. 
• Interaction Complexity : Handling fine -grained interactions, such as specific text 
selection or complex hover effects, is more difficult in a WebGL environment than in a 
DOM-based one. 
• Smaller Ecosystem : It has fewer third -party layout algorithms and plugins available 
compared to D3 or Cytoscape. 
 
===== PAGE 63 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 63 
 
3.10.5.3 G6 
3.10.5.3.1 Description 
G6 is an open-source graph visualization engine from the AntV ecosystem. It provides a robust 
set of basic mechanisms for graph visualization and analysis. It focuses on high performance and 
ease of use, sitting between low-level libraries like D3 and high-level specialized tools. 
3.10.5.3.2 Advantages 
• Industrial Strength : It includes a wide variety of professional -grade layouts (Dagre, 
Radial, Circular) and advanced analysis algorithms out of the box. 
• Rich Interaction: It features built-in support for complex user behaviors, such as multi -
selection, node collapsing, and custom tooltips. 
• Dual Engine : It supports both Canvas and SVG rendering, allowing the developer to 
choose the best engine for their specific performance needs. 
3.10.5.3.3 Disadvantages 
• Documentation Hurdles : A significant portion of its deeper documentation and 
community discussions are primarily in Chinese, which can be a barrier to solving niche 
technical issues. 
• Library Weight: It is a relatively large library, which might impact the initial load time of 
the application's frontend. 
 
3.10.6 State Management 
As the complexity of the user interface grows—simultaneously managing an editor, a graph, and 
search results —predictable data flow becomes vital. This subsection assesses various state 
management patterns to ensure that the application remains "reactive" w ithout the overhead 
of unnecessary re-renders or excessive boilerplate code. 
3.10.6.1 Redux 
3.10.6.1.1 Description 
Redux is the most established state management library in the React ecosystem. It follows a 
centralized pattern based on a single "Source of Truth." State changes are handled through a 
strict flow of Actions (describing what happened) and Reducers (pure functions that calculate 
the new state). The Redux Toolkit (RTK) is the modern standard that simplifies this process by 
providing pre-configured tools for common tasks. 
3.10.6.1.2 Advantages 
• Predictability: The strict architecture makes it very easy to track how and when the state 
changes. 
===== PAGE 64 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
64 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Industrial Debugging : It features "Redux DevTools," which allows for "Time Travel 
Debugging," enabling the developer to move back and forth through state changes to 
find bugs. 
• Vast Middleware : It has a rich ecosystem for handling side effects, such as logging, 
persistence, or complex asynchronous flows. 
3.10.6.1.3 Disadvantages 
• High Boilerplate: Even with the Redux Toolkit, it requires significantly more code (slices, 
actions, store configuration) than other alternatives to perform simple tasks. 
• Learning Curve: Its conceptual overhead is steep, requiring developers to understand 
functional programming principles and strict immutability. 
• Bundle Size: It is a relatively "heavy" library, which can impact the initial load time and 
memory usage of a lightweight application. 
 
3.10.6.2 React Context API 
3.10.6.2.1 Description 
The Context API is a native feature of React designed to share data that can be considered 
"global" for a tree of components (such as a user profile or a preferred language). It avoids "prop 
drilling" (passing data through multiple levels of components) wi thout requiring an external 
library. 
3.10.6.2.2 Advantages 
• Zero External Dependencies: Since it is built into React, it adds no overhead to the final 
bundle size and requires no third-party maintenance. 
• Native Integration: It uses standard React hooks (useContext), making it very intuitive 
for developers familiar with the library. 
• Perfect for Static Data: It is highly efficient for data that changes infrequently, such as 
UI themes or localization settings. 
3.10.6.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Performance Issues: It is not optimized for high -frequency updates. If a value in the 
Context provider changes, all components consuming that context re-render, which can 
lead to UI "stuttering" in a complex app like a Knowledge Graph. 
• Lack of Tooling : It lacks the advanced debugging and state -tracing tools found in 
dedicated libraries like Redux. 
• Complexity with Logic: It does not provide a built-in way to handle complex state logic 
or asynchronous actions, often requiring the developer to build custom solutions. 
 
===== PAGE 65 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 65 
 
3.10.6.3 MobX 
3.10.6.3.1 Description 
MobX is a library based on "Transparent Functional Reactive Programming" (TFRP). It treats the 
state as a set of observables. When a piece of state changes, MobX automatically detects which 
components are using that specific value and updates only those. I t feels similar to object -
oriented programming, where you modify properties directly. 
3.10.6.3.2 Advantages 
• Minimal Boilerplate: It requires very little code to set up. You simply define your state 
as "observable" and modify it like a regular JavaScript object. 
• High Performance: Its fine-grained reactivity ensures that only the absolute minimum 
number of components are re -rendered, which is excellent for complex, data -heavy 
interfaces. 
• Less Rigid: It does not enforce a strict "action-reducer" flow, giving the developer more 
freedom in how they structure the application logic. 
3.10.6.3.3 Disadvantages 
• Non-Transparent Behavior: Because it uses Proxies and automatic tracking, it can 
sometimes feel like "magic," making it harder to debug when the state doesn't update 
as expected. 
• Non-idiomatic React: React is built around immutability, while MobX is built around 
mutability. This can lead to conflicts with modern React features like Concurrent Mode 
or certain testing patterns. 
 
3.10.7 Text Editor 
The text editor is the primary interface through which the user interacts with their knowledge 
base. A technical user requires a specific balance: the power of an IDE combined with the speed 
of a Markdown editor. We compare "heavy -duty" editor cores agains t "headless" frameworks 
to find the most extensible and performant writing environment. 
3.10.7.1 Monaco 
3.10.7.1.1 Description 
Monaco is the code editor that powers Visual Studio Code. It is a heavy-duty, feature-rich library 
developed by Microsoft that provides out -of-the-box support for thousands of programming 
languages, advanced IntelliSense, and deep integration with the Language Server Protocol (LSP). 
It is designed to bring the full power of a professional IDE to the web browser. 
===== PAGE 66 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
66 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
3.10.7.1.2 Advantages 
• Industry Standard: It offers a familiar experience for technical users, as it is identical to 
the interface of VS Code. 
• Advanced Features: It includes complex features like a minimap, multiple cursors, and 
sophisticated diff-viewing natively. 
• Performance with Large Files : It is highly optimized for performance and can handle 
massive text files with tens of thousands of lines without significant lag. 
3.10.7.1.3 Disadvantages 
• Library Weight: It is an exceptionally large library. Including it in a desktop application 
significantly increases the bundle size and memory footprint, which contradicts the 
"lightweight" goal of this project. 
• Mobile Limitations: Monaco was never designed with mobile or touch devices in mind, 
making it very difficult to optimize for tablets or smartphones. 
• Rigid Architecture : While powerful, it is less "modular" than other alternatives; you 
often have to take the entire package even if you only need a fraction of its features. 
 
3.10.7.2 TipTap 
3.10.7.2.1 Description 
TipTap is a headless rich -text editor framework built on top of ProseMirror. Unlike traditional 
editors that provide a pre -designed UI, TipTap provides the logic and the state management, 
leaving the visual representation entirely to the developer. It uses  a "schema-based" approach 
where every element (bold text, links, code blocks) is a node in a structured document tree. 
3.10.7.2.2 Advantages 
• Headless Flexibility: Since it doesn't enforce a UI, it allows for total design freedom, 
which is perfect for creating a custom, "distraction-free" aesthetic using Tailwind CSS. 
• Collaborative Ready: It is built from the ground up to support real -time collaboration 
via Yjs, which is a major advantage if the project were to expand into multi-user sync. 
• Modern API: It offers a very intuitive, "chained" API that makes it easy to add extensions 
or custom commands, such as slash menus. 
3.10.7.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Abstraction Layer: Being a wrapper around ProseMirror, troubleshooting deep issues 
sometimes requires understanding the underlying ProseMirror library, which has a very 
steep learning curve. 
• Markdown Compatibility Limitations : While it can handle Markdown, it is 
fundamentally a rich -text editor that converts content into a JSON structure. For a 
project where Markdown files are the "source of truth," this conversion layer can 
introduce complexity. 
===== PAGE 67 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 67 
 
• Overhead: For a pure "text -to-text" workflow, the overhead of managing a complex 
document tree can be less efficient than a stream-based editor. 
 
3.10.7.3 Slate.js 
3.10.7.3.1 Description 
Slate.js is a highly customizable framework for building rich -text editors in React. It treats the 
document as a nested JSON tree, similar to the DOM itself. Its primary focus is on being 
"completely customizable," meaning it doesn't provide a "standard" e ditor but rather the 
building blocks to create one. 
3.10.7.3.2 Advantages 
• React-Centric: It is designed specifically for React, using a data model that feels very 
natural to developers familiar with React's state management and component lifecycle. 
• Total Plugin Architecture: Every feature in Slate is a plugin. This means the developer 
has full control over how the editor handles specific inputs or rendering behaviors. 
• Predictable State: Because it uses a JSON -based model, it is very easy to implement 
"Undo/Redo" functionality and complex state transformations. 
3.10.7.3.3 Disadvantages 
• Development Effort : Because it provides so few "default" behaviors, it requires a 
significant amount of development time to build even a basic Markdown editor. 
• Breaking Changes: The library has historically undergone frequent API changes, which 
can lead to maintenance challenges in long-term projects. 
• Performance overhead : For extremely large documents, the JSON -to-DOM 
reconciliation process in React can become a bottleneck compared to more traditional 
text buffers. 
 
3.10.8 Frontend Build Tool 
Development velocity and final bundle size are heavily influenced by the frontend tooling. In a 
project prioritizing a "lightweight" philosophy, every kilobyte matters. This section compares 
modern bundlers and compilers, focusing on their ability to provi de near-instant hot-module 
replacement and optimized tree-shaking for the final production binary. 
3.10.8.1 Webpack 
3.10.8.1.1 Description 
Webpack has been the industry standard for frontend bundling for over a decade. It is a highly 
powerful and flexible tool that treats every asset in your project (JavaScript, CSS, images) as a 
===== PAGE 68 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
68 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
module. It uses a "bundling" approach: during development, it crawls through your entire 
dependency graph and creates a single massive file (or several chunks) to serve to the browser. 
3.10.8.1.2 Advantages 
• Ultimate Flexibility : Through its complex configuration system of "loaders" and 
"plugins," it can handle almost any specialized technical requirement imaginable. 
• Maturity: It has the largest ecosystem of any build tool, with a solution available for 
every possible edge case on platforms like StackOverflow. 
• Code Splitting: It pioneered advanced techniques for breaking down large applications 
into smaller parts, loading them only when needed. 
3.10.8.1.3 Disadvantages 
• Complex Configuration: Setting up Webpack for a modern project is notoriously difficult 
and time-consuming, often requiring hundreds of lines of complex code. 
• Slow Development Starts : Because it bundles the entire project before starting the 
development server, large projects can take several minutes to "boot up." 
• Heavyweight: It is built on Node.js and can be quite resource-intensive during the build 
process, which contrasts with the "lightweight" philosophy of this project. 
 
3.10.8.2 Parcel 
3.10.8.2.1 Description 
Parcel is known as the "zero -configuration" bundler. Its core philosophy is that the tool should 
just work out of the box. You simply point it at your index.html file, and it automatically detects 
all your dependencies, transpiles your code, and manages your assets without needing a single 
configuration file. 
3.10.8.2.2 Advantages 
• Ease of Use: It is the fastest tool to get a project up and running. There are no complex 
configuration files to maintain or update. 
• Performance: It utilizes multi -core processing and a sophisticated caching system to 
make rebuilds extremely fast. 
• Automatic Transformations : It handles things like TypeScript, Sass, and Image 
optimization automatically without requiring manual plugin installation. 
3.10.8.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Limited Transparency: Because it does so much automatically, it can be extremely 
difficult to debug or customize when a project has highly specific needs that fall outside 
of Parcel's "default" way of doing things. 
• Customization Limits: While it has a plugin system, it is much less flexible than Webpack 
for advanced architectural requirements. 
===== PAGE 69 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 69 
 
• Community Size: While popular, its ecosystem of specialized plugins is smaller than that 
of Webpack or the more modern Vite-compatible community. 
 
3.10.8.3 Turbopack 
3.10.8.3.1 Description 
Turbopack is a relatively new build tool developed by Vercel (the creators of Next.js). It is written 
in Rust and is designed to be the successor to Webpack. It focuses on extreme speed by utilizing 
an incremental computation engine, which means it never does the same work twice. 
3.10.8.3.2 Advantages 
• High Build Speed: Being written in Rust, it is significantly faster than Node -based tools 
like Webpack. It is specifically optimized for massive projects with thousands of 
modules. 
• Efficient Caching: Its "turbo" engine ensures that it only re-computes the exact parts of 
the code that have changed, making reloads nearly instantaneous. 
• Modern Focus: It is built specifically for modern frameworks and the latest versions of 
the JavaScript ecosystem. 
3.10.8.3.3 Disadvantages 
• Relative Newness: At the time of this project's development, Turbopack is still in an 
early stage for general use outside of the Next.js ecosystem. It lacks the broad stability 
of older tools. 
• Limited Plugin Support: It does not yet support the vast array of plugins that developers 
have come to rely on in the Webpack or Rollup/Vite ecosystems. 
• Specific Workflow : It is heavily integrated with Vercel’s vision of web development, 
which might not always align with the requirements of a standalone Tauri desktop 
application. 
 
3.10.9 Testing Framework 
To ensure stability across the UI and the Rust-bridge logic, a robust testing suite is required. We 
evaluate frameworks based on their support for modern ES Modules, their execution speed, and 
their ability to handle end-to-end (E2E) desktop automation. 
3.10.9.1 Jest 
3.10.9.1.1 Description 
Jest is the most popular testing framework in the JavaScript ecosystem, developed and 
maintained by Meta (Facebook). It was designed with a "zero -configuration" philosophy for 
===== PAGE 70 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
70 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
React applications. It is an all -in-one solution that includes a test runner, an assertion library, 
and built-in mocking capabilities. It has been the industry standard for years, powering projects 
of all scales. 
3.10.9.1.2 Advantages 
• Feature Completeness: It includes everything needed for testing (mocking, snapshots, 
coverage) without requiring extra libraries. 
• Snapshot Testing: A powerful feature for React components that allows developers to 
detect unexpected UI changes by comparing the rendered output against a stored 
"baseline." 
• Parallelization: It runs tests in parallel using worker processes, which optimizes 
execution time for large suites on multi-core machines. 
3.10.9.1.3 Disadvantages 
• Performance in Vite Projects : Jest was built before the era of native ES Modules. In a 
project like Tessellum that uses Vite, Jest requires a complex transformation layer (like 
ts-jest or babel-jest), which is significantly slower and harder to configure than modern 
alternatives. 
• Heavy Footprint: It is a large package with many dependencies, which can lead to longer 
installation times and a "heavier" development environment. 
• JSDOM Overhead: While it provides a virtual browser environment (JSDOM), it can be 
slower than more modern, optimized runners. 
 
3.10.9.2 Playwright 
3.10.9.2.1 Description 
Playwright is a modern framework for Web -platform testing and automation, created by 
Microsoft. It is often seen as the primary successor to Puppeteer. It is designed to enable cross-
browser web automation that is fast, reliable, and capable of handling co mplex modern web 
features. It supports Chromium, Firefox, and WebKit (Safari) using a single API. 
3.10.9.2.2 Advantages 
• Extreme Speed : It utilizes a browser -context architecture that allows it to launch 
"incognito-like" sessions in milliseconds, making it one of the fastest E2E tools available. 
• Native OS Integration : Unlike Cypress, it has better support for multiple windows, 
frames, and even certain native system events, which is relevant for desktop -focused 
projects. 
• Strong TypeScript Support : It was built with TypeScript in mind, providing excellent 
auto-completion and type safety out of the box. 
===== PAGE 71 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 71 
 
3.10.9.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Complexity: Its API is more powerful but also more complex than that of Jest or Vitest, 
requiring a steeper learning curve for a solo developer. 
• Tauri Integration Hurdles : While powerful, the bridge between Playwright and the 
native Tauri binary is less mature than specialized WebDriver -based solutions, often 
requiring manual configuration of the tauri-driver. 
• Focus: It is primarily an E2E tool; using it for small unit tests of Rust -bridge logic would 
be over-engineered. 
 
3.10.9.3 Mocha & Chai 
3.10.9.3.1 Description 
Mocha is a feature-rich JavaScript test framework running on Node.js, often paired with Chai (an 
assertion library). It is one of the "classic" choices in the ecosystem, known for its flexibility and 
"modular" approach. Unlike Jest, Mocha does not include its own mocking or assertion tools; 
developers must choose and plug in their preferred libraries. 
3.10.9.3.2 Advantages 
• Flexibility: Because it is unopinionated, developers can build a custom testing stack that 
fits their exact needs. 
• Proven Stability: It has been around for over a decade and is extremely stable, with very 
few breaking changes over the years. 
• Asynchronous Support : It was one of the first frameworks to handle asynchronous 
testing elegantly, which is vital for testing the communication between the UI and the 
Rust backend. 
3.10.9.3.3 Disadvantages 
• Fragmented Configuration : Setting up a full suite requires installing and configuring 
multiple packages (Mocha, Chai, Sinon for mocking, nyc for coverage), which is more 
tedious than using a unified modern runner. 
• Slower Evolution: It lacks many of the modern developer-experience features found in 
newer tools, such as built -in UI dashboards or optimized "watch modes" that only run 
relevant tests. 
• Lack of Native ESM Support: Like Jest, it requires additional tooling to work seamlessly 
with the modern Vite/ESM pipeline used in Tessellum. 
 
===== PAGE 72 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
72 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
3.10.10 Search Engine 
The search engine must provide "search-as-you-type" speed while remaining entirely local. This 
analysis contrasts heavyweight industry standards against lightweight, embedded libraries to 
find a solution that offers high relevancy without requiring a background server. 
3.10.10.1 Meilisearch 
3.10.10.1.1 Description 
Meilisearch is a powerful, open-source, and fast search engine designed for developers to build 
a "search-as-you-type" experience. It is often compared to proprietary services like Algolia but 
is self-hostable. It focuses on relevancy, typo tolerance, and ease of use, providing a RESTful API 
to interact with the indexed data. 
3.10.10.1.2 Advantages 
• Superior Relevance: It offers excellent out -of-the-box relevancy and "typo tolerance," 
which makes the search feel very smart and forgiving for the end-user. 
• Developer Experience: The API is highly intuitive and easy to integrate, with specialized 
SDKs for almost every modern programming language. 
• Rich Features: Includes advanced features like synonym support, filtering, and facets 
natively. 
3.10.10.1.3 Disadvantages 
• Architecture Overhead: Meilisearch is primarily designed to run as a separate "sidecar" 
server process. For a lightweight desktop application, running an additional background 
server increases memory consumption and complicates the installation process. 
• Resource Intensity: It can be quite demanding on RAM, especially when indexing large 
amounts of text, which conflicts with the project's goal of being a "lightweight" tool. 
• Rust Integration: While written in Rust, it is intended to be used as a standalone service 
rather than a library (crate) integrated directly into the binary, adding unnecessary IPC 
(Inter-Process Communication) overhead. 
 
3.10.10.2 Lunr.js 
3.10.10.2.1 Description 
Lunr.js is a small, full -text search library for use in the browser and in Node.js. It is inspired by 
Solr and is intended to provide a "search experience" for static sites or small web applications 
where a full-scale server-side search engine would be overkill. It operates entirely in memory or 
can be serialized to a JSON file. 
===== PAGE 73 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 73 
 
3.10.10.2.2 Advantages 
• Zero Dependencies: It is a pure JavaScript library with no external requirements, making 
it extremely easy to bundle within a web frontend. 
• Simplicity: It is very easy to set up and requires no background processes or system -
level configuration. 
• Portability: The index is just a JSON object, making it easy to store and transfer. 
3.10.10.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Performance Bottlenecks: Because it runs in the JavaScript thread, indexing thousands 
of files can block the user interface and cause noticeable lag. 
• Memory Footprint: It stores the entire inverted index in memory. For a large "Second 
Brain" containing thousands of notes, this can lead to massive RAM spikes in the 
frontend browser process. 
• Feature Set: It lacks advanced features like phrase matching or complex boolean logic 
that technical users often require for precise research. 
 
3.10.10.3 Apache Lucene 
3.10.10.3.1 Description 
Apache Lucene is the "industry standard" for full -text search libraries. Written in Java, it is the 
foundation for nearly every major search product in the world, including Elasticsearch and Solr. 
It is incredibly feature -rich, supporting everything from p honetic matching to complex 
geospatial queries. 
3.10.10.3.2 Advantages 
• Unmatched Power : It is arguably one of the most mature and widely used full -text 
search libraries available. 
• Extreme Stability: It has been maintained for over two decades and is used by the many 
large-scale production systems, ensuring maximum reliability. 
• Highly Optimized: Despite its age, it is still one of the fastest search engines available 
when properly configured. 
3.10.10.3.3 Disadvantages 
• JVM Dependency: Lucene requires the Java Virtual Machine (JVM). For a lightweight 
desktop app built with Rust and Tauri, forcing the user to install a 200MB+ Java runtime 
is a prohibitive "bloat" factor. 
• Technical Complexity : Its API is extremely low -level and complex, requiring a high 
degree of expertise to implement even a basic search interface. 
• Heavyweight: The memory overhead of the JVM and the Lucene structures is far beyond 
the requirements of a personal note-taking tool. 
 
===== PAGE 74 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
74 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
3.10.11 Math Rendering 
Technical documentation often requires complex mathematical notation. For Tessellum to serve 
as a research hub, it must render LaTeX -style equations with typographic precision. This 
subsection examines the trade -offs between rendering speed, accessibility,  and the library's 
impact on the application's initial load time. 
3.10.11.1 MathJax 
3.10.11.1.1 Description 
MathJax is the most established and comprehensive open -source JavaScript display engine for 
mathematics. It is highly modular and supports a wide variety of input formats, including TeX, 
LaTeX, MathML, and AsciiMath. Since its version 3.0 rewrite in TypeScript, it has moved toward 
a more modern architecture designed for faster rendering and better integration with web -
based environments. 
3.10.11.1.2 Advantages 
• Maximum Compatibility : It supports a vast range of LaTeX environments and 
commands (such as \label and \eqref for cross -referencing) that many other libraries 
cannot handle. 
• Superior Accessibility: It includes built -in features for screen readers and allows users 
to explore expressions interactively, which is a major factor for inclusive software. 
• Typographic Quality : It is widely considered to have the most consistent and high -
quality typography across different browsers and operating systems. 
3.10.11.1.3 Disadvantages 
• Resource Intensity: Despite improvements in version 3, MathJax is still "heavier" than 
its competitors. It carries a larger bundle size and can consume more system memory 
when rendering multiple equations. 
• Asynchronous Rendering : It often renders math asynchronously, which can lead to 
"layout shifts" (where text moves as equations suddenly appear), potentially 
interrupting the reading experience. 
• Font Loading: The initial loading of its specialized web fonts can be slower than more 
lightweight alternatives. 
 
3.10.11.2 Native MathML 
3.10.11.2.1 Description 
MathML (Mathematical Markup Language) is an XML -based standard for describing 
mathematical notation. Instead of using a JavaScript library to "draw" the equations, this 
approach relies on the browser's (or WebView's) native engine to interpret and render the math 
directly from the HTML source. 
===== PAGE 75 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 75 
 
3.10.11.2.2 Advantages 
• Zero Performance Overhead: Since the browser handles the rendering natively, there 
is no JavaScript to download or execute, making it the most lightweight solution 
possible. 
• Perfect Accessibility: Because it is a semantic web standard, it is natively understood by 
screen readers and assistive technologies without extra configuration. 
• Privacy and Security : By avoiding external scripts, it reduces the application's attack 
surface and eliminates dependencies on third-party libraries. 
3.10.11.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Inconsistent Browser Support : While support has improved (with Chrome recently 
joining Firefox and Safari), the rendering quality can vary wildly between different 
operating systems and browser versions. 
• Styling Limitations: It is much harder to customize the "look and feel" of the math to 
match a specific UI theme compared to CSS-based libraries. 
• Complexity of Input: Most users prefer writing in LaTeX, which requires an additional 
conversion step (using a tool like latex2mathml) before it can be rendered as MathML. 
 
3.10.11.3 MathQuill 
3.10.11.3.1 Description 
MathQuill is a specialized library that focuses on making math "editable" as well as renderable. 
It provides a "what -you-see-is-what-you-get" (WYSIWYG) interface, allowing users to type 
mathematics naturally as if they were using a standard text editor. 
3.10.11.3.2 Advantages 
• Interactive Input: It is the best choice for applications that require the user to input 
complex formulas without knowing LaTeX syntax. 
• Visual Feedback : It provides instant, real -time rendering as the user types, which is 
excellent for educational or collaborative tools. 
3.10.11.3.3 Disadvantages 
• Heavier Focus on Input : It is primarily an input tool; using it strictly for "viewing" or 
rendering static notes is less efficient than using a dedicated rendering engine. 
• Older Architecture: Its codebase is less modern than TypeScript -based libraries, which 
can lead to integration challenges with modern React/Vite workflows. 
• Performance: It is not optimized for rendering large documents with hundreds of 
equations, as every instance carries the overhead of the interactive input logic. 
 
===== PAGE 76 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
76 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
3.10.12 Diagramming Engine 
Visualizing logic through "Diagrams as Code" is a staple of technical writing. The chosen engine 
must allow users to maintain their diagrams as plain text within their Markdown files. We 
compare various engines based on their syntax maturity, rendering qua lity, and how well they 
integrate into a seamless, offline-first workflow. 
3.10.12.1 PlantUML 
3.10.12.1.1 Description 
PlantUML is a mature, open -source tool that allows users to create diagrams from a plain -text 
language. It is widely recognized as the industry standard for "Diagrams as Code," particularly 
for UML (Unified Modeling Language) structures such as sequence, class, and state diagrams. It 
is primarily built in Java and relies on the Graphviz software for rendering its layouts. 
3.10.12.1.2 Advantages 
• Feature Maturity: It supports an extensive range of diagram types and advanced UML 
features that many modern alternatives have yet to implement. 
• Standardization: The syntax is widely known and used across large -scale enterprise 
environments for technical documentation. 
• Extensive Theming: It offers highly customizable themes and the ability to define styles 
via external CSS-like files, allowing for professional-grade visual output. 
3.10.12.1.3 Disadvantages 
• Heavyweight Dependencies : It requires the Java Runtime Environment (JRE) to run 
locally. For Tessellum, which aims to be a lightweight, single-binary application, forcing 
the user to install a Java environment is a significant drawback. 
• Integration Complexity : Rendering diagrams in a web -based UI typically requires an 
external server or a complex WebAssembly port, which adds latency and architectural 
overhead to a local-first application. 
• Aesthetic Look : By default, the diagrams can have a  visual style that may require 
additional configuration to match modern UI conventions  unless, the user spends 
significant time in configuration and styling. 
 
3.10.12.2 Graphviz 
3.10.12.2.1 Description 
Graphviz is a venerable package of open -source tools for drawing graphs specified in "DOT" 
language scripts. It is focused on automated layout; the user defines the relationships (nodes 
and edges), and the software uses mathematical algorithms to determine  the most efficient 
visual representation. It is the "engine" that many other diagramming tools use under the hood. 
===== PAGE 77 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 77 
 
3.10.12.2.2 Advantages 
• Algorithmic Precision: It excels at visualizing complex, highly interconnected networks 
and hierarchical trees that would appear cluttered in other engines. 
• Performance: The underlying C libraries are extremely fast and efficient at processing 
large datasets and generating layouts. 
• Academic Credibility: It is the standard tool for computer science research and graph 
theory visualization, offering various layout engines (dot, neato, fdp) for different graph 
types. 
3.10.12.2.3 Disadvantages 
• Steep Learning Curve: The DOT language is highly technical and less intuitive for creating 
"standard" documentation diagrams like simple flowcharts or sequence diagrams. 
• Limited Manual Control : It is difficult to force the engine to place specific nodes in 
specific locations, as it prioritizes its own mathematical layout algorithms over user 
preference. 
• Static Nature: It is primarily designed for generating static image files (PNG, SVG) rather 
than interactive, responsive components that can be manipulated in real-time. 
 
3.10.12.3 Excalidraw 
3.10.12.3.1 Description 
Excalidraw is a virtual whiteboard tool that creates diagrams with a distinctive "hand-drawn" or 
"sketchy" look. While often used as a standalone web app, it is available as a React component 
library that can be embedded into other applications, allowing users to draw and save diagrams 
within the app's interface. 
3.10.12.3.2 Advantages 
• High Visual Appeal: The "hand-drawn" aesthetic is very popular among technical users 
for making documentation feel more approachable and less "rigid" during brainstorming 
phases. 
• Ease of Use: It provides a highly intuitive "drag-and-drop" interface that is much faster 
for creating quick, non-standard diagrams than writing code. 
• Direct Interactivity : Being a canvas -based tool, it allows users to modify diagrams 
directly within the UI, providing immediate visual feedback. 
3.10.12.3.3 Disadvantages 
• Non-Textual Nature : While it can export to a specific JSON format, it is not a true 
"Diagrams as Code" engine. This makes it difficult for a user to edit diagrams purely 
through the text editor, which breaks the seamless Markdown-based PKM workflow. 
• Bundle Size: The Excalidraw library is quite large, which would significantly increase the 
frontend bundle size and memory footprint of the application. 
===== PAGE 78 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
78 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Versioning Difficulty : Comparing changes (diffing) between two versions of an 
Excalidraw diagram is much harder for a user than diffing a few lines of plain text code. 
 
3.11  Description of the Proposed Solution 
This section outlines the architectural and functional design of Tessellum, a high-performance 
Personal Knowledge Management (PKM) tool specifically engineered for technical users. The 
proposed solution pivots away from the "Software as a Service" (SaaS) model and the resource-
heavy nature of Electron-based apps, offering instead a local-first, lightweight ecosystem deeply 
integrated into a developer's existing workflow. 
The following significant characteristics demonstrate why Tessellum is the most suitable 
solution for the identified problem: 
• High-Performance Hybrid Architecture (Rust + Tauri v2):  The solution leverages Tauri 
v2 as its core, separating the user interface (React) from the system logic (Rust). By 
avoiding a full Chromium instance for the backend, it drastically reduces RAM 
consumption (up to 90% less than alternatives like Obsidian or Notion) while ensuring 
memory safety through Rust. 
• Instant Search Engine with Tantivy:  Unlike JavaScript-based search implementations 
that degrade as the "Vault" grows, Tessellum integrates Tantivy (a full -text search 
engine written in Rust). This allows for complex queries, typo tolerance, and advanced 
filtering with near-zero latency, even in repositories containing thousands of Markdown 
files. 
• Specialized Technical Editing (CodeMirror 6 + Vim Mode):  The text editor is an 
integrated development environment based on CodeMirror 6. It offers native support 
for Vim editing modes, advanced syntax highlighting, and a modular architecture that 
enables technical "power user" features like slash commands  and terminal-style 
callouts. 
• Non-Linear Graph Visualization (Cytoscape.js + Grafeo):  The solution facilitates 
networked thinking where notes are interconnected. By using Cytoscape.js on the 
frontend and a relational graph engine on the backend, users can visualize and navigate 
connections between ideas, making it easier to discover patterns and synthesize 
complex information. 
• Native Support for Scientific and Technical Documentation:  Tessellum seamlessly 
integrates KaTeX for rendering complex mathematical formulas and Mermaid.js for 
creating diagrams (flowcharts, sequence, Gantt) directly from code. This eliminates the 
need for external tools when creating high-quality technical documentation. 
• Local-First Persistence and Absolute Privacy: All data is stored in standard Markdown 
files on the user's local file system, supplemented by a SQLite database for efficient 
Commented [JC23]: @ENRIQUE JUAN DE ANDRES GALIANA 
Sección para revisar 
===== PAGE 79 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 79 
 
metadata and link management. This ensures total user control, permanent offline 
access, and full compatibility with version control systems like Git. 
• Optimized, Distraction-Free Interface (Tailwind CSS):  The UI design follows principles 
of technical minimalism. Built with Tailwind CSS , the interface is fast and supports 
dynamic themes—including circadian themes based on the user's location via suncalc—
to minimize cognitive load during deep work or study sessions. 
• Plugin Ecosystem and Extensibility:  Leveraging the new Tauri v2 plugin architecture, 
the solution is built for growth. It allows for the addition of system -level functionalities 
(filesystem access, native notifications, dialogs) without compromising the stability of 
the application core.

3.13  Project Organization and Management 
3.13.1 Organization Breakdown Structure (OBS) 
This section defines the roles and responsibilities required for the successful delivery of 
Tessellum. Although the execution is centralized in a single individual, the project is organized 
into distinct functional areas to ensure methodological rigor and proper cost allocation within 
the project budget. 
• Management and Oversight 
o Project Supervisor: Provides academic guidance, validates milestones, and 
ensures compliance with academic requirements. 
▪ Responsible for validating project milestones and ensuring the work 
adheres to UNE 157801 academic standards. 
o Project Manager (Developer Role): Responsible for the administrative health of 
the project. 
▪ Tasks include WBS maintenance, schedule tracking in MS Project, and 
the management of the Risk Register and Issue Log. 
 
• Engineering and Development 
o Systems Architect: Defines the high-level logic for the Local-first architecture. 
▪ Responsible for the design of the Tauri IPC Bridge  and the semantic 
structure of the Knowledge Graph. 
o Backend Engineer (Rust Specialist):  Focuses on memory safety, high -
performance file system operations, and low-level systems logic. 
o Frontend Engineer (React/TS Specialist):  Responsible for the User Interface 
(UI), User Experience (UX), and the implementation of the Markdown rendering 
engine and Graph View. 
 
• Quality and Documentation 
o QA/Test Engineer:  Responsible for the execution of the Test Plan , 
encompassing Unit Testing in Rust and Integration Testing for the IPC bridge. 
o Technical Writer: Responsible for drafting the mandatory Four Books of the 
technical memory and the User Manual for the "Technical User" profile.

3.13.2 Scope Changes Management Guidelines 
In accordance with the Scrum framework, the scope of this project is defined by the Product 
Backlog. Unlike traditional methodologies where changes require formal bureaucratic "Change 
Requests," this project treats scope as a flexible but prioritized list of functionalities. Any new 
requirement, feature request, or modification to the existing system is  documented as a new 
item in the Product Backlog; no change is implemented immediately, as it must first be 
categorized and estimated. 
To manage these changes effectively, a structured Refinement Process  is established. This 
workflow begins with the identification of a necessary change by either the Client (Tutor) or the 
Developer, followed by an evaluation of its impact on the final project deadline. Finally, the item 
is prioritized: high-priority items move to the top of the backlog, potentially displacing lower -
priority features to ensure the project remains within the established academic timeframe. 
To protect the immediate development cycle, Sprint Integrity  is strictly maintained. Once a 
Sprint has started, its specific scope is locked to prevent "Scope Creep." Any change requested 
during an active Sprint is added to the Backlog for consideration during the next Sprint Planning 
session. If a scope of change is significant enough to threaten the final delivery date, a Backlog 
Grooming session is held with the Project Tutor. During this session, non -essential Functional 
Requirements (such as advanced theme customization) may be de-scoped to accommodate the 
new high-priority requirements. 
Finally, to ensure academic transparency, all major shifts in the project’s direction are recorded 
in Sprint Retrospective reports. This ensures that the evolution of the software—from a simple 
note-taker to a complex knowledge graph system —is fully documented and justified for the 
examination board.
