3.13.3 Project Tracking Guidelines 
Project progress will be monitored using a combination of Scrum artifacts and technical 
performance benchmarks. This ensures that both the functional progress (features) and the 
technical health (performance of the knowledge graph and editor) stay on target. 
The project is managed through Sprint-Based Monitoring  cycles of three weeks. Each cycle 
begins with a Sprint Planning session to define the subset of the Product Backlog for 
development. Daily progress is maintained through Daily Checkpoints —brief self -audits to 
identify technical "blockers" in the rendering logic or API—and ends with Sprint Reviews, where 
the latest increment (e.g., terminal callouts or graph views) is demonstrated to the tutor to 
validate velocity. 
For Visual Progress Management, a Kanban Board tracks tasks through four workflow states: 
To Do, In Progress, Testing/Review, and Done. To detect potential delays in complex features 
like the plugin engine, a Burndown Chart is maintained to visualize work remaining versus time 
available, allowing for early detection of velocity drops. 
Given the specialized nature of this application, tracking includes specific Technical 
Performance Metrics. Specifically, Rendering Latency is audited to ensure input lag remains 
below 16ms; any breach is immediately flagged as priority technical debt. Similarly, Graph 
Scalability (FPS and load times) is tracked as the vault size increases to ensure the system meets 
NFR5.2. 
This is supported by continuous Risk Monitoring, where the Project Risk Register is updated at 
the end of every Sprint to address API instability, data integrity in Markdown files, and 
complexity creep. Finally, rigorous Quality Control is enforced through the Definition of Done 
(DoD). Progress is only officially recorded for tasks that fully satisfy the requirements outlined 
in Section 5, preventing the accumulation of "hidden work" and ensuring the codebase remains 
maintainable for the final degree of presentation. 
 
3.13.4 Information Collection and Distribution 
Guidelines 
This section defines how project -related data is gathered, stored, and shared among 
stakeholders (Developer and Tutor) to ensure transparency and technical continuity throughout 
the lifecycle of Tessellum. 
The primary Source of Truth  for the project is a Git -based repository (e.g., GitHub or GitLab). 
This centralized repository hosts the source code for the core editor and knowledge graph 
engine, as well as technical specifications, design mockups, and sample Markdown vaults for 
testing. To ensure future maintainability and facilitate potential third -party integration, 
Technical Documentation —specifically regarding the Plugin API, CSS variables, and the 
architecture of the per -line rendering engine —is maintai ned in a dedicated internal Wiki or 
standardized README files. 
===== PAGE 90 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
90 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
Project progress is gathered and communicated through Sprint Artifacts at the end of every 
three-week cycle. These deliverables include the Sprint Backlog of completed tasks, a technical 
Sprint Report documenting milestones and performance benchmarks, and a visual Burndown 
Chart to track the rate of completion against the final deadline. These materials are shared 
through formal Distribution Channels, providing the tutor with continuous repository access for 
code review, while utilizing email for formal reports and cloud storage for non-code assets, such 
as high-resolution UI demonstrations or heavy design files. 
Finally, to support the project’s local-first philosophy, a strict Backup and Data Integrity strategy 
is enforced. This includes regular pushes of the codebase to the remote repository and the use 
of diverse, anonymized Markdown samples to verify that the linking and graph generation logic 
remains robust across updates. 
 
3.13.5 Client-Provider Communication Guidelines 
To ensure the project aligns with the tutor's (Client) expectations, the following communication 
protocols are established: 
• Sprint Planning & Review (Every 3 weeks):  A formal meeting or digital sync to 
demonstrate the functionality developed in the previous 3 weeks and to agree on the 
goals for the next cycle. 
• Asynchronous Communication: For urgent technical queries, communication will be 
handled via email, with a maximum expected response time of 48 hours. 
• Feedback Loops:  Feedback on UI/UX will be collected during the Sprint Review and 
translated into new Product Backlog items if necessary. 
 
3.13.6 Deliverable Approval Guidelines 
This section defines the formal process for validating and approving the project's outputs. Given 
the iterative nature of Scrum, approval is not a single event at the end of the project, but a 
continuous process occurs every three weeks. 
• Sprint-Level Approval: At the conclusion of each 3-week Sprint, a Sprint Review is held. 
The "Client" evaluates the increment against the Acceptance Criteria of the User Stories. 
A feature is only approved if it strictly adheres to the Definition of Done (DoD) outlined 
in Section 5, ensuring that the code is not only functional but also optimized for the per-
line rendering engine. 
• Technical Validation: Before any major module is considered "Approved," it must pass 
a technical review focusing on: 
o Performance: Meeting the response time requirements (NFR5.1 and NFR5.2). 
===== PAGE 91 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 91 
 
o Integrity: Ensuring the Markdown parser correctly handles complex structures 
like terminal callouts without data loss. 
• Documentation Approval: Technical documentation, including the Plugin API reference 
and the system architecture diagrams, must be reviewed for clarity and accuracy. 
Approval is granted when the documentation is sufficient for a third-party developer to 
create a basic plugin or theme. 
• Final Project Approval: The final deliverable—consisting of the complete source code, 
the compiled application, and the comprehensive project report—requires a final sign-
off from the tutor. This indicates that the project is ready for formal defense before the 
examination board. 
3.13.7 Project Execution Location 
The development, testing, and management of this project are carried out in a specialized local 
environment designed to ensure cross-platform stability. 
• Primary Development Environment:  The core development (architecture design, UI 
implementation, and Knowledge Graph logic) is performed on a personal workstation 
running Windows 11 . This environment hosts the primary Integrated Development 
Environment (IDE) and the local development servers. 
• Compatibility Testing Environment (Linux): To satisfy the cross-platform technological 
requirement (NFR2.1), a secondary hardware-level environment is utilized. A dedicated 
hard drive has been configured to boot an Arch Linux distribution. This allows for: 
o Native verification of Terminal Callouts  and shell integration within a Unix -
based environment. 
o Validation of the Per-line rendering engine  performance under different 
window managers and graphics drivers. 
o Ensuring that the Plugin API interacts correctly with the Linux file system. 
• Version Control and Off -site Infrastructure:  While the coding is local, the project’s 
"logical location" for collaboration and backup is GitHub. This serves as the remote 
repository for all source code, issue tracking, and the project’s Kanban board. 
• Virtual Meeting Spaces: Coordination with the project tutor and formal Sprint Reviews 
(every 3 weeks) take place via Microsoft Teams. 
 
3.14  Time Schedule 
 
===== PAGE 92 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
92 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
The purpose of this section is to define the sequential ordering, time estimation of activities, 
and technological dependency constraints required for the definitive development of the 
information system under this project. The structured time planning pre sented below strictly 
complies with the regulatory criteria of the UNE 157801  standard, ensuring methodological 
consistency between the software lifecycle phases and the hierarchical decomposition of tasks. 
The scheduling strategy is formally articulated based on three fundamental metric dimensions: 
• Work Breakdown Structure (WBS):  A deliverable-oriented hierarchical decomposition 
that divides the project into three main operational phases: Technical Enablement & 
Readiness, Implementation, and Documentation. 
• Hybrid Lifecycle Model:  The schedule integrates an initial analytical -training phase 
designed to mitigate technological risks stemming from the selected core stack (Rust 
Systems Programming, TypeScript/React, and the Tauri framework), sequentially linked 
to an incremental development model divided into five (5) Agile sprints, and concluding 
with the formal documentation required by systems engineering standards. 
• Precedence Logic and Custom Calendar Constraints:  Start and finish dates have been 
calculated automatically via a hierarchical scheduling engine using Finish-to-Start (FS) 
deterministic relationships. 
The project baseline scheduling calendar is parameterized on a standard 4-hour business 
workday (20 hours per week) . However, to optimize resource utilization and align with the 
specific effort constraints of the lifecycle, specialized calendar adjustments have been applied 
to distinct phases: 
1. Technical Enablement & Readiness (Phase 1.1):  Features a restricted calendar 
allocation with reduced active hours to account for asynchronous, self -paced learning 
and onboarding limitations. 
2. Sprint 5 (Phase 1.2.5) & Documentation (Phase 1.3):  Configured with high -capacity 
calendars featuring increased daily time allocations to accommodate intensive system 
integration, end-to-end testing, and the rigorous generation of the engineering project 
blueprints. 
Fractional variations observed in task durations are the direct mathematical output of these 
varying resource calendar profiles intersecting with fixed-work assignments. 
The comprehensive project chronogram matrix is detailed below, parameterized by WBS 
identifier, task nomenclature, estimated duration, start/finish temporal milestones, and 
technological precedence vectors.

4.1 Input Documentation 
This annex includes the set of documents and foundational materials that were available to the 
author at the beginning of the project or that served as a formal starting point for its execution.  
For Project Tessellum, the following input documents and materials have been utilized: 
• Project Proposal and Academic Objectives: The initial proposal approved by the School 
of Computer Engineering at the University of Oviedo , which established the core goal 
of developing a local -first application for personal knowledge management using 
knowledge graphs.  
• Standards and Regulations: 
o Standard UNE 157801:2007 : Utilized as the primary template and structural 
guide for the development of Information Technology projects.  
o General Data Protection Regulation (EU) 2016/679 (GDPR): Provided the legal 
constraints regarding user data privacy and sovereignty that shaped the "Local-
First" architecture.  
• Methodological Frameworks: 
o The Scrum Guide (2020) : Served as the input for managing the iterative 
development cycle, defining the roles, artifacts, and ceremonies used during the 
287-day execution period.  
• Conceptual and Theoretical Inputs: 
o "Local-first software" (Ink & Switch, 2019) : The foundational research paper 
that defined the technical ideals of fast response, offline capability, and data 
ownership implemented in the project.  
o "Building a Second Brain" (Tiago Forte) : The methodology for personal 
knowledge management (PKM) that served as the primary functional 
requirement for the system's design.  
• Technical Specifications of Core Libraries: The official documentation for Tauri v2, Rust, 
React, and SQLite, which acted as the technical constraints and capabilities for the 
backend and frontend shells.

4.2 System Analysis and Design 
4.2.1 Analysis 
The analysis phase of Project Tessellum is conducted as a continuous and iterative process 
within the Scrum framework. Rather than a static, upfront specification, the system is modeled 
through the refinement of the Product Backlog, ensuring that technical decisions remain aligned 
with the initial requirements while adapting to discoveries made during development. 
4.2.1.1 System Model to be Built 
The system model for Project Tessellum serves as the architectural blueprint that translates the 
high-level objectives into a defined technical structure. This model is defined across three 
dimensions: the conceptual representation of information, the persistence strategy for data 
sovereignty, and the execution logic for high-performance interaction.  
 
Conceptual Model: The Knowledge Graph 
Tessellum is modeled as a non -hierarchical relational network, moving away from traditional 
folder-based systems that contribute to information fragmentation.  
• Nodes and Edges: Each informative unit (a Markdown note) is treated as a node in the 
graph, possessing metadata such as titles, tags, and timestamps. The explicit semantic 
relationships between these notes are represented as edges.  
• Bi-directional Navigation: The model utilizes bi-directional linking as its primary linking 
mechanism. This ensures that relationships are traversed in both directions, allowing 
relationships to be traversed in both directions, which makes it possible to identify 
connections that would not be visible in a linear structure.  
 
Data Model: Local-First Persistence 
To satisfy the requirements of privacy and data ownership, the system employs a hybrid "Local-
First" persistence architecture.  
• Primary Source of Truth: User data is stored exclusively on the local filesystem as plain-
text Markdown (.md) files. This ensures full data portability and prevents vendor lock -
in, as the files remain accessible by any standard text editor.  
• Relational Projection (Metadata Cache): For high-speed retrieval, the system maintains 
a structured SQLite database. This cache indexes note titles, bidirectional links, and tags, 
enabling complex relational queries and graph traversals without the performance 
penalty of re-parsing the entire vault on every interaction.  
 
Commented [JC30]: @ENRIQUE JUAN DE ANDRES GALIANA 
Sección para revisar 
===== PAGE 106 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
106 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
Execution Model: Asynchronous Hybrid Architecture 
The execution model is based on a decoupled, event -driven architecture that separates high -
performance system logic from the user interface.  
• Backend System Core (Rust) : A high -performance backend, powered by the Tokio 
runtime, handles heavy I/O operations, full -text indexing (via Tantivy), and graph 
calculations asynchronously. This ensures that computationally expensive tasks do not 
block the user's workflow.  
• Reactive Frontend (React/TypeScript) : The interface acts as a reactive presentation 
layer that communicates with the core through a  Tauri IPC (Inter -Process 
Communication) bridge.  
• Non-Blocking Interaction : All requests —from opening a note to executing a global 
search—are modeled as asynchronous commands. This ensures the editor maintains a 
target input latency of < 16ms.  
 
4.2.1.2 Agile Requirement Analysis and Backlog Refinement 
This section details the continuous process of analyzing user needs and translating them into 
technical requirements within the Scrum framework. Unlike traditional "Big Design Up Front" 
approaches, analysis in Tessellum is an ongoing activity that ensures the development remains 
aligned with the project's objectives while allowing for adjustments during development. 
 
Product Backlog Construction 
The analysis phase began by synthesizing the initial requirements into a Product Backlog. This 
backlog serves as the central reference for all planned work . To manage scope effectively, 
requirements were grouped into three high-level Epics: 
1. Foundational Infrastructure: Including the file system watcher, the SQLite metadata 
cache, and the Tauri IPC bridge. 
2. Core Editor and Knowledge Management : Focused on Markdown rendering, bi -
directional linking, and tagging systems. 
3. Discovery and Visualization : Covering full -text search, global/local graph views, and 
plugin extensibility. 
 
Iterative Refinement (Grooming) 
Throughout the project, high -level requirements were decomposed into 46 granular User 
Stories (US). The refinement process followed a defined analytical process: 
• Decomposition: Breaking down complex features into vertical slices. 
===== PAGE 107 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 107 
 
• Technical Discovery : Identifying edge cases, such as handling circular links in the 
knowledge graph or managing file system race conditions during bulk indexing. 
• Prioritization: Utilizing the MoSCoW method (Must have, Should have, Could have, 
Won't have) to ensure the Minimum Viable Product (MVP) was achieved within the 287-
day project timeline. 
 
The Weighted Complexity Model (𝑾𝒄) 
A critical component of the requirement analysis was the application of a Weighted Complexity 
Model. To provide a more structured basis for effort estimation than story points alone , each 
requirement was analyzed across four technical variables: 
1. 𝑽𝒖𝒊 (User Interface): Complexity of the React components and styling. 
2. 𝑽𝒅𝒃(Data/Persistence): Impact on the relational SQLite schema and indexing logic. 
3. 𝑽𝒈𝒓𝒂𝒑𝒉 (Relational Logic): Complexity of graph traversal and link discovery algorithms. 
4. 𝑽𝒔𝒚𝒔 (System/API): Difficulty of the Rust backend implementation and OS -level 
interactions. 
The resulting complexity score determined the effort estimation, where 87% of the backlog  
items were decomposed into Small (S) or Extra-Small (XS) tasks to keep individual tasks within a 
manageable scope for a single developer. 
 
Definition of Done (DoD) as Analytical Criteria 
The analysis of each requirement is finalized by establishing a formal Definition of Done (DoD). 
This serves as a quality criteria that every feature must fulfill: 
• Privacy Verification: Confirmation that the feature adheres to the "Local -First" policy 
with confirmation that no data is transmitted to external services. 
• Performance Validation: Ensuring the feature does not compromise the < 16ms input 
latency target. 
• Documentation and Testing : Verification that the logic is covered by unit tests and 
reflected in the technical documentation. 
 
4.2.1.3 User Interface Analysis 
This section analyzes the ergonomic and functional requirements of the human -system 
interface, focusing on providing an efficient environment for intensive knowledge work. The UI 
model for Tessellum is designed to reduce interface complexity that interrupts the user's 
===== PAGE 108 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
108 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
workflow, ensuring that the interface facilitates rather than hinders the user's sustained 
concentration. 
 
Layout Strategy and Visual Hierarchy 
The interface is analyzed to support a workflow that prioritizes the editor area , minimizing 
unnecessary visual elements  while keeping relational data accessible. The proposed model 
utilizes a flexible three-column layout: 
• Navigation Zone (Left Sidebar) : Analyzed as a collapsible area for high -level 
organization, containing the file explorer, search bar, and tag cloud. 
• The Workspace (Central Editor) : The focal point of the application. It is analyzed to 
prioritize vertical space and typography, ensuring the writing experience is comparable 
in responsiveness to a native text editor (NFR3.1). 
• Contextual Zone (Right Panel): Reserved for supplementary relational information, such 
as the Local Graph View and backlinks, allowing the user to see immediate connections 
without leaving the current note. 
 
Interaction Model: Keyboard-Centric Workflow 
To satisfy the needs of the Technical User persona, the UI is analyzed to minimize reliance on 
the mouse, which can interrupt the users workflow. 
• Slash Commands : A command -palette interface (triggered by /) is analyzed to allow 
formatting, embedding, and plugin execution directly from the cursor position. 
• Wiki-link Triggers: The interface must support real -time search across all notes in the 
vault when [[ is typed, allowing the user to link to existing notes or create new ones 
without manual file management. 
 
Dynamic Performance Rendering (Per-Line Model) 
A finding during the prototyping phase was that full-document re-rendering causes measurable 
rendering delays in large files. 
• Active Line Targeting: The UI rendering engine is analyzed to update only the specific 
line being edited ( FR1.2). This satisfies NFR5.1 (< 16ms latency)  by ensuring that the 
DOM (Document Object Model) operations remain constant in complexity regardless of 
total file size. 
• Layered Rendering: The analysis dictates that syntax highlighting (Markdown/LaTeX) 
should be performed on a separate layer from raw text input to prevent the main thread 
from blocking during sustained text input. 
===== PAGE 109 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 109 
 
 
Graph View Ergonomics 
The visualization of the knowledge graph is analyzed as a primary navigational tool rather than 
a static map. 
• Spatial Navigation: The model includes zoom, pan, and force -directed gravity settings 
to help the user disambiguate dense clusters of notes. 
• Contextual Filtering : To prevent cognitive overload in large vaults, the UI analysis 
includes "Depth -based Filtering," which shows only the immediate neighbors of a 
selected note, facilitating a more focused exploration. 
 
Iterative Functional Validation and Refinement 
The UI analysis was validated through an iterative testing process, in which early functional 
versions of Tessellum were used to draft the project's own technical documentation. This 
allowed for the identification of usability issues during actual use. Spe cifically, the process 
revealed that the global graph view often became too dense to be useful for routine navigation, 
which led to the implementation of the Local Graph View as a core component. 
 
4.2.1.3.1 Interface description 
 
 
Figure 4.2.1 Application Wireframe 

===== PAGE 110 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory

To illustrate the layout strategy and interaction models described in the previous sections, a 
conceptual wireframe was developed to define the system's spatial distribution. As shown in 
Figure 4.2.1, the interface is organised into four primary functional zones, keeping the focus on 
writing while maintaining immediate access to relational metadata. 
The functional distribution is defined as follows: 
 
1. Application Title Bar (Top Header) 
The top header serves as the main control area for layout and global utilities. It contains a 
set of interactive toggles that allow the user to adjust the workspace layout based on the 
current task: 
• Layout management: Dedicated toggles to expand or collapse both sidebars, allowing 
the user to switch to a minimal view with both sidebars hidden (NFR3.1). 
• View toggles: Switches for activating the Local Graph View and the search functionality, 
keeping these tools accessible without occupying permanent screen space. 
2. Primary Management Sidebar (Left) 
The left sidebar is the main area for file and vault management. This pane integrates: 
• Vault and file management: Controls for switching between vaults, along with buttons 
for creating new notes and folders. 
• File tree hierarchy:  A dynamic representation of the local filesystem, providing a 
directory-based navigation model. 
• Global utilities:  Access to system settings and the Global Graph View, grouping 
administrative and navigation tools in one place. 
3. Central Workspace: The Editor 
The central portion of the application is reserved for the Markdown editor. This zone is 
free of secondary UI elements to keep the focus on writing. It is the area where the per-
line rendering model (FR1.2) is applied, providing an environment suited to writing and 
formatting notes. 
4. Supplemental Context Sidebar (Right) 
To the right of the editor, a secondary sidebar provides real -time metadata and structural 
information about the active document. This zone is divided into three components: 
• Backlinks: A list of all notes in the vault that link to the current document, supporting 
bi-directional discovery (FR1.4). 
• Tags: The metadata tags found within the note, available for quick categorization. 
• Document outline: A table of contents generated from the Markdown headers (H1–H6), 
allowing navigation within long-form documents.

Recursive Functional Validation and Iterative Refinement 
The UI analysis was validated through a recursive testing process, wherein early functional 
versions of Tessellum were utilized to draft the project’s own technical documentation. This 
internal pilot testing allowed for the identification of UX bottlenecks  under real -world 
conditions. Specifically, this process revealed that a "global graph" often became too cluttered 
for daily tasks, leading to the prioritized analysis and implementation of the Local Graph View 
as a core component for improved usability and navigation. 
 
 
 
Figure 4.2.2 Settings Wireframe

configuration interface was analyzed. As illustrated in Figure 4.2.2, the Settings Panel is modeled

preferences remain organized and accessible without overwhelming the user. 
The functional distribution of the configuration interface is defined as follows: 
1. Category Navigation (Left Pane)

Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory

The left sidebar of the modal, as seen in Figure  4.2.2, serves as the primary navigation for

domains to customize their experience: 
• General: Core application behavior, including startup preferences and system 
integration. 
• Editor: Specific settings for the writing environment, such as line wrapping, font size, 
and Markdown parsing behavior. 
• Appearance: Interface for the Theme Engine (FR3.2), where users can modify visual 
variables, themes, and UI scaling. 
• Shortcuts: Configuration of the keyboard-centric workflow, allowing users to remap 
hotkeys for common actions to maintain their flow state. 
• Accessibility: Options dedicated to ensuring the application remains usable for all 
users, including high-contrast modes and screen-reader compatibility. 
• Plugins: The management hub for the Plugin API (FR3.3) , where third -party 
extensions are enabled, disabled, and configured.

of the application's performance and behavior. 
• Real-time Feedback : Changes applied in this pane are analyzed to provide 
immediate visual or functional feedback, ensuring the user can verify their 
configuration before returning to the workspace. 
3. Modal Controls and Layout Integrity 
As seen in  Figure 4.2.2 , the interface includes a persistent close trigger, ensuring that 
configuration is a transient task that does not permanently obstruct the primary writing 
workspace. The layout is analyzed to be scalable; as the ecosystem of "Plugins" and 
"Shortcuts" grow s, the vertical list remains scrollable, satisfying the long -term 
maintainability requirements of the software. 
 
4.2.1.4 System Integration and Communication Model 
This section analyzes the structural and operational relationship between the system's core 
components. Given the hybrid nature of Tessellum —which combines a high-performance Rust 
backend with a reactive React/TypeScript frontend—the communication model is a critical 
factor in ensuring both system security and the performance target of < 16ms input latency 
(NFR5.1). 
===== PAGE 113 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 113 
 
The integration is modeled as a decoupled system connected through a secure Inter-Process 
Communication (IPC) bridge provided by the Tauri framework. 
 
Frontend-to-Backend: The Command Pattern (Invoke) 
The primary method of communication is the Asynchronous Command Pattern. In this model: 
• Request Execution: The frontend triggers specific system actions (such as "Save File," 
"Search Vault," or "Generate Graph") by invoking typed commands. 
• Security Boundary: The frontend does not have direct access to the file system or the 
SQLite database. Instead, it sends a request to the Rust core, which validates the 
operation before execution. 
• Non-Blocking Logic: All commands are executed as fragments of asynchronous code. 
The backend processes the request on a separate thread using the Tokio runtime , 
allowing the UI thread to remain free for rendering and user input. 
 
Backend-to-Frontend: The Event Emission Pattern (Emit/Listen) 
For operations that are not initiated by the user but by the system state, an Event-Driven Model 
is utilized: 
• Proactive Notifications : The backend acts as a publisher that "emits" events to the 
frontend. This is essential for the File Watcher functionality; when a file is modified 
externally in the local directory, the Rust core notifies the UI to refresh the content. 
• Global State Synchronization: Events are used to broadcast changes in the knowledge 
graph's structure, ensuring that the Local Graph View stays synchronized with the actual 
file state without requiring constant polling from the frontend. 
 
Data Contract and Serialization (JSON/Serde) 
The communication between the two memory-isolated environments (the JavaScript V8 engine 
and the Rust binary) requires a standardized data contract: 
• Serialization Protocol: All data exchanged over the IPC bridge is serialized into JSON. 
• Type Safety : To ensure integrity, the system utilizes Serde in Rust and matching 
TypeScript interfaces. This ensures that complex relational data structures—such as the 
nodes and edges of the knowledge graph—are transmitted without loss of information 
or structural corruption. 
 
Performance Strategy: The Asynchronous Bridge 
===== PAGE 114 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
114 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
The analysis of this communication model is driven by the need for high responsiveness. By 
treating the IPC bridge as an asynchronous channel: 
• Latency Management : Heavy computations (like full -text indexing or force -directed 
graph calculations) are offloaded to the backend. The frontend receives only the "view-
ready" result. 
• Concurrent Processing : The model supports multiple simultaneous requests. For 
example, the system can perform a full -text search in the background while the user 
continues to type in the central editor, fulfilling the requirement for a professional -
grade, distraction-free environment. 
 
4.2.1.5 Testing Plan Specification 
 
This document defines the testing plan for the Tessellum application, structured in accordance 
with the principles of the UNE 157801 standard for software project specifications. This plan 
defines the verification procedures used to identify and resolve so ftware defects during the 
implementation phase, covering functional requirements and user interface interactions. 
The testing strategy is organized into three levels: 
• Unit Tests:  Verify the functional correctness of individual modules, classes, and 
components in isolation. 
• Integration Tests:  Verify that groups of interacting components function correctly 
together to execute specific workflows. 
• System Tests: Verify the fully assembled application end -to-end against the functional 
and technical specifications, including host environment interactions. 
The test cases are derived from the use cases and scenarios identified in the functional 
specification. The technical stack under test comprises: 
• Frontend: React, TypeScript, Zustand state stores, and the Tauri Inter -Process 
Communication (IPC) bridge. 
• Backend: Rust, Tauri command handlers, SQLite (via sqlx), Tantivy full -text search 
engine, and the Grafeo graph projection module. 
• Testing Tools:  Vitest with jsdom and React Testing Library for frontend verification; 
cargo test for backend verification; Playwright with tauri -driver for end-to-end system 
testing. 
 
===== PAGE 115 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 115

4.2.1.5.4 Error Detection and Correction Mechanisms 
The testing framework implements structured error detection criteria to isolate and resolve 
application defects during development. 
1. Testing Techniques Applied 
Verification procedures apply three testing methodologies: 
• Equivalence Class Partitioning (ECP):  Input domains are partitioned into valid and 
invalid operational classes. Verification boundaries check parameters such as supported 
===== PAGE 130 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
130 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
vs. unsupported system locales, Markdown vs. binary file types, and file system targets 
inside vs. outside vault paths. 
• Boundary Value Analysis (BVA): Verification targets operational limits and conditions, 
including editor font sizes clamped at 12 and 24 pixels, the 30 -day trash cleanup 
retention mark, state history limits, and debounce timer intervals. 
• Error Guessing:  Test cases target common software failure points including local 
database corruption, operating system clipboard lockups, malformed file paths, 
directory traversal attempts, and uninitialized data layers. 
 
2. Coverage Criteria 
The project configuration mandates compliance with the following coverage thresholds before 
code integration: 
Layer / Component Statement 
Coverage 
Branch Coverage 
Frontend data stores and utility modules ≥ 90% N/A 
Frontend interface modals and application 
hooks 
N/A ≥ 85% 
Backend persistence modules (trash.rs, 
validate.rs) 
≥ 90% N/A 
Backend controller API branches N/A 100% (All paths 
exercised) 
 
3. Continuous Integration Gates 
Automated test suites run in a sequential pipeline managed by the continuous integration 
system. The execution order is defined as follows: 
1. cargo test --manifest-path src -tauri/Cargo.toml — Executes backend unit and 
integration tests. 
2. npx vitest run --coverage — Executes frontend unit and interface component tests. 
3. npx playwright test — Executes end-to-end system testing using the Tauri automation 
driver. 
A failure detected within any individual step stops the pipeline execution, preventing code 
integration or release packaging. 
 
4. Test Isolation Contract 
===== PAGE 131 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 131 
 
Verification runs require isolated environments to guarantee reproducibility: 
• Frontend tests clear the tracking state stores, reset browser storage structures 
(localStorage, sessionStorage), and restore mock functions after the execution of each 
test case. 
• Backend tests initialize isolated temporary directories and separate unique SQLite 
databases for each run. No environmental state is shared across test processes. 
• System tests restore the target vault workspace using a clean instance of the seeded 
vault fixture prior to beginning an automated journey. 
 
5. Suspension and Resumption Criteria 
The execution of automated testing routines is suspended under the following environmental 
conditions: 
• Failure within the application boot sequence or core initialization routine. 
• Version mismatch between the installed system browser components and automation 
driver binaries. 
• File system write blocks preventing the initialization of test fixtures. 
• Corruption within database structures or search index templates used for fixture 
generation. 
Testing execution resumes once environmental stability is re-established, fixture configurations 
complete successfully, or faulty external resources are replaced with deterministic software 
stubs. 
 
6. Defect Tracking 
Test suite failures generate an entry within the issue tracking framework, linked to the 
corresponding test case identifier. Defect tracking logs trace failures back to their originating 
use case parameters and scenario descriptions, ensuring that corrections undergo validation by 
re-executing the failed test case. 
 
4.2.2 Design 
4.2.2.1 System Design and Architecture 
The scope of this chapter is limited to the implemented software architecture of Tessellum as it 
exists in the current version of the repository. The focus is centered on three architectural epics 
that organize the system: 
Commented [JC31]: @ENRIQUE JUAN DE ANDRES GALIANA 
Sección para revisar 
Commented [JC32]: @ENRIQUE JUAN DE ANDRES GALIANA 
Sección para revisar 
===== PAGE 132 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
132 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Foundational Infrastructure: The substrate for local-first operations. 
• Core Editor and Knowledge Management: The semantic interpretation of Markdown. 
• Discovery and Visualization: The projection of data for user exploration. 
 
Architectural Context 
The architecture is divided into four layers: 
• The Vault Layer: Contains notes, assets, and metadata in the local filesystem. 
• The Frontend Layer: Implemented in React/TypeScript, responsible for UI composition 
and state management. 
• The Backend Layer:  Implemented in Rust via Tauri commands, responsible for 
filesystem coordination, indexing, and performance-critical services. 
• The Derived Data Layer:  Composed of SQLite, Tantivy, and Grafeo, storing optimised 
projections of vault content. 
 
Main Architectural Components 
On the frontend, the main orchestration point is src/App.tsx, which restores workspace state 
and coordinates synchronization. State is managed through focused stores: 
src/stores/vaultStore.ts, src/stores/searchStore.ts, and src/stores/graphStore.ts. 
On the backend, the entry point is src-tauri/src/lib.rs, which initializes the application state and 
registers Tauri commands. The local derived data model is split by responsibility: 
• src-tauri/src/db.rs: Manages SQLite tables for notes, links, and tags. 
• src-tauri/src/search.rs: Manages Tantivy-backed full-text retrieval. 
• src-tauri/src/grafeo_projection.rs: Synchronizes the graph-native database. 
 
Epic I: Foundational Infrastructure 
• Purpose of the Epic 
The purpose of this epic is to ensure that a local Markdown vault can be treated as the 
source of truth while supporting responsive interaction and cached metadata. This includes 
the IPC boundary, the filesystem watcher, and the coordination logic. 
• React-Rust Bridge: IPC Pattern and Non-Blocking Execution 
===== PAGE 133 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 133 
 
The communication contract between the React frontend and the Rust backend is governed 
by a Readiness-First pattern. Because the application is built on Tauri, the frontend issues 
asynchronous commands through the IPC bridge. 
• 1. Initialization and Readiness Check 
Before any search can be performed, the system must verify the state of the backend. This 
prevents the UI from attempting to query an uninitialized or stale index. 
 
Figure 4.2.1 Initialization Sequence Diagram 
Technical Context: On component mount, the searchStore (Zustand) triggers a 
get_search_readiness command. This ensures the frontend UI state is always synchronized 
with the actual backend capability. 
• 2. Vault Coherence & Self-Healing (Index Maintenance) 
To maintain the Markdown vault as the source of truth, the backend performs a coherence 
check. If the files on disk have changed (drift detected), the system triggers an internal 
rebuild. 

===== PAGE 134 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
134 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
 
Figure 4.2.2 Index Maintenance Sequence Diagram 
Technical Context: The compute_markdown_coherence function acts as a guard. By 
offloading this check to the Rust backend, we keep the UI responsive while ensuring data 
integrity. If a drift is detected, the rebuild_search_index_internal task runs in the 
background. 
• 3. The Search Request Pipeline 
Once the index is "Ready," the search execution follows a high -performance, non-blocking 
path. To prevent blocking the UI thread during heavy work, the system utilizes 
tauri::async_runtime::spawn_blocking to offload Tantivy lookups to a dedicated thread 
pool. 
 
Figure 4.2.3 Search Execution Sequence Diagram 
Technical Context: This diagram illustrates the full round-trip of a search query: 

===== PAGE 135 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 135 
 
• Debouncing: Queries are throttled at 200ms in the React layer. 
• Thread Offloading: The spawn_blocking task ensures the Tantivy index lookup 
doesn't freeze the IPC bridge. 
• Post-Processing: The Snippet Reader performs targeted I/O after results are ranked, 
ensuring we only read what is necessary for the current view. 
 
• Reactive Data Pipeline: Local-First Synchronization 
In a local-first system, data may change inside or outside the app. Tessellum uses a reactive 
convergence pipeline. When the backend watcher (based on the notify crate) detects a 
filesystem event, it emits a file -changed event. The frontend receives this a nd schedules a 
sync_vault invocation. 
The indexer scans the vault, compares filesystem modification times against the SQLite 
cache, and updates only the modified files. This design ensures Fault Tolerance : if the 
derived database becomes corrupted or out of sync, the system can rebuild the entire 
projection from the Markdown files without data loss. 
===== PAGE 136 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
136 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
 
Figure 4.2.4 Synchronization Pipeline Activity Diagram 

===== PAGE 137 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 137 
 
• SQLite as Metadata Cache 
Inside this epic, SQLite acts as a central metadata cache. The schema includes tables for 
notes (metadata), links (resolved relationships), and note_tags (normalized tags). This 
allows for millisecond -latency queries for backlinks and orphan detection that  would be 
impossible if the system had to parse raw files on every request. 
 
Figure 4.2.5 Metadata ER Diagram 
Epic II: Core Editor and Knowledge Management 
• Purpose of the Epic 
This epic transforms plain Markdown files into navigable knowledge objects. It handles the 
authoring, interpretation, and connection of notes. 
• Bi-Directional Linking 
Bi-directional linking is derived from resolved outgoing links and queried in reverse through 
SQLite. When a note is saved, the backend parses the body for Wiki -links, resolves them to 
canonical paths, and stores the relationship. Backlinks are then comput ed dynamically by 
querying the links table for any records where the current note is the target_path. 
• Knowledge Flow During a Note Write 
1. Frontend sends a write_file request. 
2. Backend persists Markdown to disk. 
3. Backend extracts Frontmatter and Tags. 
4. Links are resolved against the current file index. 

===== PAGE 138 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
138 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
5. SQLite metadata is updated, and the Tantivy search index is refreshed through a 
coordinated but non-transactional follow-up step. 
Epic III: Discovery and Visualization 
• Purpose of the Epic 
The third epic is responsible for projecting stored knowledge into navigable surfaces, 
specifically the search engine and the Knowledge Graph. 
• Knowledge Graph Projection 
The graph subsystem is built dynamically from the relational metadata. The command 
get_graph_data queries SQLite for all indexed notes and links, constructing a JSON object of 
nodes and edges. 
• Nodes: Include flags for exists, orphan, and tags. 
• Edges: Identify broken links (links pointing to non-existent files). 
This projection is rendered on the frontend using Cytoscape.js. By separating graph-data 
assembly in Rust from graph rendering in React, the architecture keeps projection logic and 
visualization concerns decoupled.
 

===== PAGE 139 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 139 
 
Figure 4.2.6 Graph Visualization Data Flow Diagram 
• Grafeo Query Layer 
In addition to the visual graph, a specialized graph database (Grafeo) provides a native query 
model for advanced discovery. This allows the user to perform complex queries (e.g., "Find 
all notes linked to 'Project X' that also have the tag '#todo'") that go beyond simple visual 
exploration. 
 
4.2.2.2 Class and Package Design 
This section presents the static design view of Tessellum: the packages, classes, implementation 
modules, and structural relationships that define the internal organization of the system. Its 
purpose is to translate the architectural and behavioral results  from the previous sections into 
a concrete implementation -oriented structure, making explicit the main software elements, 
their responsibilities, and the relationships between them. 
One methodological consideration shapes how this section must be read. The implementation 
combines multiple technologies and paradigms. The frontend is built with React and TypeScript, 
relying on functional components, Zustand state stores, and runtime ser vice classes. The 
backend is built in Rust through Tauri and is organized around command modules, shared-state 
structs, indexing services, persistence services, and support models. The design model therefore 
cannot be limited to traditional object-oriented classes. It must include all implementation units 
that play a stable structural role, whether they appear in source code as state stores, service 
facades, backend structs, or command modules. 
The diagrams in this subsection represent both classical classes and the technical structures 
essential to the implementation: frontend orchestration classes such as TessellumApp, plugin 
lifecycle classes such as Plugin and PluginRegistry, API facade classes such as EditorAPI, VaultAPI, 
WorkspaceAPI, CommandAPI, UIAPI, and I18nAPI, backend shared -state structs such as 
AppState, persistence and indexing services such as Database, SearchIndex, and VaultIndexer, 
and support models such as FileMetadata, WikiLin k, SearchDoc, GraphNode, GraphEdge, and 
GraphData. 
The classes and packages identified here are a direct evolution of the analysis and architecture 
stages. Their methods, attributes, and relationships derive from the interaction flows, 
synchronization logic, search pipeline, metadata schema, and graph visu alization engine 
described earlier. They are not arbitrary implementation artifacts but the structural realization 
of decisions already introduced in the document. 
At the highest level, Tessellum divides into two implementation domains. The frontend domain, 
in src/, handles interaction, rendering, editor behavior, graph visualization, runtime 
extensibility, and application state coordination. The backend domain, in src-tauri/src/, handles 
filesystem monitoring, persistence, synchronization, indexing, graph projection, and the IPC 
boundary exposed through Tauri commands.

Figure 4.2.7 Simplified Class Diagram 
On the frontend, the most consequential structural decision is the separation between 
presentation components, state stores, plugin infrastructure, and application service facades. 
Presentation logic is concentrated in the components package, through units such as App, 
Editor, Sidebar, SearchPanel, GraphView, GraphCanvas, CommandPalette, SettingsModal, 
StatusBar, and RightSidebar. These components handle rendering and user interaction but own 
no persistence, indexing, or synchronization behavior. 
State coordination lives in the stores package, which contains the Zustand stores that persist 
and expose global application state: vaultStore, searchStore, graphStore, uiStore, settingsStore, 
themeStore, appearanceStore, accessibilityStore, selectionStore , pluginsStore, 
navigationHistoryStore, editorModeStore, and editorContentStore. Although these are not 
classical classes, they act as stable state-holder modules and must be represented as such in the 
design. Among them, vaultStore owns vault path, file c ollections, active note state, and open 
workspace tabs; searchStore governs readiness state and search warm-up behavior; graphStore 
coordinates view mode and graph node selection. 

===== PAGE 141 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 141 
 
The extensibility mechanism is concentrated in the plugins package. At its center is 
TessellumApp, the main frontend runtime container, which aggregates EventBus, 
PluginRegistry, EditorAPI, VaultAPI, WorkspaceAPI, CommandAPI, UIAPI, and I18nAPI. It is the 
root aggregation class of the frontend runtime, centralizing plugin access to editor behavior, 
workspace state, command registration, UI contributions, event publication, and translation 
services. 
The Plugin abstract class defines the lifecycle contract for all plugins through the abstract 
method onload(), the optional onunload() hook, and convenience methods for registering editor 
extensions, commands, translations, and event subscriptions. PluginR egistry manages plugin 
registration, instantiation, loading, unloading, enabling, disabling, and failure isolation. It 
composes plugin instances and depends on TessellumApp, since each plugin requires a 
reference to the frontend runtime before participating in the system. 
The built-in plugin hierarchy extends Plugin through classes including MarkdownPreviewPlugin, 
DividerPlugin, MathPlugin, InlineCodePlugin, CalloutPlugin, TablePlugin, WikiLinkPlugin, 
CoreCommandsPlugin, CodePlugin, MermaidPlugin, FrontmatterPlugin, InlineT agsPlugin, 
DailyNotesPlugin, CoreUIActionsPlugin, MediaEmbedPlugin, MediaPastePlugin, and 
TaskListPlugin. These inject editor extensions, commands, UI actions, and translations into the 
running application. The inheritance relationship appears explicitly in the class diagram. 
The API facade classes define the boundary between plugins and the rest of the application. 
EditorAPI manages CodeMirror extension registration and editor reconfiguration. VaultAPI 
wraps Tauri vault operations. WorkspaceAPI coordinates vault selection, active note state, view 
mode, and navigation history. CommandAPI stores and dispatches slash commands. UIAPI stores 
sidebar actions, palette commands, and settings tabs. I18nAPI exposes locale and translation 
services through the underlying I18nService. These  classes decouple plugins from internal 
implementation details and provide a controlled collaboration interface.

The backend follows a different but equally deliberate structure. The entry point is src -
tauri/src/lib.rs, where application state is initialized and Tauri command handlers are registered. 
The central shared struct is AppState, in models/app_state.rs, whic h groups the long -lived 
technical resources used across the command layer: the filesystem watcher, the SQLite 
Database, the in -memory FileIndex, the in -memory AssetIndex, the Tantivy SearchIndex, and 
the mutable SearchReadinessState. 
Database, defined in db.rs, is the main persistence service for the relational metadata layer. It 
encapsulates the SQL connection pool and exposes operations for schema initialization, note 
indexing, tag normalization, link storage, backlink and outgoing -link retrieval, orphan and 
broken-link detection, and synchronization bookkeeping through the search_files table. It has 
structural relationships with indexing services, graph projection logic, and multiple command 
modules. 
SearchIndex, in search.rs, manages full -text indexing and retrieval through Tantivy. It 
encapsulates a Tantivy Index, an IndexReader, a SearchFields descriptor, and the on -disk index 
directory. Its operations include opening or creating the index, clearing  it, indexing document 
batches, deleting paths, executing ranked searches, and listing indexed paths. SearchDoc is the 
associated document model, containing path, title, body, and tags. SearchFields stores the field 
definitions of the search schema. In the  class diagram, this subsystem is represented as a 
composition centered on SearchIndex, with SearchFields and SearchDoc as associated support 
models. 
VaultIndexer, in indexer.rs, coordinates synchronization between the vault filesystem, SQLite, 
and Tantivy. Its full_sync operation scans the vault, compares the current filesystem state with 
the search_files manifest, detects new, modified, and deleted files, updates relational metadata, 
builds SearchDoc values, and applies changes to the Tantivy index. The result is represented by 
IndexStats, which records the number of indexed, deleted, and skipped files and the execution 
duration. VaultIndexer depends on Database, SearchIndex, and FileIndex. 
FileIndex, in models/file_index.rs, maps note names to vault paths and resolves wikilinks to 
canonical Markdown files. AssetIndex, in models/asset_index.rs, plays the equivalent role for 
images, PDFs, and other media assets. Both are cached in AppState and invalidated by watcher 
and synchronization events. They are essential to the indexing, note-writing, media-embedding, 
and link-resolution pipelines. 
The Grafeo projection module, in grafeo_projection.rs, synchronizes a graph -native database 
alongside the SQLite and Tantivy layers. It enables complex relational queries that go beyond 
what the flat SQLite schema supports efficiently, such as multi -hop li nk traversal and tag -
conditioned graph filtering. The graph command module depends on both Database and 
grafeo_projection, using the former for standard relational retrieval and the latter for graph -
native query execution. 
The main support models include FileMetadata, which describes files and directories exposed 
to the frontend; WikiLink, which stores parsed link targets and aliases; GraphNode, GraphEdge, 
and GraphData, which define the graph projection returned to the fron tend; and the search 
request and response models TagFilter, FullTextSearchRequest, TagSearchRequest, SearchHit, 
===== PAGE 145 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 145 
 
FullTextSearchResponse, TagSearchResponse, IndexRebuildResult, and 
SearchReadinessResponse. These types define the data contracts used internally and across the 
IPC boundary.

4.2.2.3 User Interface Design 
This section provides a detailed technical specification of Tessellum's definitive user interface, 
defining the exact structural components, operational logic, and state integrations that form the 
production application. It establishes the concrete impleme ntation details that transition the 
abstract spatial layouts from the analysis phase (Figure 4.2.1 and Figure 4.2.2) into reactive 
software modules. Specifically, this documentation describes the layout boundaries, component 
hierarchies, keyboard -driven in teraction patterns, and the synchronous feedback loops 
between the React frontend and the Tauri/Rust IPC subsystem. 
4.2.2.3.1 Main interface design 
The primary interface implements a structured three-column layout bound vertically by a global 
Title Bar at the top and a system Status Bar at the bottom. 
 
Figure 4.2.24 Final UI Design 
1. Application Title Bar (Top Header) 
• Structure: A persistent horizontal bar mapped to the top boundary of the window, 
utilizing Tauri window decorations. 
• Function: Integrates workspace layout controls, specifically toggles to programmatically 
modify the visibility state of the left and right sidebars. It contains the workspace root 
directory (Vault) selector, which updates the global state upon selection changes. 

===== PAGE 153 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 153 
 
2. Primary Management Sidebar (Left Panel) 
• Structure: A collapsible vertical column located on the left axis of the application. 
• Function: Consolidates two core sub-components: 
o SearchPanel: Contains the full-text search input field. It captures user text input, 
applies a 200ms debounce within the SearchPanel component's render cycle, 
then triggers the search_full_text Tauri IPC command. It handles the rendering 
of results returned as a FullTextSearchResponse, rendering text snippets 
generated by the Rust backend's Tantivy search engine. 
o File Tree Explorer: Renders the local file system hierarchy as a recursive React 
component tree, with lazy expansion of directory nodes to manage DOM 
footprint. 
3. Central Workspace (Main Editor) 
• Structure: The central display area, prioritized to maximize vertical and horizontal text 
boundaries. 
• Function: Houses the Markdown editor. It executes the per -line rendering model, 
isolating DOM updates strictly to the active text line receiving cursor focus. Syntax 
highlighting operations (Markdown and LaTeX tokens) are processed on a separate 
execution layer to prevent input latency on the main UI thread. 
4. Supplemental Context Sidebar (Right Panel) 
• Structure: A collapsible vertical column located on the right axis of the application. 
• Function: Provides document metadata and relational data in vertically stacked, 
scrollable sections: 
o Backlinks Viewer:  Queries and displays a list of incoming references to the 
active document. 
o Tags Section: Shows the tags associated with the active document. 
o Document Outline: A structured tree generated dynamically from Markdown 
header tokens (H1–H6), allowing internal document navigation via click events. 
o Local Graph View:  A Canvas -based component rendering the immediate 
relational neighbors of the active node. It uses the CoSE (Compound Spring 
Embedder) force-directed layout algorithm provided by Cytoscape.js, rendered 
on an HTML5 Canvas 2D context.  The Local Graph is rendered independently 
from the Sidebar, as an independent component. 
5. System Status Bar (Bottom Footer) 
• Structure: A persistent horizontal bar fixed to the bottom edge of the application 
window. 
===== PAGE 154 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
154 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Function: Monitors and displays document -level metadata in real time: file encoding, 
file type, word count, estimated read time, and save state (dirty/saved). 
4.2.2.3.2 Settings interface design 
 
 
Figure 4.2.25 Final Settings UI Design 
The system configuration environment is implemented as a centralized modal overlay that 
supersedes the primary workspace when invoked, adhering to the Master-Detail design pattern 
specified in the analysis phase. 
1. Category Navigation (Left Pane) 
• Structure: A fixed vertical list on the left side of the modal container. 
• Function: Functions as the primary controller for configuration routing. Selecting an 
option updates the active category state, which shifts the context of the adjacent detail 
panel. The defined categories are: 
o General: Configures startup parameters and core system paths. 
o Editor: Manages line -wrapping rules, font families, and Markdown parsing 
parameters. 
o Appearance: Controls the system theme engine, injecting global CSS variables 
to switch between high-contrast and low-luminosity profiles. 

===== PAGE 155 =====

Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 155 
 
o Shortcuts: Registers keyboard event listeners to map custom key combinations 
to application commands. 
o Accessibility: Controls scaling factors and screen-reader compatibility tags. 
o Plugins: Interfaces with the Plugin API to enable, disable, or configure external 
extensions. 
2. Active Configuration Area (Right Pane) 
• Structure: A dynamic scrollable content pane positioned to the right of the navigation 
menu. 
• Function: Displays the individual configuration controls (input fields, sliders, and 
toggles) corresponding to the selected category. Input mutations trigger immediate, 
synchronous writes to the browser's  localStorage key-value store managed by the 
WebView engine, eliminating the need for a manual confirmation or 'Apply' step. 
3. Modal Control and Layout Integrity 
• Structure: A bounded container overlay with a persistent close trigger in the top -right 
corner. 
• Function: The modal layer intercepts all keyboard focus when active. Dismissing the 
modal destroys its transient layout state and returns keyboard and cursor focus 
immediately to the line buffer of the Central Workspace Editor. 
 
4.2.2.4 Security Design 
 
Because Tessellum operates as a local -first desktop application, its security model focuses on 
local data safety and process isolation rather than cloud perimeter defense. The design 
addresses three areas: restricting filesystem access to the user's design ated vault, eliminating 
network exposure, and maintaining the integrity of derived data stores under adverse runtime 
conditions. Each area is documented below with reference to the specific implementation 
mechanisms present in the codebase. 
4.2.2.4.1 Vault Access Control and Filesystem Permissions 
1. Operating System-Level Access Control 
Tessellum does not implement an internal authentication or authorization layer. All vault files—
including Markdown documents, embedded assets, and application metadata —are stored as 
standard files on the host filesystem and inherit the access -control semantics of the operating 
system. 
• Windows: NTFS access control lists (ACLs) assigned to the user profile that owns the 
vault directory govern read and write permissions. 
===== PAGE 156 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
156 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• macOS / Linux: Standard POSIX file modes apply analogously. 
Because the application runs as an unprivileged, user -space process, it can only access files for 
which the operating system grants the current user permission. No elevation of privilege is 
requested during execution. 
2. Tauri Filesystem Scoping 
The Tauri v2 runtime enforces filesystem restrictions independent of the operating system. The 
capability manifest (src-tauri/capabilities/default.json) declares the specific permissions granted 
to the frontend WebView: 
Permission Purpose 
fs:default Base filesystem operations scoped to allowed paths. 
fs:allow-exists Allows checking file existence without granting file-read privileges. 
core:path:default Resolves standard system platform directories. 
core:window:allow-* Grants window management capabilities (minimize, maximize, close, 
drag, resize). 
core:event:default Restricts internal event bus communication to validated system 
loops. 
dialog:default Invokes native OS file/folder selection dialogs. 
opener:default Opens files using the host system's default application handler. 
window-
state:default 
Persists and restores window geometry between application 
instances. 
TABLE 4.2.1 TAURI PERMISSIONS 
The tauri -plugin-persisted-scope plugin, declared in the Cargo dependency manifest 
(Cargo.toml), ensures that filesystem scope grants selected by the user at runtime via the native 
vault selection dialog are persisted across application restarts. The asset  protocol scope is 
configured in tauri.conf.json with a glob pattern ("") limited to files within previously granted 
scope boundaries. This configuration restricts the WebView process from accessing arbitrary 
filesystem locations if a vulnerability in the frontend code occurs. 
3. Data at Rest 
Vault contents are stored as plain-text Markdown files on disk to ensure user data sovereignty, 
interoperability, and portability. 
The derived metadata database (SQLite) and the full -text search index (Tantivy) are stored 
unencrypted in the application's local data directory (%LOCALAPPDATA%/tessellum/ on 
Windows, or the platform equivalents on macOS and Linux). No encryption -at-rest mechanism 
(such as SQLCipher or age) is implemented. Users requiring encryption at rest must employ 
===== PAGE 157 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 157 
 
volume-level encryption provided by the operating system (e.g., BitLocker on Windows, 
FileVault on macOS, or LUKS on Linux). 
 
4.2.2.4.2 Network Exposure and Isolation 
1. Zero Network Policy 
The application requires no inbound or outbound network connections to perform its functions. 
The Rust dependency manifest (Cargo.toml) contains no HTTP client libraries (such as reqwest 
or hyper) and no network socket dependencies. 
All data processing—indexing, full-text search, graph projection, and file mutations —executes 
entirely on the local machine. The application contains no telemetry, analytics, crash reporting, 
or automated update-checking mechanisms that transmit data to external servers. This network 
isolation eliminates attack vectors such as remote data exfiltration, man -in-the-middle 
interception, and remote code execution via network services. 
2. Tauri IPC Security 
Communication between the frontend WebView and the Rust backend occurs exclusively 
through Tauri's Inter -Process Communication (IPC) bridge. The frontend invokes backend 
functions via the invoke() API. Each callable function must be explicitly registered w ithin the 
invoke_handler macro declaration inside the main application entry module (src -
tauri/src/lib.rs). Any #[tauri::command] function not listed in this handler is unreachable from 
the frontend interface. 
Each command function receives its arguments as strongly -typed Rust structures deserialized 
via serde. Payloads that fail validation are discarded at the deserialization boundary before 
business logic executes. State access is mediated through Tauri's mana ged state system 
(State<'_, AppState>), providing controlled access to shared resources such as the database 
connection pool and the search index. All database -modifying operations use parameterized 
queries via sqlx to prevent SQL injection. 
3. Content Security Policy 
A Content Security Policy (CSP) is enforced on the WebView via the core application 
configuration file (tauri.conf.json). The policy is structured as follows: 
Directive Value Effect 
default-
src 
'self' Blocks all resource loading except 
from within the local application 
bundle. 
script-src 'self' Permits only scripts bundled with 
the application; blocks inline 
scripts and external script sources.

Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
158 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo

stylesheets for dynamic runtime 
theming components.

the bundle, data URIs, blob URIs, 
and the Tauri local asset protocol.

schemes as images.

(Flash, Java applets, embedded

and inline data URIs.

[http://ipc.localhost](http://ipc.localhost)

the Tauri IPC channel and local 
host endpoints. 
TABLE 4.2.2 CSP POLICY 
The connect-src directive provides a defense-in-depth mechanism: by restricting connections to 
the ipc: scheme and the local IPC endpoint ([http://ipc.localhost](http://ipc.localhost)), the 
browser engine blocks unauthorized outbound network traffic. Even if a third -party library 
loaded inside the WebView attempts to initiate an outbound HTTP request to an external server, 
the browser engine drops the request at the CSP enforcement layer. 
 
4.2.2.4.3 Index Integrity Guarantees 
1. SQLite Corruption Prevention 
The metadata database is initialized with durability and concurrency safeguards inside the core 
database initialization module (src-tauri/src/db.rs): 
• Write-Ahead Logging (WAL):  The database is opened via 
journal_mode(SqliteJournalMode::Wal), enabling concurrent readers during write 
operations and providing crash -safe transaction semantics. Under WAL mode, 
committed transactions persist if the application terminates abruptly or t he system 
experiences a power loss, as writes are appended to a log file before being checkpointed 
into the main database file. 
• Busy Timeout: A busy_timeout of 15 seconds is configured to handle write contention. 
If a write lock cannot be acquired immediately, the operation retries automatically for 
up to 15 seconds before returning an error. 
===== PAGE 159 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 159 
 
• Connection Pooling:  The SqlitePoolOptions limits the pool to a maximum of 5 
concurrent connections to bound local system resource usage and prevent file 
descriptor exhaustion. 
• Transactional Writes: Multi-step write operations (such as link updates, file renames, 
batch deletions, and tag replacements) are enclosed in explicit SQLite transactions 
(pool.begin() / tx.commit()). If a step within a transaction fails, the entire operation rolls 
back atomically to prevent partial updates. Additionally, PRAGMA defer_foreign_keys = 
ON is used during rename operations to ensure primary key updates and dependent 
foreign key references are committed as a single atomic unit. 
• Foreign Key Enforcement:  PRAGMA foreign_keys = ON is enabled upon connection 
establishment, ensuring that referential integrity constraints (such as cascading deletes 
from notes to links and tags) are enforced by the database engine. 
2. Tantivy Search Index Integrity 
The Tantivy full -text search index employs a commit -then-reload consistency protocol 
implemented within the search indexing module (src-tauri/src/search.rs): 
1. A mutable IndexWriter is obtained with a 50 MB memory budget. 
2. Documents are added or deleted within the writer's in-memory buffer. 
3. writer.commit() flushes the buffer to disk as an immutable segment, using Tantivy's 
internal segment merge and fsync mechanisms to ensure durability. 
4. reader.reload() refreshes the searcher to incorporate the newly committed segment. 
If the process terminates between steps 2 and 3, the uncommitted in -memory changes are 
discarded, and the index remains in its last known consistent state. This append -only segment 
architecture prevents partial writes from corrupting the index state. 
3. Coherence Verification and Automatic Repair 
The application implements a startup coherence verification protocol within the search 
commands module (src -tauri/src/commands/search.rs) to detect structural divergence 
between the SQLite metadata catalog and the Tantivy search index. The algorithm operat es as 
follows: 
• Enumeration: The set of expected Markdown file paths is read from the search_files 
table in SQLite. The set of indexed paths is read concurrently from the Tantivy index via 
a full collection query. 
• Mismatch Computation: A symmetric difference is computed between the two sets 
using an early -exit counter (count_mismatches_with_early_exit). The algorithm 
terminates as soon as the mismatch count reaches the configured threshold, avoiding a 
full comparison for large vaults where incoherence is detected early. 
• Threshold Evaluation:  The mismatch threshold is defined as 1% of the expected 
Markdown file count, with a floor of 1 (mismatch_threshold). If the number of 
===== PAGE 160 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
160 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
mismatches meets or exceeds this threshold, the evaluation function (needs_rebuild) 
returns true. 
• Automatic Rebuild: When incoherence is detected, the ensure_search_ready command 
triggers rebuild_search_index_internal. This routine clears the Tantivy index, re -walks 
the vault directory, and re-indexes all files from their source content on disk. This self -
healing mechan ism ensures index corruption caused by an application crash, an 
incomplete indexing pass, or external filesystem modifications is resolved without user 
intervention. 
• State Machine: The readiness subsystem enforces a bounded retry policy (maximum of 
10 attempts with a 5-second delay between retries) to prevent infinite repair loops if a 
persistent failure condition exists. The state transitions through Idle → Warming → 
Ready on succe ss, or Idle → Warming → Failed if all attempts are exhausted. The 
frontend queries this state via get_search_readiness and can reset the attempt counter 
via reset_search_readiness_attempts if the user triggers a vault reload. 
4. Startup Write Probe 
As an operational safeguard, the application performs a filesystem write probe during 
initialization (src-tauri/src/lib.rs). A temporary hidden file (.startup -write-probe) is created and 
deleted within the local application data directory. If this probe fa ils due to insufficient OS 
permissions, a read -only filesystem lock, or disk corruption, the application halts with a 
diagnostic error to prevent operations in a degraded state where data loss could occur. 
 
4.2.2.5 Build and Deployment Design 
 
This section documents the compilation toolchain, continuous integration (CI) infrastructure, 
target platform matrix, and distribution formats for Tessellum. The objective is to demonstrate 
that the software can be reproduced from source, packaged into platform-native installers, and 
distributed to end users in a verifiable, controlled manner. Technical statements are mapped 
directly to the project's configuration manifests and automated workflows. 
4.2.2.5.1 Build Process and Toolchain 
1. Prerequisites and Environment 
The build process requires two independent toolchains operating in sequence: 
Component Toolchain /
