On Linux distributions, compilation additionally requires system -level native libraries for 
GTK 3, WebKitGTK 4.1, libsoup 3.0, and librsvg2, as well as the patchelf utility for ELF binary 
patching. These dependencies are provisioned automatically in the CI runner via the system 
package manager during the workflow initialization phase. 
2. Dual-Stage Compilation Pipeline 
The compilation is a sequential two -stage process orchestrated by the Tauri CLI. The 
beforeBuildCommand directive in src -tauri/tauri.conf.json ensures that the frontend 
compilation completes successfully before the Rust backend compilation begins. 
3. Stage 1: Frontend Asset Compilation 
The compilation command npm run build executes two operations in sequence: 
4. Type Checking:  The TypeScript compiler (tsc) validates the source tree against the 
criteria defined in tsconfig.json (targeting ES2020, strict mode, and native JSX 
execution). 
5. Bundling: Vite processes the application entry point (index.html → src/main.tsx) 
through the following transformation pipeline: 
o The @vitejs/plugin -react plugin transpiles React JSX and TypeScript into 
ECMAScript-compliant JavaScript. 
o PostCSS processes styles through the @tailwindcss/postcss plugin (Tailwind CSS 
v4) and autoprefixer to generate vendor-prefixed CSS assets. 
o Vite executes tree -shaking, code-splitting, and minification routines, emitting 
the static assets into the root dist/ directory. 
A separate CI build command (npm run build:ci) skips the tsc type-checking step to optimize 
pipeline execution times. This override is managed via src -tauri/tauri.ci.conf.json, which 
substitutes the default compilation directive with the CI-specific routine. 
6. Stage 2: Native Binary Compilation 
Once assets are written to the dist/ directory, the Tauri CLI executes cargo build --release 
inside the src -tauri/ workspace. The tauri_build::build() script in build.rs runs during this 
===== PAGE 162 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
162 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
phase to generate platform -specific resource bindings. The Rust compiler completes the 
following steps: 
1. Compiles the application core library (tessellum_lib) as structured in Cargo.toml. 
2. Links the compiled binary with the host operating system's native WebView runtime 
(WebView2 on Windows, WebKitGTK on Linux, WKWebView on macOS). 
3. Embeds the contents of the static asset directory (defined via frontendDist in 
tauri.conf.json) into the compiled binary as static memory structures. 
4. Outputs a single native executable containing the application logic and the 
embedded user interface. 
The resulting executable is then automatically routed to Tauri’s internal bundler to generate 
target installers. 
 
4.2.2.5.2 CI/CD Automation 
The project utilizes GitHub Actions workflows to manage automated compilation testing and 
release distribution. 
1. Continuous Integration Workflow 
The tauri-ci.yml workflow executes on all pull requests and pushes directed to the primary 
branch. It compiles the application concurrently across a three-platform execution matrix: 
Runner Environment Target Operating System Architecture 
windows-latest Windows Server x86_64 
macos-latest macOS ARM64 (Apple Silicon) 
ubuntu-24.04 Ubuntu Linux x86_64 
TABLE 4.2.4 CI ENVIRONMENTS 
A independent execution strategy (fail-fast: false) is configured so that a compilation failure 
on one architecture does not interrupt the jobs running on the remaining platforms. This 
provides full diagnostic coverage across the matrix. 
Each runner job implements the following discrete tasks: 
1. Source Checkout: Retrieves the repository state using actions/checkout. 
2. Node.js Environment Selection:  Installs Node.js 20 and initializes local package 
caching. 
3. Rust Environment Selection: Installs the current stable Rust toolchain. 
===== PAGE 163 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 163 
 
4. Compilation Caching:  Restores historical Cargo build targets via swatinem/rust -
cache to reduce iteration times. 
5. System Dependencies:  Installs required Linux native libraries (GTK and WebKit 
components) on the Ubuntu runner. 
6. Package Installation: Performs a deterministic dependency installation using npm 
ci. 
7. Compilation: Executes npm run tauri build pointing to the CI configuration profile. 
8. Artifact Staging:  Uploads the generated native bundles into secure workflow 
storage. 
2. Release Workflow 
The tauri -release.yml workflow initializes upon the detection of a semantic version tag 
(matching the pattern v*.*.*) or via a manual administrative trigger. The workflow runs two 
sequential processes: 
1. Compilation Job: Implements the same matrix build logic defined in the CI workflow 
to construct release-ready bundles across all target environments. 
2. Publication Job:  Consolidates the generated build targets and generates a draft 
GitHub Release using softprops/action-gh-release. The release is held in draft state 
to permit manual validation of assets before public exposure. The workflow 
attaches the installer assets matching the platform glob patterns: 
o *.exe, *.msi (Windows targets) 
o *.dmg, *.app.tar.gz (macOS targets) 
o *.deb, *.rpm, *.AppImage (Linux targets)

3. Code Signing and Notarization 
Cryptographic code signing and system notarization pipelines are not currently active in the 
build framework. The automation workflows emit unsigned binaries. Consequently, the 
following execution rules apply: 
• Windows: The execution of the installer may trigger a Microsoft Defender 
SmartScreen warning until a positive reputation baseline is established by user 
download counts. 
===== PAGE 165 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 165 
 
• macOS: Gatekeeper security features will block direct application execution due to 
the lack of an Apple Developer ID signature. Users must create an explicit security 
exception inside system preferences to permit execution. 
• Linux: Package managers do not enforce cryptographic signing for direct execution 
of local .AppImage files, though .deb and .rpm workflows would require GPG keys if 
transition to public repository hosting is pursued. 
The integration of signing mechanisms (Microsoft Authenticode and Apple Developer ID 
Notarization) is planned for a future phase. It will utilize GitHub encrypted organization 
secrets to inject signing credentials into the release workflows without exposin g raw 
certificates. 
4. Update Distribution 
The application does not include an automated self -updater subsystem. The tauri -plugin-
updater dependency is omitted from Cargo.toml, and no remote polling endpoints are 
declared in tauri.conf.json. 
All software updates are delivered exclusively via manual user acquisition from the official 
project repository releases registry. This structural isolation supports the application's zero-
network operational mandate: because the client engine performs no background network 
transactions during regular operation, it remains unable to poll for, download, or execute 
remote binary updates. 
 
4.2.2.6 Technical Specification of the Testing plan 
The software testing process is a standard engineering discipline integrated across the system 
construction lifecycle. In the development of Tessellum, testing functions as a continuous 
verification activity embedded within each phase of development, incor porating unit 
verification for core utility models and backend schemas, component -driven testing for user 
interface states, and automated regression integration gates. 
This specification defines the designed test cases and introduces the verification methodologies 
(specifically Usability and Performance testing) required to validate compliance with functional 
requirements, performance limits, and user interface specifications. 
4.2.2.6.1 Testbed Environment  
To guarantee the consistency and reproducibility of all test executions, the automated and 
manual testing processes are conducted under a standardized host configuration: 
• Operating System:  Microsoft Windows 11 Professional (64 -bit, Version 22H2 / Build 
22621 or higher). 
• Processor (CPU): Intel Core i7 (10th Generation or higher) or AMD Ryzen 7 (4000 series 
or higher). 
• Memory (RAM): 16 GB DDR4/DDR5 or higher. 
===== PAGE 166 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
166 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Storage: Solid State Drive (SSD) with a minimum of 10 GB of available disk space. 
• Development Environment and Toolchain: 
o Integrated Development Environment (IDE): Visual Studio Code (Version 1.88 or 
higher). 
o Runtime Environment: Node.js (Version 20 LTS or higher) and npm (Version 10 
or higher). 
o System Compiler:  Rust Compiler and Cargo toolchain (Version 1.75 Stable or 
higher). 
o Desktop Framework: Tauri CLI (Version 1.6 or higher) utilizing Microsoft Edge 
WebView2 as the frontend rendering engine. 
o End-to-End Test Driver: Cypress (Version 13 or higher) running in a standardized 
Chromium-based browser context. 
• Multi-Process / Localhost Architecture Specification 
Tessellum implements a multi -process architecture consisting of independent runtime 
components: a React frontend client running inside a WebView2 rendering window, a Rust 
backend core controller process executing system commands, a local SQLite embedded 
database operating in Write -Ahead Logging (WAL) mode, a Tantivy full -text search engine 
indexer, and a Grafeo graph projection memory cache. 
All automated and manual tests are executed locally on a single host machine. Inter -process 
communication (IPC) between the frontend client and the backend core is performed via the 
native Tauri IPC bridge using isolated local system calls. File system mod ifications, database 
operations, search indexing, and graph cache calculations are restricted entirely to temporary 
directories within the local environment (localhost), eliminating external network dependencies 
and ensuring test isolation. 
• Test Execution Sequence  
Tests are executed in a sequential, hierarchical order within both local development 
environments and the Continuous Integration (CI) pipeline to verify lower -level components 
before testing complex integration workflows: 
Sequence

4.2.2.6.2 Unit Testing  
Unit tests validate the functional correctness of individual software modules in isolation. Each 
test case targets a single class, function, or state store to verify compliance with specifications 
prior to subsystem integration. 
• Subsystem Division and Implementation Details 
The unit testing architecture is divided into two primary subsystems based on the application 
design: 
1. Frontend Subsystem (React / TypeScript): 
o Target Modules: Zustand state stores (settingsStore.ts, editorContentStore.ts), 
interface modals (InputModal.tsx, DeleteConfirmModal.tsx), custom hook 
decision paths (useDeleteFile.ts), and markdown parsing modules 
(markdownShortcuts.ts). 
o Data Inputs: Structured state snapshots, trimmed and untrimmed strings, font 
size boundaries, and text selection coordinates. 
o Execution Framework: Vitest combined with React Testing Library (RTL) within 
a virtual jsdom environment to simulate user interface interactions and state 
transitions in memory without requiring a compiled desktop binary. 
2. Backend Subsystem (Rust / Tauri Core): 
o Target Modules:  Path security filters (validate.rs), trash lifecycle managers 
(trash.rs), search query normalizers (search.rs), and database utilities (db.rs). 
o Data Inputs:  Mock filesystem directories, invalid paths (including parent 
directory traversal tokens), database rows, and search tokens. 
o Execution Framework: cargo test using native Rust test modules isolated via the 
#[cfg(test)] attribute. 
• Triggers, Correction Measures, and Regression Strategy 
• Execution Trigger:  Unit tests are executed locally by developers during code 
modification (via active watching mechanisms) and are automatically triggered in the 
central repository platform upon every commit and Pull Request. 
===== PAGE 168 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
168 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Defect Correction Measures: A unit test failure automatically blocks code integration in 
the CI/CD pipeline. The defect is logged, isolated to the specific module, and corrected 
locally by the developer before re-submitting the code. 
• Regression Testing Strategy: The entire unit test suite is executed automatically upon 
any code change to verify that existing features remain operational. Code coverage tools 
track statement and branch coverage against established quality gates to prevent 
regression. 
 
• Functional Use Case Testing Coverage  
Unit tests directly validate the functional requirements defined in the System Analysis 
documentation. These tests map to the basic, alternative, and error paths of the 14 system use 
cases, isolating the respective components and handlers: 
• CU1: Manage Vault: Verifies that vaultStore initializes correctly, populates file lists from 
the target directory, manages workspace tab switching, and prevents duplicate tab 
references. 
• CU2: Manage Notes:  Validates that note creation requests trim whitespace, handles 
filename collisions according to filesystem rules, and blocks note modifications when 
read-only conditions are active. 
• CU3: Manage Folders: Checks that directory creation requests with duplicate names are 
blocked, and names containing invalid operating system characters are sanitized or 
rejected. 
• CU4: Search Notes: Tests query tokenization, multi-token lookups with tag filters (e.g., 
content:graph #feature), and ensures that concurrent initialization requests are 
coalesced into a single thread. 
• CU5: Manage Trash:  Verifies that trashed items are removed from active navigation 
views, name collisions on restore receive unique indexing suffixes, and the 30 -day 
retention boundary is enforced down to millisecond precision. 
• CU6: Manage Settings: Validates font size clamping between the absolute limits of 12 
and 24 pixels, verifies fallback to the default English locale on invalid language inputs, 
and ensures graceful recovery from corrupted browser storage. 
• CU7: Manage Themes:  Validates custom JSON theme schemas, verifies scheduling 
boundary timers, and checks fallback theme assignment during storage configuration 
errors. 
• CU8: Manage Plugins:  Audits the initialization and teardown lifecycles of the 
PluginRegistry, ensuring plugin runtime errors are isolated and that all UI components 
and commands are unmapped upon disabling. 
===== PAGE 169 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 169 
 
• CU9: Manage the Editor:  Tests markdown formatting shortcuts across multi -line 
selections, verifies slash command (/) context parsing, and checks case-insensitive auto-
complete string filtering. 
• CU10: Validate Paths and Inputs:  Validates security guards by blocking directory 
traversal vectors (such as .. or external system mount paths) inside 
validate_path_in_vault and strips prohibited path characters. 
• CU11: Manage the Knowledge Graph:  Validates wiki-link syntax extraction (including 
aliased and escaped forms), updates backlink indices, and generates placeholder ghost 
nodes for broken target references. 
• CU12: Manage the Internationalisation Service:  Verifies that missing translation keys 
trigger console exceptions during development mode and enforces base translation 
requirements on plugin registrations. 
• CU13: Clipboard Operations:  Audits file -tree copy and paste commands, verifies 
runtime UI error notification triggers when the operating system clipboard is locked, and 
increments filename numerical suffixes on paste conflicts. 
• CU14: Export to PD F: Validates hierarchical outline tree generation from headings, 
blocks exports on non-markdown items, and handles empty destination paths or native 
print driver failures. 
 
4.2.2.6.3 Integration and System Testing  
Integration and System testing verify the interaction between combined subsystems and 
evaluate the compiled application against end -to-end user workflows under production 
conditions. 
• Application and Methodology 
1. Integration Testing: 
o Methodology: Focuses on transactional paths where the React user interface, 
Tauri IPC commands, SQLite database schemas, Tantivy indexing threads, and 
Grafeo graph caches intersect. Tests are implemented via dedicated integration 
modules running against dynamic test vault structures. 
o Inputs & Outputs:  Inputs consist of physical filesystem mutations, database 
transactions, and file modification bursts. Outputs consist of verified database 
states, search index coherence, and updated graph models. 
o Execution Trigger: Automated via the testing toolchain during local validation 
and pre-merge integration checks. 
2. System Testing (E2E): 
o Methodology: Verifies end -to-end user journeys by executing the complete 
frontend and interface flows. Since Tessellum is built as a web -first desktop 
===== PAGE 170 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
170 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
application using Tauri, the E2E suite is implemented using Cypress as the 
primary orchestrator. To facilitate fast and robust automation without OS-level 
desktop window overhead, tests are run under E2E configuration (`cross -env 
VITE_E2E=1`) against the local React web server (running at 
`http://localhost:3000`). Native Tauri interfaces (such as filesystem access, file 
dialogs, and native commands) are mocked dynamically at the boundary via 
custom Cypress commands, simulating complete frontend -backend syst em 
integration. 
o Inputs & Outputs: Inputs are simulated user interactions (clicks, drag -and-drop 
actions, editor content entries, settings adjustments) and mock vault file 
structures loaded via `cy.openVault`. Outputs are verified UI updates, correct 
state changes in Zustand stores, valid M arkdown rendering, and Cytoscape 
graph projections. 
o Execution Trigger: Triggered via `npm run e2e` automatically on every commit 
in the CI/CD pipeline and available interactively via `npm run e2e:open` for 
developer testing. 
• Outcomes, Error Handling, and Regression Protection 
• Successful Outcome: ypress validates DOM assertions, component configurations, and 
mock IPC actions. The suite completes successfully, generating automated execution 
summaries. 
• Failing Outcome: In case of assertion failure, Cypress automatically captures: 
1. A full high-resolution screenshot at the exact millisecond of failure. 
2. A detailed execution log including command history, stub outputs, and console 
warning states. 
3. Video recordings of the test execution (when configured) to assist visual 
debugging. 
•   A developer reviews the Cypress dashboard logs, reproduces the failure locally by 
opening the interactive test runner (`npm run e2e:open`), corrects the underlying 
defect, and re-runs the spec to guarantee regression clearance. 
 
• Integration Use Case Testing Coverage  
The integration suite verifies that independent subsystems function together correctly. Tests 
map directly to the 7 core transactional pipelines defined in the system architecture: 
• CU1: Manage Vault (Vault Watcher & Sync Pipeline):  Verifies that file modifications, 
deletions, and external creation bursts are detected by the recursive watcher and 
synchronized sequentially with the database and search indices. 
• CU2: Manage Notes (Save & Metadata Pipeline):  Validates the complete note 
persistence path: saving an active note writes to disk, updates SQLite records, extracts 
tags, updates outgoing links, and modifies the search index document. 
===== PAGE 171 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 171 
 
• CU3: Manage Trash (Trash -and-Restore Lifecycle):  Coordinates file deletions, trash 
directory movements, and filename conflict index modifications across both the 
frontend store and the host filesystem. 
• CU4: Search Notes (Search Readiness & Full -Text Search):  Verifies search pipeline 
stability during cold application boots, validating that search queries return accurate 
matches and exclude deleted paths. 
• CU5: Visualise the Knowledge Graph (Graph Projection Pipeline):  Validates that the 
graph data layer processes note modifications accurately, merges duplicate link 
definitions, and updates backlink counts. 
• CU6: Manage Settings (Appearance & Spellcheck Propagation):  Verifies that changes 
to user configurations are propagated immediately as DOM CSS variables and element 
attribute updates across all active view panels. 
• CU7: Export to PDF (Frontend -Backend Export Flow):  Validates that active interface 
themes compile to valid print stylesheets, layout trees are parsed, and the resulting 
HTML payload is exported into a PDF file via the backend print engine. 
 
• System Use Case Testing Coverage  
System testing (E2E) validates the absolute interface coherence and overall operational 
flow of Tessellum under mock user environments. The automated Cypress test suite is 
organized into **3 specialized testing specs** which exercise all critical user jour neys 
defined in the Analysis Phase: 
• E2E-001: Note Lifecycle Journey: 
o   Scope: Boots from a seeded vault, clicks buttons to create notes (handling 
automatic duplication increments like `Untitled` and `Untitled (1)`), opens 
specific notes in the editor, right-clicks folders to delete notes to the Trash, and 
validates full restoration and tree updates. 
• E2E-002: Search and Graph Discovery Journey: 
o Scope: Seeds multiple test files containing tag metadata, executes queries in the 
search box, filters results dynamically, and validates cytoscape canvas 
interactive linking (drawing connections for wiki -links and mapping ghost 
nodes). 
• E2E-003: Settings Persistence Journey: 
o Scope: Operates settings toggles, switches themes, adjusts editor 
configurations, and asserts that settings persist correctly across UI updates and 
reloads.

4.2.2.6.4 Usability Testing  
Usability testing evaluates the application interface, workflow layout, and navigation structures 
with target users to ensure the system is intuitive and matches specified user productivity 
criteria. 
• Usability Elements 
• Users (Participant Profiles) 
Evaluations are conducted across three representative user groups to ensure comprehensive 
feedback: 
• Profile A (Casual User): Low-to-medium experience with advanced text applications; no 
prior familiarity with Markdown syntax or graph -based structures. Evaluates ease of 
learning and interface clarity. 
• Profile B (Technical User/Developer):  High technical literacy; regular experience with 
Markdown text syntax. Evaluates shortcut consistency, text input performance, and 
structural reliability. 
• Profile C (Advanced Graph User):  High familiarity with network -oriented knowledge 
management applications. Evaluates link generation speeds, slash commands, query 
execution, and interactive graph behaviors. 
• Location & Setup (Test Environment) 
Tests are executed in a remote and unsupervised environment (entorno remoto y no 
supervisado). Participants install the application executable directly on their personal Windows 
11 machines. This approach records feedback under realistic conditions regarding installation 
behavior, initialization performance, rendering speeds, and interface executi on under normal 
home or office operational conditions. 
• Methodology (Step-by-Step Procedure) 
The remote usability evaluation follows a three-step asynchronous methodology: 
1. Step 1: Onboarding and Profiling:  The participant receives the application installation 
package and the digital evaluation form. They fill out Section 1 (Participant Background) 
to record age, digital literacy, and tool experience. 
2. Step 2: Evaluation Survey Submission:  After using the system for some time , the 
participant completes Section 2 through Section 6  of the evaluation form, grading 
workflows via Likert-scale items, logging encountered errors, and providing qualitative 
remarks.

• Usability Analysis Framework 
The quantitative and qualitative data gathered from the evaluation questionnaire are 
aggregated and analyzed across four key usability metrics to establish baseline interface quality: 
• Learnability: Measures the capability of a first -time user to navigate the interface and 
execute core functions. This metric is evaluated by aggregating scores from tasks 1 
through 3 (opening a vault, creating a folder, and creating a note). The target success 
threshold is set at an average score of ≥ 4.3 / 5.0 on the evaluation matrices (Q21). 
• Efficiency: Evaluates the operational throughput and user navigation speed during text 
editing, note-linking, and document export operations once the user is familiar with the 
system layout. It is monitored via user ratings regarding typing responsiveness, slash -
command execution, and panel navigation (Q26). The target performance threshold is 
≥ 4.0 / 5.0. 
• Errors and Safety: Evaluates the system's fault-tolerance and error-recovery behaviors 
under incorrect user inputs. It maps self-reported technical exceptions, interface layout 
anomalies, and user-perceived recovery paths (Q9, Q10, Q27). The system must resolve 
low-severity issues automatically (e.g., trimming trailing whitespaces in filenames) and 
isolate higher-severity execution faults (e.g., duplicate directory creation requests) via 
explicit user interface notifications. 
• User Satisfaction: Measures the overall user evaluation regarding interface aesthetics, 
consistency, and functional utility. This metric aggregates overall experience scores, 
Likert-scale satisfaction inputs, and system recommendation likelihood indicators (Q29, 
Q40, Q42). The minimum target for the aggregated satisfaction index is ≥ 4.2 / 5.0. 
 
4.2.2.6.5 Performance Testing (Pruebas de Rendimiento) 
Tessellum is architected as a local -first application. Performance testing defines specific, 
measurable constraints regarding resource utilization, operation latencies, and data throughput 
to verify system responsiveness under varying workloads. 
===== PAGE 177 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 177 
 
• Resource Consumption Constraints 
The application executable must operate within the following host resource allocation 
boundaries: 
• Active Memory (RAM) Footprint: 
o Standard operational state (active markdown editor execution, file tree 
navigation, initialized search index layers): ≤ 150 MB RAM. 
o Complex graphics rendering state (active multi -node 2D/3D knowledge graph 
canvas view manipulation): ≤ 250 MB RAM. 
• Processor (CPU) Utilization: 
o Idle state (active background filesystem monitoring, no active user text inputs): 
≤ 1.0% CPU capacity. 
o Active execution state (real-time Markdown syntax tokenization and rendering): 
≤ 5.0% CPU capacity. 
o System synchronization state (background full -text search indexing or 
filesystem reconciliation bursts): ≤ 15.0%  CPU capacity. Execution must be 
restricted to background worker threads to prevent user interface thread 
blockage. 
• Disk Storage Footprint:  System overhead must be restricted exclusively to raw 
Markdown text files (.md) and the vacuumed, structurally optimized relational 
metadata cache file (.sqlite). 
• Operation Latency Criteria 
The following matrix defines the maximum target execution latencies allowed for core software 
operations:

• Profiling Strategy and Diagnostics 
System bottlenecks and memory allocations are monitored using three distinct diagnostic 
approaches: 
1. Frontend Interface Profiling:  The integrated performance panel inside the rendering 
engine tracks CPU execution flame charts, JavaScript heap lifecycle transitions, and DOM 
layout repaint timings. 
2. Backend Application Profiling:  Automated development profiling uses native 
compilation profiling utilities, including cargo flamegraph and memory tracking 
instrumentation, to isolate execution hotspots, database transaction latency issues 
within the query mapping layers, and indexing bottlenecks in the search engine core. 
3. Operating System Auditing:  Native operating system performance tracking utilities 
monitor the private working set memory allocation profiles of the compiled executable 
over continuous evaluation periods up to 24 hours to verify the complete absence of 
progressive memory retention issues. 
• Load and Stress Testing 
• Database and Index Scalability (High Volume Processing) 
To verify database access speed and indexing stability under scaled data configurations, the 
system is evaluated against specific data scale requirements: 
• Test Environment Seeding:  A synthetic testing vault containing 10,000 distinct 
Markdown files is generated, populated with metadata attributes, varied text contents, 
tag parameters, and complex cross-reference inline wiki-links. 
• System Acceptance Metrics: 
o Initial cold indexing of the entire asset collection must complete in ≤ 5 seconds. 
o Incremental filesystem change tracking updates (triggered by a single file 
modification) must process in ≤ 200 ms. 
o Multi-token search lookups across the complete document collection must 
return results in ≤ 100 ms. 
• Graph Structural Density Stress (Network Scale Ingestion) 
===== PAGE 179 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 179 
 
To evaluate the visual display canvas stability under high relational density configurations, a 
complex relationship scenario is generated: 
• Test Environment Stress Seeding:  A highly dense testing workspace layout is 
instantiated containing 5,000 active nodes interconnected via 20,000 distinct structural 
wiki-link relationships. 
• System Acceptance Metrics: 
o The graph abstraction engine must extract and project the relational matrix 
structure in ≤ 500 ms. 
o The user interface graph canvas must render and process layout scaling, nodes 
dragging, panning, and hovering interactions consistently at ≥ 60 Frames Per 
Second (FPS). 
• Resource Deprivation and Crash Resistance 
The application must guarantee absolute local data integrity under host failure simulations: 
• Disk Transaction Interruptions: Physical storage boundaries are simulated using full disk 
allocations or external file access lockouts during active modifications. The application 
must block data truncation, issue an error notification dialog to the user, and execute 
an atomic rollback of any open database transactions. 
• Low Available Memory Operations:  System memory allocations are restricted to 
minimum operating limits. The application must automatically disable layout 
animations, clear unused search query memory pools, and prioritize text editor input 
processing pathways. 
 
4.2.2.6.6 Error Detection and Correction Mechanisms 
Tessellum implements a structured error detection, classification, and mitigation framework 
across the software lifecycle to enforce stability criteria. 
• Testing Techniques Applied 
Verification procedures apply three testing methodologies: 
• Equivalence Class Partitioning (ECP):  Inputs are divided into valid and invalid 
operational domains, validating system behaviors against parameters such as supported 
vs. unsupported system locales, markdown vs. binary file formats, and directory 
references inside vs. outside the designated vault space. 
• Boundary Value Analysis (BVA):  Verification explicitly tests the limits of system 
constraints, including editor font sizing ranges (clamped between 12 and 24 pixels), the 
exact 30-day trash purging threshold, maximum search history capacities, and debounce 
window edges. 
===== PAGE 180 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
180 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Error Guessing:  Based on architecture design characteristics, specific test scenarios 
target high -probability fault points including localized database structure corruption, 
host clipboard access failures, malformed naming inputs, and uninitialized component 
sub-layers. 
• Coverage Criteria 
The system design mandates adherence to the following minimum coverage thresholds prior to 
code base integration:

• Continuous Integration Gates 
Automated test verification execution runs sequentially within the continuous integration 
infrastructure, using the following pipeline order: 
Markdown 
1. cargo test --manifest-path src-tauri/Cargo.toml:  [Executes backend isolated functional tests 
and integration suite operations] 
 
2. npx vitest run –coverage: [Executes frontend state store transitions and user interface 
component layout checks] 
 
3. npm run e2e: [Executes end-to-end multi-process system user journeys via the tauri -driver 
runtime wrapper] 
Any single verification failure within these execution stages automatically terminates the 
integration runner, blocking source code incorporation. 
===== PAGE 181 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 181 
 
• Test Isolation Contract 
To guarantee execution reproducibility and eliminate cross -test side effects, verification runs 
must adhere to strict state isolation conditions: 
• Frontend Isolation: Each test case clears all active state records, purges active browser 
data stores (localStorage, sessionStorage), and unregisters all active system function 
stubs. 
• Backend Isolation: Each test execution maps to a unique, isolated temporary workspace 
path and instantiates a discrete database file context. No file modifications or database 
updates are shared across test instances. 
• System Isolation: End-to-end automation execution models refresh the entire testing 
target vault workspace layout using a verified reference data fixture before executing 
any automation sequences. 
• 5.5. Suspension and Resumption Criteria 
Automated testing operations are suspended upon encountering any of the following system 
constraints: 
• Failure of the local development asset compiler or runtime initialization process. 
• Inability to construct clean filesystem directory testing fixtures or database storage 
paths. 
• Version discrepancies or linking anomalies between the host browser framework 
components and automation application driver binaries. 
Testing procedures resume only when system environment configurations match baseline 
specifications, testing fixture generation processes finish without warnings, or damaged system 
dependencies are replaced by isolated software stubs. 
• Defect Tracking 
Every failure recorded within the testing automation suites automatically generates a tracking 
record containing the unique validation script descriptor. Defects trace back to their originating 
functional use case parameters and target scenario matrices. Resolution verification requires a 
complete passing run of the specific verification test case path that triggered the original 
tracking entry. 
 
 
4.3 Size and Effort Estimation

4.3.1 Framework 
To keep our project estimations consistent, we use a Weighted Complexity Model . This 
framework quantifies effort based on four distinct technical dimensions, represented by the 
variables explained below. 
The core idea behind this framework is that complexity isn't monolithic; it is the sum of several 
technical and functional variables. Instead of assigning a single Fibonacci number to a story 
based on intuition, the team identifies specific complexity factors  (e.g., data logic, UI 
requirements, or integration needs) and assigns them a weight based on their relative impact 
on the overall development effort. 
The total complexity score (𝑊𝑐) for a user story is calculated using the following formula: 
𝑊𝑐 = ∑(𝑊𝑖 ∗ 𝑆𝑖)
𝑛
𝑖=1
 
Where: 
• 𝑊𝑖 represents the weight assigned to factor 𝑖. 
• 𝑆𝑖 represents the score (or intensity) of factor 𝑖 for that specific story. 
• 𝑛 is the total number of complexity factors being evaluated. 
 
By decomposing a user story into these weighted segments, two primary goals are achieved: 
1. Consistency: It reduces the variance between different estimators, as everyone 
evaluates the same set of criteria. 
2. Transparency: It allows stakeholders to see why a story is considered high -effort, 
highlighting specific technical risks or heavy UI requirements that might otherwise be 
overlooked in a traditional Planning Poker session. 
 
4.3.1.1 The Variables (𝑽) 
Each variable is scored on a scale based on the specific demands of the User Story: 
• 𝑽𝒖𝒊 (User Interface): Measures the density of the frontend work. This includes creating 
new components, handling complex layouts, managing animations, and ensuring a 
responsive design. 
• 𝑽𝒅𝒃 (Database/Index): Reflects the impact on data persistence. This involves schema 
changes, search index updates, and the complexity of data retrieval or storage. 
• 𝑽𝒈𝒓𝒂𝒑𝒉 (Knowledge Graph):  A high -weight variable focused on relational logic. It 
measures the effort required to map, traverse, or visualize connections between notes.

• 𝑽𝒔𝒚𝒔 (System/OS): Measures the direct file system I/O, operating system APIs, editor 
engine extensions, and memory management. 
 
4.3.1.2 The Formula 
We calculate the Total Weighted Complexity ( 𝑾𝒄) using specific weights that reflect how 
difficult each domain is to maintain and test: 
𝑊𝑐 = (𝑉𝑢𝑖 ⋅ 1.0) + (𝑉𝑑𝑏 ⋅ 1.2) + (𝑉𝑔𝑟𝑎𝑝ℎ ⋅ 2.0) + (𝑉𝑠𝑦𝑠 ⋅ 1.5) 
 
Once we have the 𝑊𝑐 score, it falls into one of the following buckets. These ranges help us 
translate technical density into predictable development cycles.

TABLE 4.3.2 USER STORY SIZE CALCULATION 
The results clearly demonstrate that while the user interface requires the most frequent 
attention, the project ’s technical “weight” is concentrated in the System and Graph 
components. 
Specifically, stories involving the Knowledge Graph are rare but carry a disproportionate amount 
of the project’s total complexity. This suggests that these stories should be prioritized early in 
the development lifecycle to mitigate architectural risks. 
 
4.3.2 Effort Estimation 
The transition from abstract complexity points to labor hours is managed by the Velocity 
Coefficient (𝑹). For this project, the coefficient is established as: 
===== PAGE 186 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
186 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
𝑅 = 0.85 
This value was derived through a calibration process where a baseline “Extra Small” (XS) task 
was measured against its actual implementation time. In this model, 1 point of is equivalent to 
0.85 hours (approximately 51 minutes). 
This coefficient accounts for the “True Development Time,” which includes: 
• Implementation: Active coding and logic construction. 
• Environment Overhead:  Context switching and development environment 
management. 
• Quality Assurance: Unit testing, debugging, and edge-case validation. 
• Documentation: Internal technical documentation and string internationalization.

allows for a steady, predictable velocity across Sprints. Conversely, ide ntifying US-009 as the

enabling more rigorous resource and time planning for that specific critical phase. Overall, the 
balance between quick -win tasks and high -envergure modules ensures a continuous delivery 
cycle and a smooth technical validation of the project requirements.

4.4 Project Management Plans 
4.4.1 Integration Management Plan 
 
The objective of the integration management plan is to unify and coordinate all project 
processes, activities, and components, ensuring that deliverables and milestones are achieved 
synchronously and in compliance with the initial specifications. Pursuant to the guidelines of the 
UNE 157801 standard, this plan ensures cohesion between the available resources, the 
schedule, and the technical scope of the developed information system (Tessellum). 
 
Project life cycle 
The project development follows a hybrid life cycle model, combining an initial predictive 
planning phase with iterative and incremental development cycles for the software 
implementation. The main phases are defined as follows: 
1. Initiation and Planning: Definition of the conceptual scope, system objectives, technical 
feasibility, and initial schedule estimation. 
2. Requirements Analysis and Specification: Identification of operational user needs and 
formal specification of functional and non-functional requirements. 
3. System Design: Definition of the application architecture, the knowledge -graph-based 
data model, and the user interface design. 
4. Implementation: Source code development of the desktop application according to 
local-first principles and Markdown-formatted note processing. 
5. Testing and Validation:  Execution of unit, integration, and system tests to verify 
software stability and compliance with technical requirements. 
Commented [JC43]: @ENRIQUE JUAN DE ANDRES GALIANA 
Sección para revisar 
===== PAGE 190 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
190 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
6. Closure: Consolidation of technical documentation, final report writing, and preparation 
for the public thesis defense. 
 
Configuration management and version control 
Configuration management ensures the integrity, availability, and traceability of all 
configuration items (source code, technical documentation, and design assets). The operational 
guidelines are established as follows: 
• Version Control System: Git is utilized as the decentralized version control system, using 
a remote hosting platform for secure storage, synchronization, and repository access 
management. 
• Branching Strategy: A feature-branching model is adopted. New features or bug fixes 
are developed in isolation and integrated into the main branch ( main) exclusively via 
pull requests, following conflict verification and code review. 
• Version Identification: The software adheres to the Semantic Versioning 2.0.0 standard, 
structuring version identifiers in the MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH format based on the impact 
of the introduced modifications. 
 
Change management and control 
Any modification affecting the project scope, schedule, or baseline requirements must undergo 
a formal change control process. The procedure consists of the following consecutive stages: 
1. Identification and Logging: The change request is formally documented, detailing the 
technical justification and the affected components. 
2. Impact Analysis:  The technical feasibility of the modification and its impact on the 
schedule and system architecture are evaluated. 
3. Approval: The final decision regarding acceptance or rejection is jointly assessed by the 
author and the project advisor. 
4. Implementation and Tracking:  If approved, the project baseline is updated, the 
modifications are executed, and their correct integration into the global system is 
verified. 
 
Project closure 
The closure process formalizes the completion of planned activities and the release of 
deliverables. The project is considered technically complete when the following acceptance 
criteria are met: 
• Successful validation of all system requirements through the established testing plan. 
===== PAGE 191 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 191 
 
• Consolidation of the definitive source code repository, free of critical execution errors. 
• Submission and approval of this technical documentation by the evaluation tribunal and 
the project advisor. 
 
4.4.2 Scope Management Plan 
 
The scope management plan establishes the processes required to ensure that the project 
includes all the work necessary, and only the work necessary, to complete the development of 
Tessellum successfully. In accordance with the UNE 157801 standard, this plan defines how the 
scope is defined, validated, and controlled throughout the project life cycle. 
 
Scope definition and project boundaries 
• The technical boundaries of the project, including the detailed functional inclusions (In-
Scope) and technical exclusions (Out -of-Scope) for the Tessellum application, are 
explicitly defined in Section 3.8 (Scope) of this document. 
 
Work Breakdown Structure (WBS) 
The project scope is hierarchically structured into Work Packages (WP) to facilitate planning, 
assignment, and tracking: 
• WP 1: Project Management and Documentation 
o Deliverable 1.1: Initial project charter and planning documentation. 
o Deliverable 1.2: Final project thesis (Memoria). 
• WP 2: Research and Requirements Specification 
o Deliverable 2.1: Analysis on local-first applications and knowledge graphs. 
o Deliverable 2.2: Software Requirements Specification (SRS) document including 
functional and non-functional requirements. 
• WP 3: System Design and Architecture 
o Deliverable 3.1:  Architectural design document (component, class, and data 
model diagrams). 
o Deliverable 3.2: User Interface (UI) wireframes and navigation flows. 
• WP 4: Software Implementation 
===== PAGE 192 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
192 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
o Deliverable 4.1:  Core application logic and local file system management 
module. 
o Deliverable 4.2: Markdown parsing and bidirectional linking engine. 
o Deliverable 4.3: Indexing and full-text search module. 
o Deliverable 4.4: Graph visualization interface component. 
• WP 5: Quality Assurance and Verification 
o Deliverable 5.1: Test plan and test case specification. 
o Deliverable 5.2: Automated test execution reports and bug tracking matrix. 
• WP 6: Deployment and Closure 
o Deliverable 6.1: Executable application package and installation manual. 
o Deliverable 6.2:  Project closure report and source code repository 
consolidation. 
 
Scope verification and validation 
Scope verification is the formal process of obtaining acceptance of the completed project 
deliverables by the stakeholders (the project author and advisor). 
• Inspection: Each completed deliverable undergoes technical review against the 
technical requirements defined in WP 2. 
• Acceptance Criteria:  A work package is considered complete when its respective 
deliverables meet all functional criteria, pass specified test cases, and comply with the 
documentation standards outlined by the University of Oviedo and the UNE 157801 
standard. 
• Sign-off: Formal validation requires the explicit approval of the project advisor, recorded 
in the periodic review milestones. 
 
Scope control 
Scope control monitors the status of the project scope and manages any changes to the scope 
baseline. This process is integrated with the Change Management Procedure defined previously. 
• Variance Detection:  Periodic comparisons between the work performed and the 
approved WBS will be conducted to identify deviations. 
• Scope Creep Mitigation:  Any proposed functionality not explicitly detailed in the SRS 
must be treated as a change request. Features that threaten the project schedule or 
technical feasibility will be deferred to future software iterations post-thesis defense. 
===== PAGE 193 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 193 
 
 
4.4.3 Schedule Management Plan 
 
The schedule management plan (plan de gestión de plazos) establishes the processes, metrics, 
and controls required to ensure the timely completion of the project. In accordance with the 
UNE 157801 standard, this plan outlines how schedule variances are identified, monitored, and 
mitigated throughout the project lifecycle. 
 
Schedule baseline and development methodology 
The project schedule is developed using the Critical Path Method (CPM) to identify sequential 
dependencies between work packages. Task durations are estimated using expert judgment and 
historical data from similar software development projects. 
The definitive timeline, including task durations, sequences, and dependencies, is formalized in 
Section 3.14 (Temporal Planification) of this document, which constitutes the Schedule Baseline. 
Any modification to this baseline must be processed through the formal change control 
procedure. 
 
Project milestones 
To facilitate tracking and verification, the schedule defines specific, non-overlapping milestones 
that signify the completion of critical phases: 
• M1 - Planning and Requirements Approval: Completion of the state-of-the-art research 
and formal sign-off of the Software Requirements Specification (SRS). 
• M2 - Architecture and Design Consolidation:  Finalization of data models, graph 
schemas, and user interface wireframes. 
• M3 - Core Engine Implementation:  Completion of the local -first file system observer 
and the Markdown parsing engine. 
• M4 - Interface and Visualization Integration:  Functional implementation of the 
interactive graph visualization component and user interface. 
• M5 - Testing and Quality Assurance:  Execution of the test plan and resolution of all 
identified critical software defects. 
• M6 - Final Submission and Closure: Approval of the technical thesis ( Memoria) by the 
project advisor and preparation for the public defense. 
 
Schedule monitoring and control 
===== PAGE 194 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
194 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
Schedule tracking is conducted on a weekly basis by comparing the actual progress of the Work 
Breakdown Structure (WBS) deliverables against the Schedule Baseline. 
• Tracking Mechanism: Progress is measured via the completion percentage of individual 
tasks within each work package. A task is only considered 100% complete when its 
corresponding technical deliverable complies with the criteria. 
• Variance Thresholds: 
o Green Status (Low Variance):  Delays under 5% of the total phase duration. No 
corrective action required. 
o Yellow Status (Moderate Variance):  Delays between 5% and 12% of the phase 
duration. Requires a reallocation of weekly hours to prevent impact on 
subsequent critical path dependencies. 
o Red Status (Critical Variance):  Delays exceeding 12% of the phase duration or 
any delay affecting a milestone deadline. This status mandates the immediate 
execution of schedule compression techniques. 
 
Schedule compression and contingency actions 
In the event of critical schedule variances (Red Status), the following corrective actions will be 
evaluated and applied hierarchically: 
1. Fast-Tracking: Executing specific development phases or testing tasks concurrently 
instead of sequentially, provided that technical dependencies permit parallel execution. 
2. Crashing: Increasing the weekly hours dedicated to critical path tasks to accelerate 
completion, optimizing the allocation of available technical resources. 
3. Scope Reduction: If schedule compression cannot resolve the variance due to fixed time 
constraints (e.g., academic submission deadlines), a formal change request will be 
initiated to transfer non -critical functional requirements from the current scope 
baseline to a post-defense phase. 
 
4.4.4 Costs Management Plan 
 
The cost management plan establishes the processes required to plan, estimate, budget, and 
control costs throughout the project life cycle. In accordance with the UNE 157801 standard, 
this plan outlines the mechanisms for identifying financial variances an d implementing 
corrective measures to ensure the project completes within the approved budget. 
 
===== PAGE 195 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 195 
 
Cost baseline and resource categorization 
The total financial allocation for the development of Tessellum is structured into distinct cost 
categories, encompassing direct human resources (engineering hours), hardware and software 
infrastructure, and indirect operational expenses. 
The detailed breakdown of these costs, including unit rates, asset depreciation, and the finalized 
project budget, is formalized in Section 3.15 ( Budget) of this document. The aforementioned 
section serves as the Cost Baseline. Any modification affecting the economic allocations must 
be processed through the formal change control procedure. 
 
Units of measure and precision 
To ensure consistency in economic tracking, the following parameters are established: 
• Currency Units: All costs are calculated and recorded in Euros (€). 
• Precision Level: Financial figures and calculations are rounded to two decimal places. 
• Labor Metric: Human resource costs are estimated and tracked based on engineering 
hours dedicated to the Work Packages (WP). 
 
Cost monitoring and control 
Financial tracking is conducted at the completion of each project milestone. Cost performance 
is assessed by comparing the actual expenditures and consumed engineering hours against the 
planned allocations in the Cost Baseline. 
The primary metrics used to monitor financial performance are: 
• Planned Value (PV):  The authorized budget assigned to the work scheduled to be 
completed by a given milestone. 
• Actual Cost (AC):  The total cost actually incurred and recorded for work performed 
during a given period. 
• Cost Variance (CV): The difference between the budgeted value of work completed and 
the actual costs incurred ($CV = EV - AC$, where $EV$ represents the Earned Value of 
the deliverables validated via the criteria in Section 4.4.2.3). 
 
Variance thresholds and corrective actions 
To manage deviations from the Cost Baseline, specific variance thresholds are defined: 
• Green Status (Low Variance):  Cost deviations under 5% of the allocated milestone 
budget. No corrective action is required. 
===== PAGE 196 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
196 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Yellow Status (Moderate Variance):  Cost overruns between 5% and 10%. Requires an 
immediate audit of engineering hours and an optimization of resource allocation to 
eliminate inefficiencies in subsequent tasks. 
• Red Status (Critical Variance):  Cost overruns exceeding 10%. This status mandates 
structural interventions: 
1. Re-negotiation or replacement of technical infrastructure assets with lower -
cost or open-source alternatives. 
2. Execution of the Scope Control procedure to remove low -priority functional 
requirements, thereby reducing the total engineering hours required to 
complete the project. 
 
Contingency and management reserves 
Pursuant to technical project planning standards, a contingency reserve equal to 10% of the total 
direct costs is integrated into the baseline budget. This reserve is restricted to addressing 
identified technical risks, such as data structural incompatibil ities during the graph database 
integration or unexpected software dependencies, and its drawdown must be formally 
documented. 
 
 
4.4.5 Quality Management Plan 
 
The quality management plan defines the quality policies, standards, and control mechanisms 
applicable to the development of Tessellum. Pursuant to the UNE 157801 standard, this plan 
outlines the quality assurance (QA) and quality control (QC) procedures implemented to ensure 
that all deliverables conform to both academic criteria and engineering technical requirements. 
• 4.4.5.1 Quality standards and regulations 
The project complies with the following regulatory and technical standards: 
• Documentation Standard:  UNE 157801 (Criteria for the presentation of technical 
reports for Information Systems projects). 
• Software Quality Model: ISO/IEC 25010 (System and Software Quality Models), focusing 
specifically on functional suitability, reliability, usability, and performance efficiency. 
• Code Formatting Standard:  Adherence to standardized style guides for the selected 
programming language (e.g., standard formatting rules for C#, TypeScript, or JavaScript 
depending on the implementation stack) to ensure maintainability. 
===== PAGE 197 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 197 
 
 
Quality Assurance (QA) procedures 
Quality assurance focuses on the processes used to prevent defects and ensure continuous 
improvement throughout the lifecycle. 
• Code Reviews:  Peer reviews or structured self -inspections of the source code are 
performed prior to merging any feature branch into the main repository branch. 
• Continuous Integration (CI): The repository is configured with automated pipelines that 
trigger static code analysis and compilation checks upon every push or pull request to 
identify syntax errors, anti-patterns, and security vulnerabilities early. 
• Documentation Reviews:  The progress of the technical thesis ( Memoria) is 
systematically reviewed against the formal guidelines established by the Escuela de 
Ingeniería Informática of the University of Oviedo. 
 
Quality Control (QC) procedures 
Quality control consists of the specific inspection and testing activities executed to verify that 
the software meets its technical requirements. 
• Testing Levels: 
o Unit Testing: Verification of individual classes, methods, and functions isolated 
from external dependencies (e.g., validating Markdown text parsing logic). 
o Integration Testing: Verification of the interaction between combined modules, 
specifically the communication between the local file system observer, the 
metadata indexing engine, and the knowledge graph data structure. 
o System Testing:  Execution of end -to-end user scenarios to validate that the 
completely integrated software fulfills all functional requirements specified in 
the SRS. 
• Metrics and Targets: 
o Code Coverage: A target minimum of 75% statement coverage for core business 
logic modules (parsing and graph management). 
o Defect Density: Zero critical or blocking defects unresolved at the time of final 
system deployment. 
 
Defect management and resolution 
When a deviation or defect is identified during quality control inspections, it must be formally 
tracked using the following workflow: 
===== PAGE 198 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
198 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
1. Logging: The defect is registered in the repository's issue tracking system, detailing the 
steps to reproduce, the expected behavior, and the observed behavior. 
2. Classification: Defects are categorized by severity: 
o Critical: Causes system crashes, data corruption, or prevents the execution of 
core functions. Must be resolved immediately. 
o Major: Fails to meet a functional requirement but a technical workaround 
exists. Must be resolved before the current milestone ends. 
o Minor: Cosmetically impacts the user interface or documentation without 
affecting system operation. Fixed as resources permit. 
3. Resolution and Verification: Once the code modification is applied, the respective test 
case is re-executed alongside a regression test suite to ensure the defect is resolved and 
no new errors have been introduced. 
 
Deliverable acceptance criteria 
A deliverable is officially approved from a quality perspective only when it meets the following 
objective thresholds: 
• Successful compilation and execution under target environment parameters. 
• 100% passing rate for the verified test suite corresponding to that specific work package. 
• Conformance of associated technical documentation to the structure and professional 
tone mandated by the UNE 157801 standard. 
 
4.4.6 Human Resources Management Plan 
 
The resource and organization management plan defines the organizational structure, roles, and 
resource allocation principles governing the development of Tessellum. In accordance with the 
UNE 157801 standard and the academic framework of an individual undergraduate thesis, this 
plan delineates the functional responsibilities of the involved entities and establishes the 
mechanisms for optimizing individual effort and technical infrastructure. 
 
Organizational Breakdown Structure (OBS) and roles 
Although the operational execution of the project is performed by a single developer, a clear 
division of roles is established to maintain formal project governance, quality verification, and 
strategic alignment. The functional organizational structure is defined as follows: 
===== PAGE 199 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 199 
 
• Project Director / Advisor:  Responsible for high -level oversight, validation of project 
milestones, academic compliance verification, and final authorization of deliverables. 
• Project Manager (Author):  Responsible for schedule tracking, risk monitoring, cost 
management, and communication baseline maintenance. 
• Software Architect and Developer (Author): Responsible for technical research, system 
design, software engineering, source code implementation, and local database schema 
definition. 
• Quality Assurance Engineer (Author):  Responsible for test case design, execution of 
automated verification suites, and defect tracking. 
 
Resource allocation and effort tracking 
Because human resource capacity is constrained to a single engineering asset, resource 
management focuses strictly on time-allocation management and individual effort optimization: 
• Effort Estimation: Resource allocation is managed by translating the Work Breakdown 
Structure (WBS) deliverables into quantified engineering hours based on historical 
benchmarks for similar software development components. 
• Workload Balancing: Weekly dedication is tracked against the Schedule Baseline. To 
prevent resource over -allocation or burnout, weekly workloads are bound to a pre -
established maximum capacity of hours. 
• Resource Conflict Resolution:  Since team -based interpersonal conflicts are non -
applicable, resource availability constraints (e.g., illness or technical impediments) are 
resolved strictly through the Schedule Compression or Scope Control mechanisms. 
 
Material and infrastructure resources 
Human resource efficiency is directly dependent on the provision and maintenance of the 
technical infrastructure. The material resources allocated to this project are categorized into: 
• Hardware Assets: One standard x86-64 client workstation utilized for local development 
environment execution, application compilation, and local -first knowledge graph 
rendering. 
• Software Infrastructure:  Open-source frameworks, integrated development 
environments (IDEs), and decentralized version control repositories (as detailed in the 
technical stack specification) provided without licensing costs, ensuring strict budget 
compliance with the Cost Baseline. 
• Work Environments: Physical space and network connectivity infrastructure suitable for 
uninterrupted execution of engineering and writing tasks.
