4.4.7 Communication Management Plan 
 
The communications management plan establishes the mechanisms, channels, and frequencies 
required to ensure the efficient and structured flow of information between the project 
stakeholders. In accordance with the UNE 157801 standard, this plan defines how project status, 
performance, requirements, and modifications are formally transmitted and documented 
throughout the lifecycle. 
 
Communication requirements and stakeholders 
The stakeholder register for this project is restricted to two core entities: the Project Author 
(acting as Developer and Manager) and the Project Advisor. The communications matrix is 
designed to optimize information exchange while minimizing overhead, structured as follows: 
• Internal Communication (Author):  As an individual project, day -to-day coordination 
between technical execution roles (development, architecture, and testing) is direct and 
requires no formal communication channels. Information integrity is maintained strictly 
through version control commit logs and issue tracking comments. 
• External Governance Communication (Author to Advisor):  Formal information 
exchange focused on milestone validation, academic compliance, technical guidance, 
and scope approval. 
 
Communication channels and tools 
To ensure traceability and formalization of all agreements, the approved communication 
channels are restricted to the following tools: 
• Corporate Email:  Utilized as the primary channel for non -urgent notifications, 
scheduling of reviews, formal document submission, and official correspondence. 
• Videoconferencing / In -Person Meetings:  Employed for complex technical reviews, 
milestone validation, and structural feedback sessions. 
• Version Control Repository: Used as a transparent communication channel where code 
documentation, structural architecture changes, and defect management are publicly 
visible and tracked through automated pull request discussions. 
 
Communication frequency and reporting 
Information distribution is structured around specific temporal boundaries and project events 
to prevent deviations from the Schedule Baseline: 
===== PAGE 201 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 201 
 
• Bi-weekly Progress Reports: The Author compiles a brief status summary detailing the 
work performed during the preceding sprint, the objectives targeted for the next period, 
and any technical impediments encountered. This report is submitted via corporate 
email. 
• Milestone Review Sessions: Conducted upon the completion of each project milestone. 
These sessions involve the technical demonstration of completed deliverables and the 
formal evaluation of the respective Work Packages against the quality standards. 
• Ad-hoc Consultations:  Initiated by the Author via corporate email when blocking 
technical constraints arise that threaten the critical path or require a structural 
architectural deviation. 
 
Escalation and change communication 
In the event of critical project variances, a formal escalation procedure is triggered: 
1. Notification: The Author must immediately document the root cause of the variance, its 
projected impact on the final thesis submission deadline, and the proposed technical 
solution. 
2. Transmission: This documentation is formally communicated to the Project Advisor via 
corporate email within 48 hours of variance detection. 
3. Resolution: A mandatory review session is scheduled to evaluate the application of the 
Scope Control procedure or Schedule Compression techniques. The final decisions and 
modifications to any project baseline are appended to the project minutes and 
integrated into the change log. 
 
4.4.8 Risk Management Plan 
 
The risk management plan establishes the processes required to identify, analyze, evaluate, and 
mitigate risks throughout the lifecycle of Tessellum. Pursuant to the UNE 157801 standard, this 
plan outlines the structured approach used to minimize the probability and impact of negative 
threats and maximize the benefits of positive technical opportunities. 
 
Risk identification and categorization 
Risks and opportunities within the Tessellum ecosystem are systematically categorized to 
address engineering, architectural, and procedural constraints: 
• Technical Risks (TEC):  Associated with software engineering complexities, platform -
level system behavior, performance thresholds, and implementation toolchains. 
===== PAGE 202 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
202 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Scope and Management Risks (MAN):  Related to project limitations, single -resource 
dependencies, and feature-set boundaries within the fixed calendar timeline. 
• Technical Opportunities (OPP):  Structural advantages resulting from architectural 
paradigms, technical decisions, or testing frameworks that increase development 
velocity and software quality. 
 
Qualitative risk analysis and metric parameters 
The assessment of identified uncertainties follows a multidimensional qualitative structure. In 
alignment with the project's engineering parameters, each event is evaluated against specific 
impact categories, including Probability, Budget Impact, Planification Impact, Scope Impact, and 
Quality Impact. These variables dictate whether the required operational strategy is to Mitigate, 
Avoid, or actively Leverage the condition. 
 
Baseline reference and risk log 
The detailed inventory of project threats, technical bottlenecks, and systemic development 
opportunities is formalized outside the management processes section. 
The complete risk matrix —including detailed descriptions, individual impact vector metrics, 
specific preventive strategies, and technical contingency plans —is explicitly detailed in Section 
3.12 (Risk Analysis) of this document. The aforementioned section serves as the formal Project 
Risk Baseline. Any subsequent identification of structural threats or opportunities must be 
appended directly to that matrix following the documentation update parameters. 
 
Monitoring and response execution protocols 
Risk and opportunity metrics are reassessed continuously during the Sprint Review sessions held 
with the Project Advisor. 
• Active Threat Triggers: Mitigation and avoidance protocols defined in the Risk Baseline 
are executed immediately when their specific technical trigger conditions are met (such 
as a memory ownership conflict halting a development sprint or a feature proposal 
threatening the baseline scope boundary). 
• Opportunity Capitalization: Design and programming routines must actively integrate 
identified positive synergies, such as utilizing the system's local -first architecture to 
maximize execution speed or exploiting component reusability to decrease front -end 
interface overhead. All ri sk responses, status changes, and closure actions are 
documented chronologically in the technical logs. 
 
===== PAGE 203 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 203 
 
4.4.9 Acquisitions Management Plan 
 
The procurement management plan (plan de gestión de adquisiciones) establishes the processes 
required to acquire products, services, or results needed from outside the project team. In 
accordance with the UNE 157801 standard, this plan defines how external  procurement 
operations are planned, executed, and controlled to ensure technical compatibility and 
compliance with the Cost Baseline. 
 
Procurement strategy and boundaries 
Due to the nature of Tessellum as an individual software engineering project focused on a local-
first architecture, the procurement strategy is heavily optimized to prioritize open -source 
software libraries and zero -cost digital assets. This minimizes contract overhead and ensures 
complete fiscal alignment with the budget parameters. 
• Inclusions (Make-or-Buy Boundaries): 
o Procurement is strictly confined to off-the-shelf software packages, third-party 
development tools, open -source programming frameworks, runtime 
environments, and infrastructure hardware components. 
o No professional services, external software sub -contracting, outsourcing, or 
external engineering labor will be procured for this project. All design, 
implementation, and testing tasks are executed internally. 
 
Roles and responsibilities in procurement 
The procurement workflow is managed within the functional structure of the project: 
• Requester and Evaluator (Author):  Identifies the technical need for an external 
component, performs technical compatibility evaluations, and verifies open -source 
license compliance. 
• Approver and Financial Controller (Project Advisor): Reviews the technical justification 
and provides formal authorization for the integration of the requested asset or 
infrastructure component. 
 
Selection criteria and contract types 
For any software dependency, package, or development infrastructure to be acquired and 
integrated into Tessellum, it must satisfy the following objective selection criteria: 
• Licensing Compliance: The asset must be governed by permissive open-source licenses 
that allow free execution, structural modification, and compilation within an academic 
===== PAGE 204 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
204 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
software framework without introducing restrictive copyleft obligations (e.g., standard 
GPL variations that conflict with specific deployment models). 
• Technical Maturity: The package must demonstrate active maintainer support, updated 
documentation, and proven performance stability under local-first workloads. 
• Cost Structure:  Priority is assigned to assets with a zero -cost tier. Any commercial 
acquisition (such as development hardware or dedicated physical testing devices) must 
utilize standard fixed-price procurement parameters to completely insulate the project 
against variable billing risks. 
 
Procurement monitoring and control 
The tracking of acquisitions is performed continuously and reviewed during the milestone 
validation sessions. 
• Inventory Tracking: Every acquired component, third -party library, and infrastructure 
hardware item is systematically logged in the project's configuration management 
baseline via explicit dependency manifests (such as lockfiles or technical asset registers). 
• Variance Mitigation:  If an acquired open -source dependency becomes deprecated, 
introduces security vulnerabilities, or exhibits performance degradation that violates 
the Quality Management Plan parameters, it is flagged within the issue tracking system. 
A formal technical rep lacement process is then initiated to locate, validate, and 
integrate an alternative open-source component without impacting the Cost Baseline. 
 
4.5 Security Plan 
The security plan establishes the guidelines, methodologies, tools, and organizational controls 
required to ensure the integrity, confidentiality, and availability of the project information 
assets. In accordance with the guidelines of the UNE 157801 stand ard, this plan unifies the 
technical, organizational, and legal aspects applicable to Tessellum, focusing specifically on 
critical control points determined by the nature of the software and current legislation. 
 
Methodology and tools for security management 
Security management throughout this project is governed by a Security by Design  approach, 
embedding attack vector identification and vulnerability mitigation into every iteration of the 
software development life cycle. 
• Analysis Methodology:  A simplified adaptation of standard risk analysis and 
management methodologies for information systems is employed. Each technical 
component (the file system parser, the IPC communication bridge, and the viewport 
Commented [JC44]: @ENRIQUE JUAN DE ANDRES GALIANA 
Sección para revisar 
===== PAGE 205 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 205 
 
rendering engine) is evaluated to identify potential threats prior to code 
implementation. 
• Technical Control Tools: 
o Dependency Auditing: Automated static analysis vulnerability scanners (cargo 
audit for the Rust core engine and npm audit for the React/TypeScript user 
interface environment) are integrated into the version control workflow. These 
tools automatically detect known vulnerabilities in third-party libraries prior to 
application compilation. 
o Input Sanitization:  Specialized parsing libraries are utilized to neutralize 
malicious scripts (Cross -Site Scripting or XSS vulnerabilities) potentially 
embedded inside local Markdown files. 
 
Organizational and management aspects 
At the organizational level, security duties are distributed within the project resource structure 
defined in previous sections: 
• Governance and Review: The Project Author is responsible for enforcing secure coding 
standards, while the Project Advisor validates that the selected technical 
implementations do not compromise the integrity of the system's operational 
environment. 
• Security Incident Management:  If a critical vulnerability is identified in a third -party 
dependency or within the core source code, development on the affected feature is 
suspended immediately. The defect is formally documented in the issue tracking system 
and prioritized for resoluti on via a security patch before establishing the next 
configuration baseline. 
 
Identification of system critical points 
Due to the architecture and purpose of Tessellum, specific critical control points are identified 
where technical security is determinant: 
1. Execution Environment Isolation (IPC Bridge):  As a desktop application built on Tauri, 
communication between the front-end user interface (JavaScript) and the back-end core 
engine (Rust) is conducted via an Inter -Process Communication (IPC) bridge. This point 
is critical because a security breach would allow the execution of arbitrary code on the 
host operating system. Security is managed by restricting exposed IPC commands 
exclusively to the bare functions necessary for file system operations. 
2. Local File System Access: The local-first architectural paradigm requires the software to 
read from and write directly to local directories designated by the user. The critical risk 
lies in preventing the accidental modification or deletion of directories outside the user's 
===== PAGE 206 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
206 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
note vaults. This is mitigated by restricting the scope of the file system observer 
(watcher) strictly to the root path selected by the user. 
3. Code Injection in Graph Visualization: The rendering of the knowledge graph and notes 
processes dynamically generated metadata. The system must guarantee that 
Markdown syntax content is not interpreted directly by the UI rendering engine as 
executable scripts. 
 
Legal and regulatory aspects 
Security management is strictly aligned with the current legal frameworks governing data 
protection and intellectual property: 
• GDPR / RGPD Compliance:  Although Tessellum stores information exclusively on the 
user's local storage infrastructure and implements no centralized servers or telemetry, 
the system fulfills the Privacy by Default  principle. The lifecycle of the data remains 
under the absolute control of the end user, completely mitigating the legal risks 
associated with cloud-based data breaches. 
• Intellectual Property and Licensing:  The integration of third -party libraries requires 
continuous legal tracking to ensure that all procurement operations utilize permissive 
licenses compatible with academic software distribution guidelines, preventing legal 
infringements regarding protected source code.

5.1.1 User Personas 
The following personas have been defined to represent the diverse requirements of the system's 
target audience, ranging from basic content creation to complex technical documentation and 
architectural maintenance. 
 
Persona Role Description 
General User Focuses on everyday writing and personal organization. They prioritize a 
clean, distraction-free environment and an intuitive interface where the 
technical syntax is hidden until needed. Their goal is simplicity and 
aesthetic polish. 
Technical User A power user who documents scientific, mathematical, or engineering 
concepts. They require high-precision tools like LaTeX rendering and raw 
syntax control to ensure their documentation meets professional and 
academic standards. 
Knowledge 
Architect 
Dedicated to building a "second brain" or a vast network of 
interconnected ideas. They rely heavily on internal linking (Wikilinks) and 
quick navigation tools to discover relationships between disparate notes 
without breaking their creative flow. 
System 
Maintainer 
A developer-focused profile concerned with the application’s underlying 
health. They value standardized project structures, clean state 
management, and robust import/export capabilities to ensure the 
software remains maintainable and scalable. 
Visual 
Communicator 
A user who creates notes intended for high readability and scannability. 
They use visual markers like callout blocks and selective rendering to 
create a clear information hierarchy, making complex documents easier 
to digest at a glance.

5.1.3 Acceptance Criteria and Definition of Done 
5.1.3.1 US-001 
5.1.3.1.1 Real-Time Rendering Engine 
• The editor must parse and render Markdown syntax into formatted rich text 
immediately as the user types (latency should be imperceptible to the user). 
• The system must not require a manual toggle, "Preview Mode," or side-by-side pane to 
display the formatted output. 
5.1.3.1.2 Supported CommonMark Syntax  
The live preview must correctly render the following elements according to standard 
CommonMark specifications: 
• Headers: Six levels of nesting using the # symbol (H1–H6). 
• Emphasis: Bold text using or __ and Italics using * or _. 
• Strikethrough: Text wrapped in ~~. 
• Lists: Both unordered lists (using *, -, or +) and ordered lists (using 1.). 
• Blockquotes: Text preceded by the > character, supporting multi-line nesting. 
5.1.3.1.3 Data Integrity and Persistence 
• The underlying data model must store only raw Markdown strings. 
• When saving to disk, the resulting file must be a .md (or .txt) file containing pure plain 
text. 
• The application is strictly prohibited from injecting HTML tags (<b>, <i>, etc.) or 
proprietary metadata/JSON wrappers into the saved file. 
5.1.3.1.4 External Compatibility (Interoperability) 
• Files generated and saved by the editor must be fully readable and correctly formatted 
when opened in external standard editors, specifically VS Code and Notepad. 
• The editor must be able to open and render existing standard Markdown files without 
losing formatting or introducing incompatible characters. 
 
5.1.3.2 US-002 
5.1.3.2.1 Vault Initialization and Configuration 
• Upon the first launch of the application, the system must prompt the user to select a 
specific local directory to function as the "Vault". 
===== PAGE 238 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
238 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• The application must store and remember this local directory path so that subsequent 
uses do not require re-selection. 
5.1.3.2.2 Note Generation and Data Standards 
• When a user creates a new note, the system must immediately generate a valid file 
within the Vault directory. 
• Every note file must use the .md file extension. 
• All file operations must utilize UTF-8 encoding to ensure the notes remain accessible 
and readable by other tools on the hard drive. 
5.1.3.2.3 Filename Sanitization and Collision Logic 
• The application must automatically sanitize filenames by stripping illegal system 
characters (such as /, ,, and :) to prevent file system errors. 
• If a file with the same name already exists in the directory, the system must resolve the 
collision by appending a number, such as "Note (1).md," instead of overwriting the 
existing file. 
5.1.3.2.4 Auto-save and Data Persistence 
• The editor must implement a debounce mechanism that triggers an auto-save only after 
the user has stopped typing for a window of 1–2 seconds. 
• To prevent any data loss, the system must perform an immediate save operation if the 
user closes the application window. 
5.1.3.2.5 Non-Destructive Deletion 
• Deleting a note from within the user interface must not result in the permanent, instant 
destruction of the file. 
• The system must move the deleted file to the operating system's native trash or recycle 
bin, or to a hidden .trash folder within the Vault, to allow for accidental recovery. 
 
5.1.3.3 US-003 
5.1.3.3.1 Syntax Detection and Visual Rendering 
• The editor must continuously monitor the user's text input to detect the completion of 
the double-bracket syntax (e.g., [[Target Note]]). 
• Immediately upon the user typing the closing ]] brackets, the editor must recognize the 
pattern and render the internal text as a styled, clickable anchor. 
• The visual style of the link must be distinct from standard text, utilizing formatting such 
as an underline or blue coloration. 
===== PAGE 239 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 239 
 
• While the link is rendered visually in the UI, the system must keep the underlying 
Markdown text ([[...]]) intact within the raw file data. 
5.1.3.3.2 Navigation and File System Interaction 
• When a rendered link is clicked, the application must perform an automated check of 
the file system within the local Vault. 
• If a file matching the name inside the brackets exists, the editor must close the current 
note and open the target note for editing. 
• If no matching file exists, the system must seamlessly create a new .md file with that 
exact name and save it to the disk immediately. 
• Following the creation of a new file, the application must automatically open the new 
blank note to facilitate "click-to-create" non-linear writing. 
 
5.1.3.4 US-004 
5.1.3.4.1 Hierarchical Tree Visualization 
• The application must display the entire contents of the designated "Vault" as a nested 
tree structure. 
• The tree must allow users to navigate through multiple levels of nested folders to access 
individual notes. 
5.1.3.4.2 Visual Distinction and Indentation 
• The interface must provide a clear visual distinction between folders and files (e.g., using 
different icons). 
• The system must implement consistent indentation to accurately represent the depth 
and parent-child relationships of each element within the hierarchy. 
5.1.3.4.3 Sorting and Display Logic 
• The tree view must prioritize directories by displaying them at the top of their respective 
levels, followed by individual files. 
• Both directories and files must be sorted in alphabetical order within their groups to 
ensure predictable navigation. 
 
===== PAGE 240 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
240 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
5.1.3.5 US-005 
5.1.3.5.1 Trigger and Menu Activation 
• The system must monitor for a forward slash (/) character to trigger the formatting 
menu. 
• The trigger must only activate if the forward slash is typed at the absolute beginning of 
a line or is preceded by whitespace. 
• Upon activation, a floating dropdown menu containing available formatting elements 
must appear near the text cursor. 
5.1.3.5.2 Navigation and Filtering 
• The menu must support real-time filtering based on additional characters typed by the 
user after the slash (e.g., typing "h1" narrows the list to heading options). 
• Users must be able to navigate the menu items using the keyboard (Up/Down arrow 
keys) or the mouse. 
5.1.3.5.3 Selection and Syntax Insertion 
• Selecting a menu option via the "Enter" key or a mouse click must automatically remove 
the slash trigger and any filter text. 
• The removed trigger text must be replaced immediately with the correct Markdown 
syntax for the selected element. 
5.1.3.5.4 Dismissal Logic 
• The context menu must close automatically once an item is selected. 
• The menu must be dismissed without inserting syntax if the user presses the "Escape" 
key, clicks anywhere outside the menu, or deletes the forward slash trigger. 
 
5.1.3.6 US-006 
5.1.3.6.1 Inline Mathematical Rendering 
• The application must identify LaTeX syntax enclosed within single dollar signs (e.g., 
$E=mc^2$) and render it as formatted math. 
• Inline equations must be rendered within the text stream and maintain proper vertical 
alignment with the surrounding text baseline. 
5.1.3.6.2 Display and Block Rendering 
• The system must recognize LaTeX syntax enclosed between double dollar signs ($$) 
placed on separate lines as a block element. 
===== PAGE 241 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 241 
 
• Display equations must be rendered as a centered block, ensuring they are visually 
distinct from the preceding and following paragraphs. 
5.1.3.6.3 Mathematical Command and Notation Support 
• The rendering engine must support standard LaTeX commands without requiring 
additional user configuration. 
• Supported notations must include, but are not limited to, fractions (\frac), summations 
(\sum), integrals (\int), and square roots (\sqrt). 
• The system must correctly render Greek letters, complex matrices, and multi -line 
aligned equation environments. 
5.1.3.6.4 Visual Professionalism and Formatting 
• All rendered mathematical content must be presented in a professional, high -fidelity 
format suitable for technical and scientific documentation. 
• The rendered output must be readable and maintain consistent styling across both 
inline and display modes. 
 
5.1.3.7 US-007 
5.1.3.7.1 Workspace and Sidebar Management 
• The application must feature a simplified sidebar that users can toggle (hide or show) to 
maximize the available writing space. 
• When the sidebar is hidden, the editor must automatically expand to fill the newly 
available screen real estate. 
• The interface must maintain a modern, integrated look that reduces visual clutter to 
help the user focus on writing. 
5.1.3.7.2 Command Menu and Workflow Efficiency 
• The command menu must be optimized to consistently appear in a convenient, 
predictable location within the workspace. 
• The system must support quick keyboard shortcuts for menu actions to facilitate an 
uninterrupted, faster workflow. 
• Navigation within the menu must be intuitive and responsive to both mouse and 
keyboard inputs. 
5.1.3.7.3 Unified Visual Identity 
• All windows, dialogs, and menus must share a unified and polished design language to 
ensure the application feels cohesive. 
===== PAGE 242 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
242 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• UI elements (such as buttons, icons, and borders) must use consistent styling, spacing, 
and color palettes across the entire application. 
• The final interface design must meet professional standards, ensuring the software is 
easy to navigate even for new users. 
 
5.1.3.8 US-008 
5.1.3.8.1 Trigger Detection and Menu Activation 
• The application must monitor the editor for the specific link trigger (e.g., [[). 
• Upon detecting the trigger, the system must immediately present a clear, floating menu 
positioned near the cursor. 
• The menu must be populated with a list of all current notes existing within the user's 
Vault. 
5.1.3.8.2 Real-Time Filtering and Search 
• The suggestion menu must support real -time, fuzzy searching as the user continues to 
type after the trigger. 
• The filtering mechanism must allow users to find relevant notes without needing to 
remember or type the exact file names. 
• The search results must update dynamically with every keystroke to ensure a responsive 
experience. 
5.1.3.8.3 Selection and Link Insertion 
• Users must be able to navigate the suggested notes using either the keyboard (Up/Down 
arrows) or the mouse. 
• Selecting a note from the menu must automatically complete the WikiLink syntax and 
insert the correct internal link into the text on the fly. 
• The insertion process must seamlessly transition the user back to the editing flow 
without requiring manual closing of the menu. 
5.1.3.8.4 Workflow and Interconnectivity 
• The system must ensure that the link suggestion process does not interrupt the writing 
flow, facilitating the creation of an interconnected knowledge graph. 
• If no matching note is found or the user wishes to dismiss the menu, the application 
must allow for easy cancellation (e.g., via the Escape key or clicking away). 
 
 
===== PAGE 243 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 243 
 
5.1.3.9 US-009 
5.1.3.9.1 Global and Local Graph Visualization 
• The system must provide a global graph view that visually maps all notes and their inter-
note relationships across the entire vault. 
• The application must include a local graph view that isolates and displays only the direct 
relationships associated with the currently active note. 
• Both graph views must be interactive, allowing users to identify information clusters and 
structural patterns within their knowledge base. 
5.1.3.9.2 Visual Representation of Note States 
• Nodes representing existing notes must be visually distinguishable from nodes 
representing non-existent notes (notes referenced via links but not yet created). 
• Connections leading to non -existent notes must be rendered using dashed lines  to 
indicate their status. 
5.1.3.9.3 Node Interaction and Metadata Display 
• Single-click interaction: Clicking a node once must trigger a display showing a list of that 
note's relationships and its specific file system path. 
• Double-click navigation: Double-clicking a node must immediately redirect the user to 
the corresponding note in the editor. 
5.1.3.9.4 Dynamic Note Creation 
• If a user double -clicks a node for a note that does not yet exist, the system must 
automatically create the new .md file in the vault. 
• Following the automatic creation, the application must immediately open the new note 
for editing. 
 
5.1.3.10 US-010 
5.1.3.10.1 Focus-Based Rendering Toggle 
• The editor must automatically toggle the display mode of a specific text line or block 
between raw Markdown syntax and its final rich-text formatted version. 
• When a line or block does not have the active focus of the text cursor, it must render in 
its final formatted state to ensure a clean, distraction-free reading experience. 
5.1.3.10.2 Visibility of Underlying Structure 
• The system must immediately reveal the underlying Markdown symbols (e.g., #, , >) the

5.1.3.31.1 Automatic Delimiter Pairing 
• The editor must automatically insert the corresponding closing character immediately 
after the user types an opening bracket ([), parenthesis ((), or brace ({). 
• The system must automatically provide closing Markdown markers for formatting —
such as backticks (`) for code or asterisks (*) and underscores (_) for emphasis —once 
the opening character is detected. 
5.1.3.31.2 Momentum-Preserving Cursor Behavior 
• Upon auto-inserting a closing marker, the system must position the cursor immediately 
between the pair to allow for continuous, uninterrupted text entry. 
• The functionality must prioritize maintaining the knowledge architect's writing 
momentum by reducing the manual overhead required to finish structural syntax. 
5.1.3.31.3 Syntax Integrity and Accuracy 
• The automation must ensure that all Markdown syntax is always perfectly balanced, 
preventing errors caused by unclosed tags or mismatched delimiters. 
• The feature must eliminate the need for manual correction of brackets and markers, 
ensuring that the final document is structured correctly from the first draft. 
5.1.3.31.4 Workflow Optimization 
• The editor should implement "overtype" logic, ensuring that if a user manually types the 
closing character that was already auto -inserted, the system does not generate a 
duplicate character. 
• The feature must be responsive and non -intrusive, adapting to the user's typing speed 
to keep the creative flow seamless. 
 
5.1.3.32 US-032 
5.1.3.32.1 Navigation History Management 
• The system must maintain a chronological history stack of all recently visited notes and 
views during the active session. 
• The navigation logic must allow the user to "quickly retrace" their steps through the 
sequence of documents they have accessed. 
===== PAGE 260 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
260 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
5.1.3.32.2 Directional Controls and Logic 
• The Backward Arrow must be functional whenever there is at least one previous note 
or view in the session history. 
• The Forward Arrow  must become active only after a user has performed a "back" 
operation, allowing them to return to the more recent note in the sequence. 
• Navigation must be instantaneous, allowing users to jump between "related topics" 
without the need to "manually search" for their previous document. 
5.1.3.32.3 Context and State Persistence 
• The application must preserve the user's specific context within a note, including the 
scroll position and active cursor location, to ensure they do not "lose their place" when 
navigating. 
• Switching between notes via arrows must maintain the current view mode (e.g., Reading 
vs. Editing) for each document in the history stack. 
5.1.3.32.4 UI Responsiveness 
• The navigation controls must provide visual feedback (such as a disabled state or grayed-
out icon) when no further backward or forward history is available. 
• The arrows must be positioned in a consistent, easily accessible location within the 
workspace header to facilitate a fluid research workflow. 
 
5.1.3.33 US-033 
5.1.3.33.1 Hierarchical Sidebar View 
• The application must provide a dedicated sidebar panel that displays a hierarchical table 
of contents for the active note. 
• The table of contents must be generated automatically based on the presence of 
Markdown headings (from Level 1 to Level 6). 
• The outline must visually represent the heading hierarchy (e.g., through indentation) to 
allow the user to instantly grasp the document's structure. 
5.1.3.33.2 One-Click Navigation 
• The system must enable instant navigation to any section of the document with a single 
click on the corresponding heading in the outline. 
• The editor's scroll position must update immediately to center the selected heading 
within the view. 
===== PAGE 261 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 261 
 
5.1.3.33.3 Workflow Support for Complex Research 
• The feature must specifically support the needs of a knowledge architect when dealing 
with long-form writing and complex research. 
• The outline must remain accessible in the sidebar, ensuring that structural management 
is consistent regardless of the current editing position in the file. 
5.1.3.33.4 Dynamic Synchronization 
• The table of contents must update in real -time as headings are added, modified, or 
removed within the editor. 
• The outline must accurately reflect the structure of the active note even after switching 
between multiple tabs or files in the workspace. 
 
5.1.3.34 US-034 
5.1.3.34.1 Syntax and Recognition 
• The editor must recognize and parse single backticks (`) as the standard Markdown 
delimiter for inline code elements. 
• The system must correctly identify and render technical text wrapped in backticks even 
when it is positioned directly within a sentence of standard prose. 
5.1.3.34.2 Visual Formatting and Distinction 
• Formatted inline code must utilize a distinct monospace font to clearly separate it from 
the surrounding proportional-width prose. 
• The interface should apply subtle visual cues, such as background shading, to ensure 
technical terms, variables, and commands are "easy to read at a glance". 
• The rendering must ensure a high -contrast distinction between the technical markers 
and the general narrative text. 
5.1.3.34.3 Precision and Documentation Standards 
• The system must treat content within backticks as literal text to ensure that complex 
technical documentation remains precise and avoids accidental Markdown parsing. 
• Inline code elements must remain on the same line as the surrounding text, maintaining 
the flow of the sentence without triggering block-level formatting. 
5.1.3.34.4 User Experience for Technical Workflows 
• The application must support the rapid formatting of technical terms to minimize 
friction during the creation of documentation. 
===== PAGE 262 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
262 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Styling for inline code must be consistent across all themes to ensure cross-environment 
readability for the technical user. 
 
5.1.3.35 US-035 
5.1.3.35.1 Markdown Task Syntax Support 
• The editor must recognize and render the standard Markdown checkbox syntax: - [ ] for 
incomplete tasks and - [x] for completed tasks. 
• The system must support nesting task lists and mixing them with standard bulleted or 
numbered lists. 
5.1.3.35.2 Interactive Checkbox Toggling 
• Users must be able to toggle the completion state of a task by clicking the checkbox 
directly within the note interface. 
• Toggling a checkbox in the UI must immediately update the underlying Markdown 
source code (changing [ ] to [x] or vice versa). 
5.1.3.35.3 Visual Completion Indicators 
• The interface must provide clear visual feedback when a task is marked as complete, 
such as a visible checkmark within the box. 
• Completed tasks should ideally feature a subtle styling change, like dimmed text or a 
strikethrough, to distinguish them from active action items at a glance. 
5.1.3.35.4 Seamless Inline Integration 
• Task lists must be integrated directly into the note's body, allowing the user to manage 
"daily to-dos" alongside their research or prose without switching views. 
• The rendering of checkboxes must not disrupt the alignment or readability of the 
surrounding text. 
5.1.3.35.5 Data Persistence and Portability 
• The state of each task must be saved as plain text within the .md file to ensure that task 
progress is preserved across different sessions and devices. 
• The system must ensure that the "action items" remain functional and editable even if 
the file is moved to a different folder within the vault. 
 
===== PAGE 263 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 263 
 
5.1.3.36 US-036 
5.1.3.36.1 Raw Markdown Display 
• The application must provide a dedicated "Source Mode" that displays the unrendered, 
raw Markdown text of the note. 
• All Markdown syntax markers (such as #, , [[ ]], and ![]()) must be visible and editable as 
plain text. 
• The system must disable all "Live Preview" or WYSIWYG rendering features while this 
mode is active. 
5.1.3.36.2 High-Precision Toggle Mechanism 
• The system must include a clear toggle mechanism (e.g., a status bar button or a 
keyboard shortcut) to switch instantly between Source Mode and the standard 
rendered view. 
• The transition must be seamless, maintaining the current cursor position and scroll 
depth within the document. 
5.1.3.36.3 Manual Syntax Management 
• Source Mode must allow the technical user to manually manage complex syntax, such 
as multi-line tables, nested HTML, or intricate frontmatter, without interference from 
automated formatting. 
• The editor should utilize a monospace font in this mode to ensure character alignment 
and precision control over the document’s structure. 
5.1.3.36.4 Editing Reliability and Synchronization 
• Changes made in Source Mode must be saved directly to the underlying .md file, 
ensuring no data is lost or altered during the switch back to rendered mode. 
• The system must handle incomplete or "broken" Markdown syntax in Source Mode 
without crashing or forcing a rendering attempt until the user toggles out of the mode. 
5.1.3.36.5 Visual Clarity 
• The interface must provide a distinct visual indicator (such as a label or icon change) 
when Source Mode is active to prevent accidental edits in the wrong viewing context. 
• The UI must prioritize a clean, minimal environment to ensure the focus remains entirely 
on the raw code structure. 
 
===== PAGE 264 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory

5.1.3.37 US-037 
5.1.3.37.1 Deletion to Dedicated Trash 
• When a user deletes a file, the application must move the file to a dedicated, local Trash 
system rather than removing it from the disk immediately. 
• Deleted files must be hidden from the primary file explorer and search results to ensure 
the user maintains a clean, distraction-free environment. 
5.1.3.37.2 File Restoration 
• The system must provide a mechanism to view all items currently residing in the trash. 
• Users must be able to restore a file to its original location within the Vault with a single 
action. 
• Upon restoration, the file must be immediately re -indexed and made available for 
editing and linking. 
5.1.3.37.3 Permanent Deletion 
• The system must allow users to manually select and permanently delete files from the 
trash to free up local storage. 
• A confirmation prompt should appear before a permanent deletion is executed to 
prevent further accidental data loss. 
5.1.3.37.4 Peace of Mind and Safety 
• The trash system must function as a reliable "safety net" during everyday writing, 
ensuring that accidental deletions can be easily reversed without technical expertise. 
• The application must ensure that the trash contents are stored locally, preserving the 
user's data privacy and control. 
5.1.3.37.5 Integration and Accessibility 
• Access to the trash system must be intuitive, potentially located within the settings 
panel or as a dedicated view in the file management sidebar. 
• The system must handle file metadata (such as the original deletion date) to assist the 
user in identifying which files to restore or purge. 
 
5.1.3.38 US-038 
5.1.3.38.1 Language and Locale Selection 
• The application must feature a centralized setting within the preferences panel that 
allows users to change the application's language and locale settings.

• The system must support a variety of languages, allowing the interface to be displayed 
in the user’s native language. 
5.1.3.38.2 Interface Adaptation 
• Upon changing the language, all core UI elements —including menus, buttons, tooltips, 
and labels—must update immediately or upon a prompt to restart. 
• The transition must ensure a "truly intuitive experience" by providing accurate 
translations that avoid technical jargon or awkward phrasing. 
5.1.3.38.3 Locale-Specific Formatting 
• The software must adapt locale settings to match regional standards, specifically for 
date, time, and number formatting. 
• The environment must "feel familiar and accessible" to the user, ensuring that structural 
elements of the UI (like right -to-left support, if applicable) align with the chosen 
language. 
5.1.3.38.4 Settings Persistence 
• Language and locale preferences must be saved to the local configuration to ensure a 
distraction-free environment that persists across all future sessions. 
• The application must load the user's preferred language automatically upon startup 
without requiring manual re-selection. 
 
5.1.3.39 US-039 
5.1.3.39.1 Dedicated Reference Interface 
• The application must include a dedicated tab or section within the settings panel 
specifically for keyboard shortcuts. 
• The shortcut list must be presented as a static reference list that is easily accessible and 
readable. 
5.1.3.39.2 Navigation and Global Commands 
• The reference list must include the commands necessary to navigate between different 
notes within the vault. 
• The system must list shortcuts for executing global actions rapidly (e.g., opening search 
or creating new files). 
5.1.3.39.3 Workflow Efficiency and Flow 
• The shortcuts must be designed to ensure the user never has to break their creative flow 
to use a mouse for standard navigation or global tasks.

• The layout must pair each action with its corresponding key combination clearly to 
facilitate rapid learning for the "knowledge architect". 
 
5.1.3.40 US-040 
5.1.3.40.1 Adaptive Selection Logic 
• The sidebar context menu must dynamically detect the specific object type (note or 
folder) targeted by the user's selection. 
• The system must identify the target type before rendering the menu to ensure that only 
relevant operational tools are visible. 
5.1.3.40.2 Folder-Specific Organizational Tools 
• When a folder is selected, the context menu must display organizational actions, such 
as "Create New Note," "New Subfolder," or "Rename Folder". 
• Organizational tools must be grouped to help the system maintainer efficiently manage 
the underlying structure of the workspace. 
5.1.3.40.3 Note-Specific File Handling 
• When an individual note is selected, the menu must prioritize file-handling actions, such 
as "Open in New Tab," "Duplicate File," or "Delete Note". 
• The interface must exclude folder -level actions when a note is selected to prevent UI 
clutter and ensure standardized file management. 
5.1.3.40.4 Structural Hierarchy and Scalability 
• The context menu logic must support a scalable project hierarchy, ensuring 
performance remains consistent as the number of folders and notes increases. 
• Implementation of these adaptive menus must enable the user to maintain a 
standardized structure without needing to navigate through external settings. 
5.1.3.40.5 UI Consistency and Efficiency 
• The behavior of the context menu must be consistent throughout the sidebar, including 
all nested subfolders and linked assets. 
• The transition between different menu sets (note vs. folder) must be instantaneous to 
support a fast, uninterrupted management workflow.

5.1.3.41 US-041 
5.1.3.41.1 High-Contrast Theme Implementation 
• The application must include a dedicated "High -Contrast" theme option within the 
centralized appearance settings. 
• The theme must utilize a color palette that maximizes the contrast ratio between 
background and foreground elements (text, icons, and borders) to meet or exceed 
accessibility standards. 
• Switching to the High-Contrast theme must be applied instantaneously across the entire 
interface without requiring a restart. 
5.1.3.41.2 Visual Hierarchy and Scannability 
• The theme must establish a "sharp information hierarchy," utilizing high -contrast 
borders and distinct font weights to separate headers, body text, and UI components 
clearly. 
• All interactive elements must be "easily scannable," ensuring that the active focus and 
selection states are unmistakably visible. 
• The workspace must remain "digestible," meaning the increased contrast should 
enhance clarity without creating visual noise or excessive eye strain during long -term 
use. 
5.1.3.41.3 Environmental and Hardware Adaptability 
• The interface must provide "maximum readability" that remains effective regardless of 
external "lighting conditions," such as high-glare environments or low-light settings. 
• The visual design must ensure that information is not lost due to "screen quality" issues, 
maintaining clarity even on displays with lower color accuracy or resolution. 
5.1.3.41.4 Universal UI Consistency 
• High-contrast styling must be applied consistently to all application areas, including the 
sidebar, tab workspace, settings panel, and graph views. 
• The theme must ensure that specialized Markdown elements—such as code blocks, task 
lists, and links—are rendered with high-contrast visibility relative to the standard prose. 
 
5.1.3.42 US-042 
5.1.3.42.1 Modal Editing Implementation 
• The application must include a toggleable Vim Mode within the settings panel to enable 
or disable modal editing. 
===== PAGE 268 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
268 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• When active, the editor must support the three core Vim modes: Normal (for navigation 
and commands), Insert (for standard text entry), and Visual (for text selection and block 
manipulation). 
• The interface must provide a visible status indicator to inform the technical user which 
mode is currently active. 
5.1.3.42.2 Navigation and Precision Commands 
• The system must support standard h, j, k, l directional movement and advanced 
navigation motions (e.g., w, b, e, $, 0, G, gg) in Normal mode. 
• High-precision commands for text manipulation —including deletion (d), yanking (y), 
pasting (p), and changing (c)—must be fully functional. 
• The editor must support combining operators with motions (e.g., dw to delete a word 
or y$ to yank to the end of a line) to maintain professional engineering standards for 
speed and efficiency. 
5.1.3.42.3 Keyboard-Centric Workflow 
• The system must allow for a complete editing workflow where the user never has to 
take their hands off the keyboard to use a mouse for navigation or manipulation. 
• The application must support basic command -line mode (initiated with :) for global 
actions such as searching (/) or basic file operations. 
• Keybinding execution must be instantaneous and free of perceptible lag to ensure the 
user’s creative and technical momentum is preserved. 
5.1.3.42.4 Persistence and Reliability 
• The Vim mode configuration must be saved locally and persist across application 
restarts. 
• The system must ensure that enabling Vim keybindings does not interfere with global 
application shortcuts unless specifically overridden for the editing context. 
 
5.1.3.43 US-043 
5.1.3.43.1 Formatting Toolbar Accessibility 
• The application must provide a visible formatting toolbar within the editor interface. 
• The toolbar must be easily accessible to the general user without requiring complex 
navigation. 
5.1.3.43.2 Core Formatting Styles 
• The toolbar must include intuitive buttons or icons to apply common text styles, 
specifically bold and italics.

Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 269 
 
• The system must provide options for creating and managing lists (bulleted or numbered) 
directly from the toolbar interface. 
5.1.3.43.3 Syntax Hiding and Intuitive Interface 
• The toolbar must allow users to apply formatting through an intuitive UI, keeping the 
underlying Markdown syntax hidden from view. 
• The interface must be designed to facilitate "everyday writing" by reducing the need for 
users to memorize specific Markdown symbols. 
5.1.3.43.4 Real-Time Interaction 
• Applying a style via the toolbar must immediately update the visual representation of 
the text in the editor. 
• The toolbar should remain responsive and synchronized with the user's current 
selection or cursor position. 
 
5.1.3.44 US-044 
5.1.3.44.1 Editor Gutter Implementation 
• The application must feature a dedicated vertical gutter on the left side of the editor 
specifically for displaying line numbers. 
• Line numbers must be displayed sequentially, starting from 1 at the beginning of the 
document. 
• The gutter must remain visually distinct from the main text area to prevent interference 
with the document's content. 
5.1.3.44.2 High-Precision Referencing 
• The system must ensure that each number is perfectly aligned horizontally with its 
corresponding line of text. 
• Line numbers must update dynamically in real -time as the technical user  adds or 
removes lines, maintaining absolute accuracy for referencing. 
• The numbering must account for wrapped lines, ensuring that line numbers only 
increment at actual newline characters to maintain "professional development 
environment" standards. 
5.1.3.44.3 Professional Review Standards 
• The visual style of the line numbers (font size and color) must be optimized for legibility 
while remaining subtle enough to not distract from the primary documentation. 
• The feature must support reviewing "complex data structures" or code by allowing users 
to pinpoint and communicate specific locations within a file with high precision. 
===== PAGE 270 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
270 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
5.1.3.44.4 Workflow and Performance 
• The rendering of line numbers in the gutter must be performant, even in exceptionally 
long documents, without causing input lag. 
 
5.1.3.45 US-045 
5.1.3.45.1 Real-Time Detection and Highlighting 
• The application must automatically detect spelling errors in real -time as the general 
user types. 
• Errors must be visually highlighted using a standard non -intrusive indicator (e.g., a red 
wavy underline) to maintain the "aesthetic polish" of the document. 
• The highlighting must update instantly when a word is corrected or modified. 
5.1.3.45.2 Contextual Suggestions 
• The system should provide a list of suggested correct spellings when a user interacts 
with a highlighted error (e.g., via right-click). 
• Selecting a suggestion must immediately replace the misspelled word with the chosen 
correction while preserving the surrounding text formatting. 
5.1.3.45.3 Dictionary Management 
• Users must have the ability to "Ignore" a highlighted word or "Add to Dictionary" to 
prevent future flags for specialized terminology or names. 
• The personal dictionary must persist across sessions, ensuring that "professional and 
error-free" notes are maintained consistently. 
5.1.3.45.4 Configuration and Performance 
• The application must provide a toggle in the settings panel to enable or disable the spell 
check feature globally. 
• The background spell -checking process must be highly performant, ensuring no 
perceptible input lag even during rapid typing or in long documents. 
 
5.1.3.46 US-046 
5.1.3.46.1 Export Execution and Workflow 
• The application must provide a clear "Export to PDF" action accessible via the file menu 
or command palette for the active note. 
===== PAGE 271 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 271 
 
• The system must allow the user to specify a destination path on the local file system for 
the generated PDF. 
• The default filename for the export must match the title of the note. 
5.1.3.46.2 High-Fidelity Rendering 
• The exported PDF must accurately preserve the information hierarchy (headings, sub-
headings, and lists) established in the Markdown source. 
• The "aesthetic polish" of the application —including theme colors, custom styling, and 
font choices—must be reflected in the final output. 
• All embedded visual assets, such as images and diagrams, must be rendered at high 
resolution within the PDF document. 
5.1.3.46.3 Universal Readability 
• The output must be a standard .pdf file that is universally readable across all common 
PDF viewers on desktops, tablets, and mobile devices. 
• The document layout must be automatically paginated (e.g., A4 or US Letter) to ensure 
the content remains "easy to digest" regardless of the viewing device. 
• Internal links and standard URLs within the note should remain interactive in the 
exported file. 
5.1.3.46.4 Performance and Reliability 
• The export process must be performant, generating the file within a reasonable 
timeframe even for documents with significant media content. 
• The system must handle the conversion process without altering the original .md source 
file. 
5.1.3.47 Definition of Done 
To ensure the quality and consistency of the developed features within the Scrum framework, a 
formal Definition of Done (DoD) has been established. A User Story is only considered "Done" 
and ready for the Product Increment when it satisfies the following criteria: 
5.1.3.47.1 Functional & Technical Criteria 
• Requirement Fulfillment: The feature fully implements the functionality described in 
the corresponding Functional Requirement (FR) and meets all acceptance criteria 
defined in the User Story. 
• Code Quality: The source code follows the project's style guide (e.g., ESLint/Prettier for 
TypeScript). The code must be modular and documented according to the internal API 
standards. 
===== PAGE 272 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
272 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Per-Line Performance: For editor-related features, the implementation must be verified 
to maintain the NFR5.1 (Input Latency) standard, ensuring no degradation in the per -
line rendering performance. 
• Knowledge Graph Integrity: Any change affecting note relationships must be reflected 
accurately in the Graph View without breaking existing nodes or edges. 
5.1.3.47.2 Testing & Validation 
• Unit Testing: All new logic must be covered by unit tests. Existing tests must pass to 
ensure no regressions were introduced. 
• Integration Testing: Features involving the Plugin API or Theme Engine must be tested 
against the core system to ensure interoperability. 
• Manual UI/UX Review:  The feature must be verified across the supported operating 
systems (NFR2.1) and must comply with the dark/light mode CSS variables of the Theme 
Engine (NFR3.2). 
5.1.3.47.3 Security & Compliance 
• Privacy Check:  Verification that the feature does not trigger unauthorized external 
network calls, adhering to the "Local-First" policy (NFR4.1). 
• Sanitization: Any user input rendered via Markdown or Terminal Callouts must be 
sanitized to prevent XSS (Cross -Site Scripting) or unauthorized system command 
execution. 
5.1.3.47.4 Documentation 
• User Documentation:  If the feature introduces new Markdown syntax or a new API 
endpoint for plugins, the internal README or user guide must be updated. 
 
6 Budget 
This budget has been developed in strict compliance with the drafting guidelines specified in the 
UNE 157801 standard. The economic evaluation of project Tessellum is strictly parameterized 
under the following engineering baseline assumptions: 
1. Single-Resource, Multi -Role Execution:  The project is executed by a single physical 
engineering resource operating across multiple professional profiles. Cost calculations 
are structured by treating each profile as an independent operational cost center based 
on actual hours recorded in the project schedule. 
2. Standard Labor Burden:  Hourly rates defined for each role are fully burdened, 
incorporating baseline wages, Spanish statutory employer -side social security 
Commented [JC46]: @ENRIQUE JUAN DE ANDRES GALIANA 
Sección para revisar 
===== PAGE 273 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 273 
 
contributions, general corporate overhead, and specialized workspace operational 
infrastructure. 
3. Hardware, Software, and Capital Expenditures Baseline:  The system architecture 
leverages existing consumer-grade development hardware and utilizes an entirely open-
source, royalty-free software stack (Rust systems toolchain, Node.js/TypeScript, React 
ecosystem, and the Tauri framework). Consequently, the acqu isition cost for physical 
computing assets and software licensing is factored at €0.00, isolating the entire 
material execution budget to human resource engineering effort. 
4. Fiscal Provisions:  In accordance with Spanish fiscal legislation for professional 
engineering and technology consulting services, a standard 21% Value Added Tax 
(V.A.T.) is applied globally to the net cost of material execution.
