7 Studies with Independent Entity 
7.1 Regulatory Compliance Framework (GDPR / 
LOPDGDD) 
Tessellum is designed to operate in full compliance with the European Union’s General Data 
Protection Regulation ( GDPR) and the Spanish LOPDGDD 3/2018. In its baseline architecture, 
the system is fundamentally highly favorable from a data protection standpoint because it 
enforces a strict Privacy-by-Design and Privacy-by-Default paradigm. 
Commented [JC47]: @ENRIQUE JUAN DE ANDRES GALIANA 
Sección para revisar 
===== PAGE 284 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
284 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
 
Data Exposure and Local-First Architecture 
Because the application functions as a local -first desktop system, the following architectural 
boundaries apply: 
• Local Execution:  All user -generated text notes, metadata databases, and index 
structures are processed and maintained strictly on the host machine's local storage file 
system. 
• Absence of Centralized Cloud Risk: The application lacks a mandatory cloud ecosystem, 
meaning no automated telemetry, sync loops, or unauthorized data transfers occur 
across external networks. 
• Organizational Dependency:  While the core software is inherently secure against 
unauthorized cloud processing, lawful usage ultimately depends on the nature of the 
content stored by the end -user and the administrative security policies of the 
organizational environment where the software is compiled and deployed. 
 
7.2 Study on Intellectual and Industrial Property 
Legislation 
 
Intellectual Property of the Software 
The Tessellum codebase, structural documentation, interface assets, and original engineering 
materials constitute intellectual creations protected by copyright law. The project explicitly 
establishes its engineering footprint under open source principles, ensuring that authorship, 
copyright ownership, and the licensing conditions governing how the software can be studied, 
modified, distributed, or reused are systematically transparent. 
This study comprehensively maps third-party dependencies incorporated into the project, since 
the final binary artifact is compiled on top of external crates, libraries, components, icons, and 
development tools. 
 
Third-Party Components and License Compatibility 
The project integrates open -source dependencies from the Rust (Cargo) and Node.js (npm) 
packaging ecosystems. Legal compliance and system validity require adherence to the following 
conditions: 
===== PAGE 285 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 285 
 
• Permissive Framework Licensing:  The core foundational dependency stack relies on 
highly permissive frameworks, specifically governed under the MIT and Apache 2.0  
licenses. 
• Notice Preservation:  The final binary compilation preserves the structural legal 
attribution notices and copyright blocks mandated by these third -party open -source 
components. 
• Tree Verification:  No dependencies, code fragments, graphical resources, or media 
assets of unknown, proprietary, or copyleft-restrictive (such as strict GPL configurations 
that could force the licensing of your own code) origins are permitted within the core 
development tree. 
 
User Content and Generated Artifacts 
Tessellum manages notes, attachments, and exported documents created or imported by the 
user. Ownership of that content remains strictly separate from ownership of the software 
framework itself. Consequently: 
• The application does not transfer authorship or exploitation rights of user-created notes 
to the software author. 
• The end -user remains legally responsible for ensuring that imported text engines, 
graphics, PDFs, and embedded assets do not infringe third-party intellectual property. 
• Exported outputs generated by the application (such as compiled PDF exports or 
Markdown trees) include protected user material and must be handled under the 
corresponding legal conditions of the owner. 
 
Industrial Property Considerations 
Although Tessellum is an engineering software artifact rather than a physical industrial design 
product, industrial property considerations regarding trademarks, trade names, logos, or 
distinctive commercial signs associated with the application apply. To ensure compliance, the 
project strictly enforces: 
• The avoidance of names, configurations, or visual branding elements that conflict with 
existing protected trade marks. 
• The non-reuse of brand assets from third parties without formal authorization. 
 
Assessment 
The project is completely viable in intellectual and industrial property terms provided that core 
authorship is documented, third -party permissive licenses are respected, and the origin of 
external assets is tightly controlled via lockfiles. The primary legal risk does not derive from the 
===== PAGE 286 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
286 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
system's internal architecture, but from potential user-driven inclusion of protected content or 
improper commercial recycling of the open-source components. 
 
7.3 Study on Occupational Risk Prevention 
 
Nature of the Project 
Tessellum is a software engine developed through computer -based systems engineering 
activities, including active systems programming, user interface scaffolding, testing, and 
engineering documentation design. It does not utilize heavy mechanical infrastructure, chemical 
agents, or hazardous industrial processes. Therefore, the associated occupational risks are 
categorized strictly as ergonomic, visual, and psycho-organizational. 
 
Main Risk Factors 
The most relevant occupational risk prevention (ORP) parameters identified during the 
execution lifecycle are: 
• Asthenopia (visual fatigue) caused by prolonged exposure to display screen equipment 
(DSE). 
• Musculoskeletal disorders resulting from poor workstation ergonomics or improper 
screen alignments. 
• Repetitive strain injuries (RSI), such as carpal tunnel syndrome, associated with 
continuous keyboard and mouse utilization. 
• Mental fatigue and cognitive overload linked to sustained debugging, logical 
troubleshooting, and rigorous documentation sprints. 
• Secondary electrical safety hazards regarding office cabling and infrastructure 
connections. 
 
Preventive Measures 
The recommended preventive measures for the execution of this project align with standard IT 
office safety guidelines: 
• Ergonomic Configuration: Mandatory deployment of ergonomically adjustable seating, 
desks, and optimized display screen angles. 
• Visual Hygiene:  Application of periodic break schedules (e.g., the 20 -20-20 rule) to 
mitigate eye strain and postural rigidity. 
===== PAGE 287 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 287 
 
• Environmental Management:  Maintaining adequate workspace lighting levels, 
structural ventilation, and controlled ambient noise profiles. 
• Electrical Ordering:  Clean organization and checking of all power supplies, surge 
protections, and grounding vectors. 
• Workload Balancing: Balanced schedule planning across the 4 -hour workday baseline 
to mitigate severe stress peaks during integration and delivery phases. 
 
Assessment 
No extraordinary or high -severity occupational hazards are identified for the standard 
development lifecycle of Tessellum. The project complies fully with conventional academic and 
professional software development risk profiles, meaning ORP parameters are  completely 
satisfied through standard workstation safety management and ergonomic best practices. 
 
7.4 Study on Environmental Impact 
 
General Considerations 
The environmental footprint of Tessellum is exceptionally low when contrasted with enterprise 
software systems that require dedicated cloud multi -tenancy, distributed database servers, or 
continuous machine learning cloud loops. Its local -first topology li mits remote dependency, 
drastically lowering the indirect data-center processing emissions and network overhead energy 
costs. 
 
Main Environmental Factors 
The environmental metrics tied to the development and runtime lifecycle of the software 
include: 
• Electrical power consumption of the local workstation during engineering and end-user 
execution. 
• Indirect energy load consumed during local compiler optimization loops, unit testing 
suites, and data indexation. 
• Storage hardware resource footprint on local storage arrays. 
• Potential electronic waste (e -waste) associated with the operational lifecycle of the 
underlying physical computer assets. 
 
===== PAGE 288 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
288 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
Green Computing Advantages of the Project Stack 
Several deliberate engineering and architectural decisions explicitly reduce the environmental 
footprint of Tessellum: 
• The Rust Green Efficiency Factor:  The selection of Rust as the core systems language 
provides a massive environmental advantage. Compiled Rust binaries execute without 
a garbage collector or a heavy virtual machine, optimizing CPU execution and memory 
usage. Academic and industry benchmarks prove Rust consumes significantly less power 
and clock cycles than interpreted runtimes or resource -heavy Electron-based desktop 
alternatives (e.g., Obsidian or VS Code), directly lowering operational carbon emissions. 
• Zero Cloud Persistence:  The system operates natively without a permanent, power -
hungry cloud server infrastructure running 24/7. 
• Lightweight Storage Footprint: User databases are kept as highly optimized, lightweight 
Markdown files, avoiding massive proprietary block storage allocations. 
• Hardware Lifespan Extension:  By optimizing performance through a compiled 
Rust/Tauri footprint rather than an Electron wrapper, the application runs smoothly on 
older, low -spec hardware assets, helping to mitigate premature e -waste cycles by 
extending computer longevity. 
 
Assessment 
The environmental impact of Tessellum is highly limited, efficient, and fully acceptable for a 
modern software engineering project. Its main carbon vector is indirect and restricted to 
standard workstation electricity use. No adverse or blocking environmen tal effects are 
identified, positioning the system as an environmentally friendly alternative within the 
knowledge-management software domain. 
 
7.5 Final Synthesis 
The comprehensive analytical studies compiled in this section formally validate the external 
legal, operational, safety, and environmental adequacy of Tessellum, complementing its 
technical design specifications. 
From the viewpoint of UNE 157801  compliance, the project achieves an optimal structural 
profile: 
• Data Protection:  The local -first, privacy -by-design framework minimizes information 
exposure and satisfies the core requirements of the GDPR. 
• Intellectual Property: Legal viability is fully established by using permissive open-source 
licenses (MIT/Apache 2.0) and implementing distinct content-ownership boundaries. 
===== PAGE 289 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 289 
 
• Risk Prevention:  The project's risks fall strictly within office ergonomic baselines, 
requiring only standard visual and posture controls. 
• Environmental Sustainability: The local execution combined with the runtime energy 
efficiency of compiled Rust code guarantees a minimalist carbon footprint. 
Consequently, no blocking legal, regulatory, environmental, or operational friction exists that 
would impede the active development, academic validation, or standard deployment of 
Tessellum. 
8 System Implementation 
8.1 Standards and Norms Followed 
During the engineering lifecycle of Tessellum, specific coding standards, formatting protocols, 
and quality assurance norms were integrated into the development workflow to ensure code 
maintainability, systemic security, and structural compliance. 
 
Applied Engineering Standards 
1. Rust Idiomatic Standards : The backend subsystem architecture complies with the 
official Rust API Guidelines. Source code formatting is strictly governed by the rustfmt 
utility, enforcing uniform indentation, spacing parameters, and maximum line -length 
thresholds across the Rust codebase. 
2. TypeScript and React Development Specifications : The frontend subsystem complies 
with the ECMAScript 2022 (ES2022+) specification, strict TypeScript typing protocols 
(forbidding the utilization of the any type), and the structural Rules of Hooks for React 
components. Syntactic styling and formatting are managed via Prettier. 
3. Engineering Documentation Standard: The structure, nomenclature, and presentation 
of the project documentation strictly adhere to the guidelines set forth by the UNE 
157801:2014 norm for Information Technology and Software Engineering projects. 
 
Automated Compliance Validation 
The validation of the defined development standards is executed via an automated continuous 
integration pipeline rather than manual inspection. A workflow automation pipeline deployed 
via GitHub Actions (tauri-ci.yml) is initialized upon every repository commit or pull request. This 
pipeline executes the following deterministic validation sequences: 
• cargo clippy -- -D warnings: Enforces idiomatic Rust compilation parameters and treats 
syntactic warnings as compilation errors. 
Commented [JC48]: @ENRIQUE JUAN DE ANDRES GALIANA 
Sección para revisar 
===== PAGE 290 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
290 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• cargo fmt --check: Evaluates codebase alignment with the rustfmt configuration, 
rejecting non-compliant styling. 
• eslint and prettier --check: Validates frontend TypeScript and React code structures to 
identify potential runtime anomalies and styling deviations. 
Any non-compliance detected within these automated checks results in a pipeline execution 
failure, preventing integration into the primary branch. 
 
8.2 Programming Languages 
The decoupled architecture of the application needs the utilization of two primary programming 
languages, each selected and optimized for specific execution domains. 
 
Rust 
• Version: 1.95.0 (Stable channel) 
• Distribution Management: Managed via rustup, the official Rust toolchain installer. 
• Functional Scope: Implementation of the native backend layer. Handles low -level file 
system operations, concurrent background indexing processes, relational database 
queries, and the Inter-Process Communication (IPC) bridge. 
• Core Libraries (Crates): 
o tauri: Core framework for desktop environment integration. 
o sqlx: Asynchronous SQL toolkit utilized for SQLite database management. 
o tantivy: Full-text search engine library used for note text indexing. 
o grafeo: Embedded graph library for bidirectional link projections. 
o serde: Serialization and deserialization framework for structured JSON data 
transition. 
 
TypeScript 
• Version: 5.x 
• Distribution Management: Executed and managed via Node.js (v24.14.x LTS) and the 
npm package manager (v10.x). 
===== PAGE 291 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 291 
 
• Functional Scope: Implementation of the Graphical User Interface (GUI). Provides static 
type-checking over JavaScript to eliminate runtime state anomalies within the client 
interface. 
• Core Libraries and Frameworks: 
o react: Declarative interface rendering engine. 
o tailwindcss: Utility-first CSS framework for programmatic interface styling. 
o zustand: State management library for data storage isolation (vault contexts, 
search queries, interface states). 
o cytoscape: Graph theory analysis and rendering library for knowledge graph 
visualizations. 
 
8.3 Development Tools and Subsystems Used 
The implementation of Tessellum required a specific software ecosystem to manage the 
compilation, execution, and testing requirements of the dual-stack architecture. 
8.3.1 JetBrains RustRover 
• Version Reference: 2026.1 (or compatible release) 
• Functional Scope : Integrated Development Environment (IDE) optimized for the 
backend. Interacts natively with the Rust compiler and Cargo package manager to supply 
real-time memory safety analysis, borrow-checker telemetry, and diagnostic debugging 
within the src-tauri directory. 
8.3.2 Visual Studio Code (VS Code) 
• Version Reference: 1.90+ 
• Functional Scope : Core development environment for the frontend subsystem. 
Interfaces with the npm runtime environment using language server protocols (ESLint, 
Prettier, and Tailwind CSS IntelliSense) to standardize React component development 
within the src directory. 
8.3.3 Tauri CLI 
• Version Reference: 2.x 
===== PAGE 292 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
292 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Functional Scope: Main compilation and packaging utility. Orchestrates the integration 
between the frontend asset build system and the native Rust compiler, compiling web 
assets and embedding them into the target native executable binary. 
8.3.4 Vite 
• Version Reference: 6.4.x 
• Functional Scope : Frontend build tool and local development server. Compiles 
TypeScript code assets and processes PostCSS stylesheets. During execution testing, it 
interfaces with the Tauri WebView to supply Hot Module Replacement (HMR) 
capabilities, modifying the UI state without recompiling the backend binary. 
8.3.5 Cypress & Vitest 
• Version Reference: Cypress 13.12.x / Vitest 4.1.x 
• Functional Scope: Automated testing frameworks. Cypress executes End -to-End (E2E) 
functional testing, interfacing with the frontend via a simulated abstraction layer 
(mockBackend.ts) to circumvent native API dependency blocks. Vitest executes isolated 
unit tests for core frontend logic and utility functions. 
8.3.6 Git & GitHub Actions 
• Version Reference: Git 2.40+ / GitHub Enterprise Cloud 
• Functional Scope: Distributed version control and CI/CD automation. Git tracks source 
code modifications locally, while GitHub Actions allocates virtual machines running 
Windows, macOS, and Ubuntu to execute cross -platform compilation and binary asset 
validation. 
 
8.4 System Creation 
8.4.1 Encountered Problems 
This section documents the most relevant technical problems encountered during the 
development process of Tessellum, detailing the nature of each issue, the identified root cause, 
and the applied solution. 
 
===== PAGE 293 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 293 
 
8.4.1.1 Problem 1: Cross -Platform Incompatibility of the Kùzu 
Graph Database 
 
Problem Description 
The initial implementation of Tessellum's graph subsystem used Kùzu as the embedded graph 
database engine. Kùzu was selected for its native Cypher query support and its performance in 
in-memory graph traversal operations. 
However, during the continuous integration phase on GitHub Actions, the Rust crate kuzu failed 
to compile correctly on the Ubuntu (Linux) and macOS runners. It produced linking errors with 
the native C++ libraries that Kùzu required as a system dependency. While compilation 
succeeded on Windows, the CI pipelines for the other two platforms failed systematically, 
blocking the generation of cross-platform artifacts. 
 
Root Cause 
Kùzu internally depends on a native C++ library that requires specific compilation toolchains 
(such as CMake and C++ compilers with C++20 support) along with system libraries that differ 
significantly between platforms. 
• The GitHub CI runners do not include these dependencies by default. 
• The versions of the kuzu crate available on crates.io at the time of development did not 
provide precompiled binaries for all target platforms (Windows x64, macOS arm64/x64, 
Ubuntu x64). 
 
Applied Solution 
Kùzu was replaced with Grafeo (grafeo = "0.5.39"), an embedded graph library written entirely 
in Rust. 
• Platform Uniformity:  Being a native Rust crate with no external C/C++ system 
dependencies, Grafeo compiles identically on all three target platforms without 
requiring additional toolchains. 
• Code Adaptation:  The grafeo_projection.rs module was reimplemented using the 
Grafeo API, maintaining Cypher-style (GQL) query functionality through the GrafeoDB, 
Config, and Session primitives provided by the library. 
• CI Integration:  This migration allowed the CI pipeline (tauri -ci.yml) to successfully 
complete builds on Windows, macOS, and Ubuntu consistently. 
===== PAGE 294 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
294 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
8.4.1.2 Problem 2: Inability to Execute E2E Tests on the Native 
Tauri Application 
 
Problem Description 
Tessellum is a desktop application built with Tauri, where the React frontend communicates 
with the Rust backend through an IPC (Inter -Process Communication) bridge via @tauri -
apps/api/core. 
When attempting to implement end -to-end (E2E) tests with Cypress, it was discovered that 
Cypress operates exclusively within a conventional web browser and cannot interact with the 
native Tauri environment. IPC calls to functions such as invoke("list_files"), invoke("write_file"), 
or invoke("get_graph_data") failed immediately since the Tauri process was not available within 
the test browser context. This prevented the validation of any functional flow depending on the 
backend (note creation, search, graph visualization, trash management, etc.). 
 
Root Cause 
Tauri executes the web interface inside a native system WebView (WebView2 on Windows, 
WebKitGTK on Linux, WKWebView on macOS), injecting a proprietary IPC bridge at 
window.__TAURI_INTERNALS__. Cypress, however, launches an independent Chromium 
browser that  lacks this IPC bridge, causing all invocations to the Rust backend to return 
connection errors or remain unresolved. 
 
Applied Solution 
A complete backend mock layer  was designed to substitute the Tauri APIs during E2E test 
execution. The solution consists of two complementary mechanisms: 
• Conditional Vite Aliases: In vite.config.ts, when the environment variable VITE_E2E=1 
is active, imports from Tauri modules (@tauri -apps/api/core, @tauri -apps/plugin-fs, 
@tauri-apps/plugin-dialog, etc.) are redirected to local mock implementations located 
in src/e2e/tauri/. 
• In-Memory Mock Backend:  The file src/e2e/mockBackend.ts implements a complete 
simulated backend that emulates the Rust backend operations in pure JavaScript. This 
includes a virtual file system with MockVault, directory tree construction, simulated full-
text search, graph data g eneration from parsed wiki -links, trash management, and file 
change event emission. Each IPC invocation is intercepted in the invokeMock() function 
and resolved against this in-memory state. 
===== PAGE 295 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 295 
 
8.4.1.3 Problem 3: File Path Normalization Inconsistencies Across 
Platforms 
 
Problem Description 
During the testing of features involving bidirectional links (wiki-links), backlinks, and knowledge 
graph visualization, severe inconsistencies in path resolution were detected. Links that worked 
correctly on Windows (using \ separators) did not resolve in Linux and macOS builds (which use 
/), and vice versa. This caused backlinks to appear as broken links, graph nodes to be duplicated 
(one with / and another with \), and SQLite queries searching for links by target_path to return 
no results. 
 
Root Cause 
Windows uses the backslash ( \) as the directory separator, while Linux and macOS use the 
forward slash (/). The paths stored in the SQLite database reflected the separator of the 
operating system where the application was running. When backlink or link que ries compared 
paths, a path stored as Vault\Notes\Idea.md did not match the search for Vault/Notes/Idea.md, 
producing empty results and duplicate ghost nodes in the graph. 
 
Applied Solution 
• Centralized Normalization: A function named normalize_path() was implemented in the 
src-tauri/src/utils/ module that canonically converts all backslashes to forward slashes 
(/) before any storage or comparison operation. 
• Database Adaptations:  The critical SQL queries in db.rs involving link searches 
(get_outgoing_links, get_backlinks) were modified to perform a dual comparison. They 
now search for both the normalized path and the backslash variant 
(source_path.replace('/', '\\')) to guarantee compatibility with legacy data. 
8.4.1.4 Problem 4: Content Security Policy Conflict with Local Vault 
Resource Loading 
 
Problem Description 
Tessellum allows users to embed images, videos, and PDF documents within their Markdown 
notes (e.g., ![photo](image.png)). After configuring the CSP (Content Security Policy) directives 
in tauri.conf.json, images and other multimedia resources from the user's vault stopped loading 
in the editor and preview view. 
===== PAGE 296 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
296 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
The embedded browser (WebView2) blocked requests to local files with errors of the type 
“Refused to load the image because it violates the Content Security Policy directive”, preventing 
the rendering of any local multimedia content. 
 
Root Cause 
Tauri serves the user's local files through a custom protocol (asset:// in native environments, 
which translates to [https://asset.localhost](https://asset.localhost) in the WebView). The initial 
CSP only allowed 'self' origins in the img -src and media -src directives, rejecting any resource 
originating from the asset:// protocol. Furthermore, there were differences in how different 
WebViews interpret the asset protocol origin: some resolve it as 
[http://asset.localhost](http://asset.localhost) and others as  
[https://asset.localhost](https://asset.localhost). 
 
Applied Solution 
A detailed adjustment of the CSP policy was performed in tauri.conf.json, extending the img-src, 
media-src, and frame-src directives to explicitly include all possible origins of the asset protocol: 
Plaintext 
img-src 'self' data: blob: asset: http://asset.localhost https://asset.localhost https:; 
media-src 'self' data: blob: asset: https://asset.localhost http://asset.localhost https:; 
frame-src 'self' asset: https://asset.localhost http://asset.localhost; 
This configuration allows the loading of local resources from the user's vault through the Tauri 
asset protocol, while maintaining the security restrictions that prevent the execution of external 
scripts (script-src 'self') and the loading of arbitrary objects (object-src 'none'). 
8.4.1.5 Problem 5: Search Index Unavailability Immediately After 
Application Startup 
 
Problem Description 
Users who opened a large vault (with hundreds of notes) and attempted to perform a search 
immediately after application startup received empty or incomplete results. The search 
interface provided no indication that the index was still being built, giving t he impression that 
the search functionality was broken. In vaults of considerable size, the initial Tantivy indexing 
could take several seconds, during which the frontend search component sent queries to an 
empty or partially built index. 
 
===== PAGE 297 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 297 
 
Root Cause 
The Tantivy indexing process runs asynchronously in the Rust backend. During the startup phase, 
the IndexWriter scans all vault files, parses their Markdown content, extracts tags and links, and 
writes the documents to the index. While this process is underway, the IndexReader may return 
partial or empty results if a reload() has not been performed after the last commit(). The 
frontend had no knowledge of the index's readiness state and sent search queries without 
verifying whether the backend was prepared. 
 
Applied Solution 
A search index readiness system was implemented with the following components: 
• Backend Readiness State:  The Tauri commands get_search_readiness, 
ensure_search_ready, and reset_search_readiness_attempts were created, exposing a 
status payload with the fields status (idle, warming, ready, failed), attempt_count, 
max_attempts, retry_delay_ms, and reopen_required. 
• Frontend Polling: The search store (searchStore.ts) periodically queries the readiness 
state before sending search queries. While the status is warming, the interface displays 
a loading indicator informing the user that the index is being built. 
• Retries with Backoff:  If the first verification attempt fails, the system retries with a 
configurable delay strategy up to a maximum number of attempts, allowing the indexing 
to complete even in large vaults. 
8.4.1.6 Problem 6: Native Title Bar Incompatible with the 
Application's Visual Design 
 
Problem Description 
During the user interface design phase, it was determined that the operating system's native 
title bar (with the standard minimize, maximize, and close buttons) broke the visual coherence 
of Tessellum's interface design. 
The Windows title bar applied the colors and typography of the user's operating system theme, 
creating a discordant contrast with the application's dark and minimalist interface. Furthermore, 
the native title bar prevented the implementation of custom func tionalities such as displaying 
the active vault name, integrated navigation buttons, and a unified edge-to-edge design. 
 
Root Cause 
By default, Tauri generates windows with the operating system's native decorations. These 
decorations (title bar, borders, shadows) are controlled by the system's window compositor 
(DWM on Windows, Mutter/Kwin on Linux, WindowServer on macOS) and cannot be  visually 
===== PAGE 298 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
298 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
customized from the web frontend. Any visual modification requires the complete deactivation 
of native decorations and the reimplementation of all window management functionality in the 
frontend itself. 
 
Applied Solution 
Native decorations were deactivated by setting "decorations": false in tauri.conf.json, and a 
custom TitleBar component was implemented in the React frontend that replicates all the 
functionality of the native title bar: 
• Drag to Move the Window: Managed through the startDragging() Tauri API invoked on 
the custom title bar region. 
• Window Control Buttons: Minimize, maximize, and close actions were implemented as 
React components that invoke the Tauri window API functions (appWindow.minimize(), 
appWindow.toggleMaximize(), appWindow.close()). 
• Interactivity: Double-clicking the bar triggers an event managed in the frontend to 
toggle the window state between maximized and restored. 
• Visual Integration: The custom title bar natively inherits the colors, typography, and 
opacity of the active Tessellum theme, achieving a continuous and unified design with 
the rest of the interface. 
Additionally, the tauri -plugin-window-state plugin was integrated to persist the window's 
position, size, and maximization state between user sessions —functionality that native 
decorations previously handled automatically. 
 
8.4.2 Detailed Description of the Classes 
Tessellum is structured using a hybrid, decoupled architecture: - TypeScript Subsystem : 
Implements event-driven orchestration, sandbox plug-in facades, state management stores, and 
core UI layouts. - Rust Subsystem: Executes heavy background indexers, Tantivy full-text index 
pipelines, SQLite WAL database management, and platform-level operations.

8.4.6.1.4 Internal Data Structures (Structs) 
The following structures are defined inside src-tauri/src/models/app_state.rs 
and are scoped directly under AppStateModule: 
8.4.6.1.4.1 Struct SearchReadinessState 
Data structure scoped under AppStateModule. 
Access Mode Type or Struct Field Name 
Public None SearchReadinessStatus status 
Public None u32 attempt_count 
Public None u32 max_attempts 
Public None Option<String> last_error 
Public None Option<String> vault_path 
8.4.6.1.4.2 Struct AppState 
Represents the application state that contains shared resources such as a file watcher 
and a database connection. # Fields * watcher - A thread-safe, optional wrapper 
around a RecommendedWatcher instance. This watcher is typically used for monitoring 
file system events. It is wrapped in a Mutex to ensure safe concurrent access across 
threads. * db - A thread-safe, optional shared reference to a Database instance. The 
Database is wrapped in an Arc for shared ownership across threads. Internally, sqlx 
handles concurrent access through its connection pool. * file_index - Cached 
FileIndex to resolve links quickly without traversing the FS. * asset_index - Cached 
AssetIndex for media embeds. 
Access Mode Type or Struct Field Name 
Public None tokio::sync::Mu
tex<Option<Reco
mmendedWatcher>
> 
watcher 
Public None Arc<Database> db 
Public None Arc<Mutex<Optio
n<FileIndex>>> 
file_index 
Public None Arc<Mutex<Optio
n<AssetIndex>>> 
asset_index

ID Description

updates.

and tags query operations.

9 Test Results 
9.1 Unit Tests 
This section describes the execution of the unit tests previously designed in the testing plan, the 
results obtained, and the corrective actions adopted when defects or execution problems were 
identified.  
 
Test Execution 
The unit test campaign was executed on May 20, 2026, utilizing the standardized CLI boundaries 
specified in the project engineering plan. The execution commands are defined as follows:  
cmd /c npm test 
cargo test --lib 
 
Results Obtained 
The frontend unit test suite, executed via the Vitest framework engine, concluded with nominal 
execution parameters:  
• Test files executed: 46  
• Tests executed: 192  
• Execution result: 192 passed, 0 failed  
The backend core infrastructure unit test suite, compiled and executed via the Cargo toolchain, 
finished within strict deterministic boundaries:  
• Tests executed: 85  
===== PAGE 378 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
378 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
• Execution result: 85 passed, 0 failed  
Consolidated Metric Summary The comprehensive automated unit test campaign executed for 
this standard technical report completed with a cumulative metric of 277 passed tests and 0 
failed tests, achieving a 100% success rate across all covered logical segments.  
 
Functional Interpretation of the Results 
The active unit test suites provide empirical verification of the critical, isolated behaviors 
documented in the structural testing specification:  
• Input Validation & Parsing : Strict verification of path sanitization, markdown 
frontmatter lexical analysis, and metadata tag extraction patterns within the core Rust 
utility layer.  
• Database Layer Transactions : Validation of localized data access functions for 
document link tracking, search indexes, and isolated relational projections using 
temporary transactional fixtures.  
• Graph Topology Resolution: Verification of processing algorithms for wiki-links, cyclical 
references, unresolved target nodes, and placeholder entity injections.  
• Frontend Runtime Environment: Isolated validation of reactive global stores, reactive 
context hooks, markdown editor abstraction helpers, plugin execution boundaries, and 
PDF document generation orchestration.  
These empirical results formally demonstrate that the low -level logical components of the 
Tessellum application remain completely stable under the operational boundaries specified in 
the test fixtures.  
 
Defects Found and Corrective Actions 
During the specific execution instance reported in this engineering document, no unit test 
failures or behavioral deviations were detected.  
However, the current stability of the unit architecture is the direct result of iterative engineering 
actions integrated into the project codebase during the development phase. The primary 
corrective actions preserved in the system configuration comprise:  
• Path Safety Overhaul : Reinforcement of strict local path validation and filesystem 
traversal constraints to mitigate unauthorized file boundary access.  
• Parser Edge-Case Hardening: Resolution of edge cases within the wiki -link processing 
mechanism, focusing on explicitly escaped formatting and corrupt syntax patterns.  
• State Synchronization : Stabilization of persistence layers and state initialization 
routines across deep global application contexts.  
===== PAGE 379 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 379 
 
• Boundary Mocking: Consolidation of highly deterministic mock behaviors for temporary 
backend test vaults and frontend-to-native Tauri IPC bridges.  
 
9.2 System and Integration Tests 
This section records the execution parameters and technical outcomes of the integration and 
system tests established in the verification plan. In strict conformance with the testing strategy, 
two distinct empirical evidence baselines were targeted:  
1. Backend Integration Verification : Stateful integration test units executed inside 
isolated native boundaries using ephemeral local filesystem configurations and sandbox 
databases.  
2. End-to-End (E2E) System Verification: Black-box behavioral scenarios orchestrated via 
the Cypress automation framework to validate top-level workspace flows.  
 
Backend Integration-Style Verification 
The native backend verification execution command:  
cargo test --lib 
encompasses targeted integration test cases embedded across the system modules. These 
modules verified the execution integrity of complex transactional sequences, including:  
• Vault Lifecycle Synchronization: State reconciliation, structural directory indexing, and 
asset removal operations within deep local directory structures.  
• Graph Matrix Construction : Full compilation of internal node -edge relationships, 
successfully handling disconnected subgraphs and missing targets.  
• Refactoring & Renaming Operations : File movement and path propagation rules 
affecting dependent internal links and relative static media assets.  
• System Indexer Orchestration : Asynchronous queue dispatching, tokenization, and 
write-ahead logging safety under concurrent index requests.  
All integrated backend subsystems successfully achieved nominal termination criteria during the 
reported runtime execution.  
 
System Test Execution Status 
The automated end -to-end system test suite was initialized using the standard environment 
entry point:  
PowerShell 
===== PAGE 380 =====
Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs | Project Memory 
380 Jorge Carriles Ruiz | Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo 
 
cmd /c npm run e2e 
The system -level execution campaign failed to terminate successfully within the host 
infrastructure environment on May 20, 2026. This failure was strictly caused by operating 
system privilege and environment configuration constraints, separate from any application code 
regressions or functional assertion failures inside the Cypress specification files.  
The specific blocking constraints logged during initialization are defined as:  
• Vite Configuration Resolution Block : The build engine could not initialize the E2E 
configuration matrix due to an operating system level "Access Denied" restriction during 
recursive directory resolution paths.  
• Cypress Binary Authorization Failure: The runtime shell raised an explicit EPERM error, 
blocking process execution over the local Cypress.exe execution file.  
• Missing Host Subsystems : The localized Windows environment lacked the 
administrative wmic.exe utility, triggering an immediate process tracking failure within 
the framework runner.  
Execution Blockage Notice As a direct consequence of these host environment errors, the E2E 
automation suite was completely blocked at the initialization phase before any application 
functional verification checks could be performed or assessed.

Actions Carried Out After the Detected Problems 
Following the complete structural blockage of the automated E2E system testing execution, the 
following technical engineering actions were performed:  
• Log Archival: The standard error output and core tracebacks from the shell session were 
captured and preserved within the local technical repository logs.  
• Anomaly Classification: The block was isolated and officially categorized as a host-level 
environment and integration tooling issue, completely independent of the core 
application software safety.  
• Data Integrity Maintenance: This document preserves an explicit distinction between 
successful backend native integration outcomes and blocked framework -level 
validation, preventing the entry of unverified pass claims.

The required out -of-scope remediation consists of standard administrative corrections within 
the target Windows runtime environment. This involves rectifying execution group policies, 
downloading missing core dependencies, and re -executing the complete E2E  validation script 
suite to fully resolve the empirical fields of the scenario tables.

9.4 Performance Tests 
This section reports the implementation parameters, empirical metrics, and engineering 
modifications resulting from the automated performance validation routines defined in the 
system testing specification.  
 
Performance Suite Execution 
The performance testing suite was implemented as an isolated, native integration target located 
within the following repository tree location:  
src-tauri/tests/performance.rs 
The evaluation suite was executed via the native toolchain through the following specific 
instructions:  
cargo test --test performance 
cargo test --release --test performance -- --ignored 
The initial command verifies that performance test cases are successfully decoupled from 
standard development debug compilations. The secondary command triggers the optimized 
release-mode compilation matrix to collect highly accurate execution metrics.  
 
Performance Test Results 
The results compiled during the execution session on May 20, 2026, are detailed individually 
below:  
Performance Target Scenario Design

Functional Interpretation of Results: 
• Test P1 Assessment : The indexing pipeline is stable and functions without data 
degradation. However, it violates the strict 5-second efficiency threshold established in 
the plan when operating on the target host environment.  
• Test P2 Assessment: The optimized memory footprint and graph calculation algorithms 
satisfy the standard performance constraints in release mode.  
• Test P3 Assessment : The database WAL configuration and concurrency managers 
mitigate thread contention, satisfying all multi-threaded access parameters.  
 
Changes Derived from the Performance Campaign 
The execution profile of the 10,000-file indexing pipeline uncovered a genuine database I/O and 
processing bottleneck. Consequently, the following structural optimization changes were 
engineered into the codebase:  
• Target Isolation: Creation of an independent, automated performance verification suite 
to establish repeatable regression baselines.  
• API Exposure : Export of an explicit public test surface across low -level core objects: 
Database, VaultIndexer, SearchIndex, and TestVault.  
• I/O Overhead Reduction : Optimization of filesystem access paths by reusing the 
primary directory traversal data array, completely removing a redundant secondary disk 
walk.  
• Batch-Oriented Database Operations : Implementation of vector -based bulk 
persistence queries for node links, frontmatter metadata, categorization tags, and 
search lexical fields.  
• Bulk Insertion Synchronization Paths : Integration of a specialized database 
synchronization path optimized exclusively for initial bulk workspace load sequences.  
• Documentation Integration: Addition of internal architecture specifications detailing 
the performance testing framework and the implemented optimizations.  
===== PAGE 385 =====
Project Memory | Note Taking Application Based on Knowledge Graphs 
Escuela de Ingeniería Informática - Universidad de Oviedo | Jorge Carriles Ruiz 385 
 
While these engineering modifications provided a substantial reduction in absolute execution 
times compared to the legacy implementation, the final recorded metric still exceeds the rigid 
5-second technical threshold.  
 
Final Assessment of the Performance Campaign 
The formal compliance matrix of the Tessellum platform performance vectors is specified as 
follows:  
• High-Volume File Indexing Throughput (10,000 Files): NOT YET COMPLIANT 
• Graph Matrix Structural Projection Density: COMPLIANT 
• SQLite Concurrency Transactional Security: COMPLIANT 
In summary, the performance engineering validation framework is fully operational and verified. 
It provides standard, mathematically reproducible empirical evidence regarding the remaining 
optimization work required within the document indexing subsystem.

11 Conclusiones y Ampliaciones 
11.1 Conclusiones 
Conclusiones del sistema: Qué hemos elaborado, si los resultados están dentro de lo esperado, 
si hemos cumplido las expectativas, justificación de haber escogido las mejores opciones para 
cada uno de los aspectos del sistema, etc. 
11.2 Ampliaciones 
Cualquier labor de ampliación que tengamos contemplada en el sistema debe ser descrita aquí, 
mencionando en qué consiste, cómo ampliará el sistema, qué ventajas nos aporta y porqué no 
se ha incluido en el sistema diseñado, entre otros aspectos. 
11.3  Contenido Entregado en el CD-ROM 
11.3.1 Contenidos 
Descripción del contenido de los diskettes o CDs (directorios y para qu é sirve cada  cosa), 
descripción de esta documentación y de cualquier material que adicionalmente se entregue en 
la presentación. En esta sección se presenta una estructura de directorios de ejemplo para el CD 
que se puede seguir para distribuir todos sus contenidos en el m ismo. Conviene por tanto 
tenerla en cuenta desde el principio de la implementación. 
11.3.1.1.1 Introducción 
La estructura de directorios del proyecto debe poder recoger todos los ficheros relacionados 
con el proyecto, clasificándolos por su propósito dentro del mismo. Los tipos más frecuentes 
son: ficheros fuente, ficheros de configuración, ficheros de documentación… 
Se deben crear directorios para contener cada uno de los tipos de ficheros. Tener una estructura 
estandarizada de los directorios del proyecto es importante por varias razones: 
• Ayuda a localizar la información del proyecto. Por ejemplo, los ficheros fuente siempre 
deben estar en la carpeta src. 
• Ayuda a los desarrolladores a determinar donde debe ir cada fichero. 
• Permite crear scripts de construcción estandarizados. 
11.3.1.1.2 Recomendación estructura general directorios del CD 
NOTA: El nombre del CD debe corresponder con el del proyecto. 
Directorio Contenido

11.5  Código Fuente 
El código fuente tiene que ir dividido por paquetes y por archivos, con un formato que haga que 
resulte legible, tal y como se muestra a continuación en este ejemplo . En la mayoría de las 
ocasiones, es posible que no sea conveniente colocar la totalidad del código fuente en esta 
sección, sino solo una parte, que contenga aquellas clases más significativas e importantes. En 
cualquier caso, conviene consultar al director del proyecto este aspecto. 
11.5.1 Paquete Ejemplo 1: 
11.5.1.1 Fichero “A.cs”: 
using System; 
using System.Collections.Generic; 
using System.Text; 
 
namespace ControlesAvisos 
{ 
    public class Usuario: ICloneable  
    { 
        public Usuario() 
        { 
            this.nombre = ""; 
            this.clave = ""; 
        } 
 
        public Usuario(string nombre, string clave)  
        { 
            this.nombre = nombre; 
            this.clave = clave; 
        } 
 
        private string nombre; 
        public string Nombre 
        { 
            get 
            { 
                return nombre; 
            } 
            set 
            { 
                nombre = value; 
            } 
        } 
 
        private string clave; 
        public string Clave 
        { 
            get 
            { 
                return clave; 
            } 
            set 
            { 
                clave = value; 
            } 
        } 
 
        public Object Clone() 
        { 
            Usuario u = new Usuario(this.Nombre, this.Clave); 
 
            return u; 
        } 
    } 
}
